The Scholarly Foundation of Al-Lubab: Its Sources and Scope
Listing the classical Hanafi sources used in Al-Lubab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the number of sources used in Al-Lubab and identify at least five major Hanafi works that form its foundation.

Core Idea
Al-Lubab synthesizes over 150 Hanafi sources, making it a cornerstone of the madhhab's transmitted authority.

Understanding the sources behind a classical text is crucial for assessing its reliability. Al-Lubab, a commentary on Al-Quduri, draws from a vast network of Hanafi scholarship. This lesson explores the original list of sources and the actual scope of Al-Lubab's foundation.

Guided Path
1
Examine the original list from the 1257 AH edition
Note the 19 sources explicitly mentioned by the author in the first edition of Al-Lubab.
This list includes works like Al-Kanz, Al-Hidayah, Al-Mabsut, etc.
2
Understand the list as a sample, not exhaustive
The passage states that the actual number of sources used is over 150, far exceeding the initial list.
The researcher found that Al-Maydani quoted from more than 150 sources, directly or indirectly.
3
Recognize the diversity of sources
The sources span various genres: primary matn, commentaries, fatwa collections, and usul works.
Examples: Al-Hidayah (commentary), Fatawa Qadi Khan (fatwa), Al-Mabsut (matn).
4
Appreciate the methodological implications
The interweaving of sources shows Al-Lubab's comprehensive nature and the difficulty of tracing direct transmission.
Al-Maydani may have combined or quoted through intermediaries.

Chapter Two: Study of Al-Lubab
001
Section Four
Sources of Al-Lubab
On the first page of the Ottoman edition of Al-Lubab dated 1275 AH, printed during the author's lifetime, a statement appears mentioning the sources of Al-Maydani in Al-Lubab in the following wording:

Statement of what is in this elegant commentary of rulings taken from reliable books, which the eminent jurists compiled, may God's mercy be upon them, and upon those who recorded them and implemented rulings in accordance with them until the Day of Judgment:
1. Kitab al-Kanz and some of its commentaries. 2. Al-Hidayah and some of its commentaries. 3. Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah Sharh al-Quduri. 4. Tashih al-Quduri. 5. Sharh al-Mujma'. 6. Al-Mabsut. 7. Al-Nahr al-Fa'iq. 8. Al-Ikhtiyar Sharh al-Mukhtar. 9. Al-Durar wa al-Ghurar li-Mullah Khusraw. 10. Sadr al-Shari'ah. 11. Kitab al-Sirajiyyah. 12. Jami' al-Fusulayn. 13. Fatawa Qadi Khan. 14. Sharh Fiqh Kaydani. 15. Qahistani. 16. Al-Fatawa al-Khayriyyah. 17. Al-Durr al-Mukhtar and some of its glosses. 18. Fatawa al-Atabi. 19. Al-Dhakhirah and others. End.

*****
Chapter Two: Study of Al-Lubab
This is only what was mentioned. However, when I traced the sources mentioned in Al-Lubab, I found them to be much more than this; they reached more than one hundred and fifty, whether directly quoted or indirectly. Hence it is difficult to identify the direct sources of Al-Maydani because they are interwoven. And I have made, in this volume dedicated to the study of Al-Lubab and Al-Quduri, a special index for the sources mentioned in Al-Lubab, and I have introduced them with a brief definition, which will follow shortly.
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage is a study of the sources of Al-Maydani's Al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri. It begins by citing the original list of sources from the first edition of Al-Lubab (1257 AH). The list includes major Hanafi works such as Al-Kanz, Al-Hidayah, Al-Mabsut, Al-Ikhtiyar, Fatawa Qadi Khan, Al-Durr al-Mukhtar, etc. The author then notes that his own research revealed that Al-Lubab actually draws from over 150 sources, making it difficult to identify the exact direct sources due to overlapping. This highlights the comprehensive nature of Al-Lubab as a commentary that synthesizes many authoritative Hanafi texts.

Key Terms
اللباب (Al-Lubab): The commentary by al-Maydani on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar, a foundational Hanafi fiqh text.
القدوري (Al-Quduri): Abu al-Hasan al-Quduri, author of the Mukhtasar that Al-Lubab comments on.
الهداية (Al-Hidayah): A major Hanafi fiqh work by al-Marghinani, used as a key source in Al-Lubab.
المبسوط (Al-Mabsut): A comprehensive Hanafi fiqh work by al-Sarakhsi, another source for Al-Lubab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, approximately how many sources does Al-Lubab draw from?
A) 19
B) 150
C) Over 150
D) 200

Key Takeaway
Al-Lubab draws from over 150 Hanafi sources, making it a comprehensive synthesis of the madhhab's legal tradition.

The Five Printed Editions of Al-Lubab and Their Significance
Describes the five printed editions of Al-Lubab used in the critical edition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the five printed editions of Al-Lubab and explain why the fifth edition became the standard reference.

Core Idea
A book's reliability depends on the manuscript tradition; knowing its editions is key to authoritative study.

This passage introduces the editorial history of Al-Lubab, the Hanafi fiqh commentary by Abdul Ghani al-Maydani. Understanding which editions were printed during the author's lifetime and which later became standard helps you assess the reliability of the text. The fifth edition, edited by Muhammad Muhyi al-Din Abd al-Hamid, is the most widespread today.

Guided Path
1
List the five printed editions
Identify each edition by year and place: first Istanbul 1275 AH, second Istanbul 1286 AH, third Istanbul 1316 AH, fourth Cairo 1331 AH, fifth Egypt (edited by Muhammad Muhyi al-Din Abd al-Hamid, no year given but later).
The first two were printed during al-Maydani's lifetime.
2
Distinguish author's lifetime editions
Note which were printed during al-Maydani's life: the first two (1275 and 1286 AH). The third was after his death.
3
Explain the spread of the fifth edition
The fifth edition was edited by the respected scholar Muhammad Muhyi al-Din Abd al-Hamid and was widely reproduced by publishers in Beirut, Egypt, Pakistan, etc., making it the most accessible.
4
Reflect on the importance of critical editions
Critical editions compare multiple manuscripts to produce a reliable text. This passage shows the editor's efforts to obtain all available editions.

Source Text

الفصل الثاني : دراسة عن اللباب
هذا ما ذكر فقط، وحين تتبعت المصادر المذكورة في اللباب، وجدت أنها أكثر من بكثير، فقد بلغت أكثر من مائة وخمسين سواء كان النقل عنها مباشرة أم بواسطة، ومن هنا يصعب مصدراً، معرفة مصادر الميداني المباشرة ؛ لأنها متداخلة، وقد جعلتُ في هذا المجلد الخاص بالدراسة عن اللباب والقدوري فهرساً خاصاً للمصادر المذكورة في اللباب، وعرفت بها تعريفاً موجزاً، وسيأتي قريباً.
المبحث الخامس
النسخ المعتمدة في تحقيق اللباب
لقد كتب الله تعالى القبول العظيم لكتاب اللباب للعلامة الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني، فما أن انتهى من تأليفه سنة ١٢٦٦ هـ ـ أو سنة ١٢٦٨ هـ ـ إلا والمحبون للمؤلف، والعارفون بفقهه وقدره العلمي الكبير راحوا يستنسخون منه نسخاً لأنفسهم، ويتداولونه بينهم، بل سعى بعض محبيه لطبعه في الأستانة في اسطنبول، حيث حصل على أحد كبار السلطنة العثمانية. من ذلك موافقة في وهكذا طبع اللباب طبعتين في اسطنبول في حياة المؤلف، الأولى منهما سنة ١٢٧٥هـ ، والثانية سنة ١٢٨٦هـ. كما طبع طبعةً ثالثة في اسطنبول بعد حياة المؤلف سنة ١٣١٦هـ. وكانت له طبعة رابعة في القاهرة بمصر سنة ١٣٣١هـ. ود الدين وطبعة خامسة في مصر بتحقيق الأستاذ محمد محيي عبد الحميد، وهي التي انتشرت بين طلاب العلم، وصور عنها كثيراً دور النشر في بيروت، ومصر، وباكستان، وغيرها. وقد حصلت بفضل الله تعالى على هذه النسخ الخمس، والله الحمد.
Chapter Two: Study of Al-Lubab. This is what I mentioned only, and when I traced the sources mentioned in Al-Lubab, I found that they are much more than that; indeed they amounted to more than one hundred and fifty, whether directly or indirectly transmitted, and from here it is difficult to identify the direct sources of Al-Maydani because they are interlinked. I have made in this volume devoted to the study of Al-Lubab and Al-Quduri a special index for the sources mentioned in Al-Lubab, and I defined them briefly, and it will come soon. The Fifth Research: The relied-upon copies in the critical edition of Al-Lubab. Allah Almighty granted great acceptance to the book Al-Lubab by the scholar Sheikh Abdul Ghani Al-Maydani. As soon as he finished its composition in the year 1266 AH - or 1268 AH - the admirers of the author, and those who knew his jurisprudence and his great scholarly stature, began to copy copies for themselves and circulate it among them, rather some of his admirers sought to print it in Al-Astanah in Istanbul, where they obtained [the approval] of one of the grandees of the Ottoman Sultanate. From that, approval in... Thus Al-Lubab was printed in two editions in Istanbul during the author's lifetime: the first of them in the year 1275 AH, and the second in the year 1286 AH. It was also printed a third edition in Istanbul after the author's death in the year 1316 AH. And it had a fourth edition in Cairo, Egypt in the year 1331 AH. And a fifth edition in Egypt with the critical edition of Professor Muhammad Muhyi al-Din Abd al-Hamid, which spread among students of knowledge, and many publishing houses in Beirut, Egypt, Pakistan and elsewhere have reproduced it. By the grace of Allah, I have obtained these five copies, and praise be to Allah.
Source pages p. 156

Commentary
This passage is part of the introduction or study section of the critical edition of Al-Lubab. The author describes the extensive sources—over 150—used in writing Al-Lubab, and notes the difficulty in pinpointing Al-Maydani's immediate sources due to their overlap. He then focuses on the fifth research topic: the editions used in the critical edition. He reports that Al-Lubab was well-received; copies were made even before the ink was dry. The first two editions were printed in Istanbul during the author's lifetime (1275 and 1286 AH). A third Istanbul edition appeared posthumously (1316 AH), then a Cairo edition (1331 AH). The fifth edition, edited by Muhammad Muhyi al-Din Abd al-Hamid, became the most widespread, reproduced by publishers in multiple countries. The author states he obtained all five editions.

Key Terms
اللباب (Al-Lubab): The book being studied, a commentary on Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar by Abdul Ghani Al-Maydani.
القدوري (Al-Quduri): The author of Mukhtasar Al-Quduri, a foundational Hanafi text; the base text for Al-Lubab.
الميداني (Al-Maydani): The author of Al-Lubab, Sheikh Abdul Ghani Al-Maydani, a Hanafi scholar.
نسخة (nuskhah): A copy or edition of a book; in this context, a printed edition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The fifth edition of Al-Lubab, edited by Muhammad Muhyi al-Din Abd al-Hamid, is the most widely used reliable edition.

The Manuscript Tradition of Al-Lubab Sharh Al-Quduri
Describing the manuscript copies used in the critical edition of Al-Lubab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three manuscript copies used in the critical edition of Al-Lubab and explain their significance for Hanafi text transmission.

Core Idea
Three manuscript witnesses — two autograph-era copies and one first edition — anchor the critical text of Al-Lubab.

In studying Hanafi fiqh, knowing the textual history of our primary sources is essential. This passage from the editor's introduction describes the three copies used to establish the text of Al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri. Understanding the provenance and dates of these copies helps us evaluate the reliability of the edition.

Guided Path
1
Identify each manuscript copy
Read the passage and note the three copies: the first coded (مخ), the second coded (ص), and the printed Istanbul edition. Note their locations and dates.
2
Determine the date of each copy relative to the author's life
The first copy has a colophon dated 1266 AH, the second was copied in 1269 AH (three years after completion), the third was printed in 1275 AH (the year of the author's death).
3
Assess the value of each copy
The first two are manuscripts from the author's lifetime; the ms. in Cairo is particularly close to the original. The printed edition is a first edition. The editor coded them for reference.
4
Connect to Hanafi text criticism
Critical editions rely on multiple witnesses. For a fiqh text, the accuracy of the text directly affects rulings derived from it.

Chapter Two: Study of Al-Lubab. Composed by its humble, sinful compiler, full of hopes, Abd al-Ghani al-Ghunaimi al-Maydani, may Allah forgive him, his parents, his loved ones, and those who have a right upon him, and be good to them and to him, and make us firm with the firm word at the end and on the day of standing before Him. Praise be to Allah by whose grace good deeds are completed, and blessings and peace upon our master Muhammad, his family, companions, and pure wives, everlasting blessings and peace as long as times follow one another and blessings continue. End. I have coded this copy as (Makh). 2 - The second copy: A photocopy of a manuscript in the Egyptian National Library in Cairo, number 2136, Hanafi fiqh 42147 M, comprising 400 folios, each page 21 lines, copied during the author's lifetime in 1269 AH, three years after the author finished the book. At its end, the author al-Maydani, may Allah have mercy on him, says: 'By the grace of Allah, the time of the forenoon on Monday, the 13th of blessed Ramadan, 1266 AH...' (1) The noble, virtuous brother Dr. Sheikh Ahmad Sa'd al-Din ibn Sheikh Muhammad 'Awwamah kindly facilitated its photography; may Allah reward him and grant him his hopes in the good of this world and the Hereafter... '...from the Hijra of the Chosen Prophet described with the most perfect description, composed by its humble, sinful compiler, full of hopes, Abd al-Ghani al-Ghunaimi al-Maydani...' End. The writing of this book, known by its famous name Al-Lubab Sharh al-Kitab, was completed by the poorest and most needy of servants, in 1269 AH, on the 27th of Jumada al-Awwal, after the Hijra of the Prophet – and I am the poor, confessing sin and deficiency, hoping for the Generous: Muhammad, attributed to the master of the first and last, son of Yasin al-Safubri (al-Sanubri well-known), may Allah forgive him, his parents, his loved ones, his neighbors, and those who have a right upon him, and blessings upon the Master of the Worlds, the Ornament of the Chosen Messengers. Amen, Amen, Amen. End. I have coded it with the letter (Sad). The third copy: A photocopy of a printed copy in Istanbul during the author's lifetime, in 1275 AH, during the time of the Ottoman Sultan Abd al-Majid ibn Mahmud Khan. Some dignitaries sought to print it with permission from the Supreme Ottoman State.
Source pages p. 160

Commentary
This passage is the second chapter of the editor's introduction, titled 'Study of Al-Lubab'. The editor describes three copies of the book Al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri by Abd al-Ghani al-Ghunaimi al-Maydani, used in his critical edition.

The first copy is coded (مخ). It is a manuscript containing the author's original colophon dated 1266 AH, with the author's supplications. The editor quotes the colophon's opening words.

The second copy is a manuscript from the Egyptian National Library (Dar al-Kutub al-Misriyya) coded (ص). It has 400 folios, 21 lines per page, and was copied in 1269 AH, just three years after the author completed the work. The editor again quotes from its colophon, which repeats similar supplications and confirms the date 1269 AH.

The third copy is a printed edition from Istanbul, dated 1275 AH (the same year as the author's death). It was printed under the Ottoman sultan Abd al-Majid. The passage cuts off mid-sentence, stating that 'some dignitaries sought to print it with permission from the Supreme Ottoman State.'

This is purely biographical and codicological information, not a legal ruling. It establishes the textual basis for the edition.

Key Terms
اللباب (Al-Lubab): The title of the commentary by al-Maydani on Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar.
القدوري (Al-Quduri): Author of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, a foundational Hanafi fiqh text.
نسخة خطية (nuskhah khattiyyah): A handwritten manuscript copy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

D) Four

Key Takeaway
The critical edition of Al-Lubab relies on three witnesses: two lifetime manuscripts and a first printed edition.

Introduction and Front Matter

Historical Analysis of Al-Lubab's Completion Dates
Describes the completion dates and manuscript versions of Al-Lubab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze discrepancies in manuscript colophons and reconcile conflicting dates using scholarly reasoning based on Hanafi textual criticism.

Core Idea
A manuscript's colophon gives the date of completion, but multiple copies may have different dates—the scholar must reconcile them by considering revisions and printing history.

This lesson examines the completion dates of Al-Lubab Sharh al-Kitab by Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani. The passage presents multiple colophons with different dates and an editor's reconciliation. Understanding how to evaluate such textual evidence is crucial for verifying the authenticity and chronology of classical Hanafi works.

Guided Path
1
Identify the colophon dates
List all mentioned completion dates from the passage. Note the year and month/day where given.
Dates: 1266 AH (first draft), 1268 AH (final completion in Istanbul print), 1269 AH (author's colophon).
2
Note the manuscript sources
Which copy gives which date? The author's own colophon gives 1269; the Istanbul print colophon gives 1268; other copies mention 1266.
3
Analyze the discrepancy
What is the contradiction between the author's colophon and the printed copy? The printed copy shows a different date (1268) and mentions the author's companion who facilitated printing.
4
Apply the editor's reconciliation
Why might the author have two completion dates? The editor suggests the author completed a first draft in 1266, revised in 1268, and the author's colophon in 1269 may be an error or a different stage.
5
Consider the historical context
What does the involvement of the Ottoman Sultan and a companion of the author tell us about the work's transmission? It indicates the work was valued by the state and circulated through authorized copies.

من هجرة المصطفى الموصوف بأكمل وصف على يد جامعه الحقير الجاني كثير الأماني عبد الغني الغنيمي الميداني، غفر الله له ولوالديــه وأحبابه ومَن له حق عليه وأحسن إليهم وإليه، وثبتنا بالقول الثابت عند الخاتمة، ويوم الوقوف بين يديه، والحمد لله الذي بنعمتـه تـتـم الصالحات، وصلى الله على سيدنا محمد وعلى آله وأصحابه وأزواجه الطاهرات صلاة وسلاماً دائمين ما تعاقبت الأوقات، وتواصلت البركات. آمين. اهـ.

النسخة الثالثة :
صورة من نسخة مطبوعة في اسطنبول في حياة المؤلف، سنة ١٢٧٥هـ، زمن السلطان العثماني عبد المجيد بن محمود خان. وقد سعى في طبعها بإذن من الدولة العلية العثمانية أحد الأعيان لديهم، ممن تشرف بصحبة المؤلف بدمشق، واستنسخ من نسخة، ثم طبعها كما وَعَدَ، كما جاء في مقدمة هذه الطبعة، وهي في مجلد كبير، يقع في (٤٧٤) صفحة مرصوصة.
وفي آخر هذه النسخة ذكر تاريخ انتهاء المؤلف منها، كما يلي:
تم الكتاب وقت الضحوة الكبرى من يوم السبت المبارك، سابع شهر المحرم الحرام، سنة ثمانية وستين ومائتين وألف، مـن هـجـرة المصطفى الموصوف بأكمل وصف». اهـ
وأما بقية نسخ اللباب فسيأتي أنه ذُكر فيها تاريخ انتهاء المؤلف من تأليفه، وهو وقت الضحوة الكبرى من يوم الاثنين، ثالث عشر من شهر رمضان المبارك، سنة ست وستين ومائتين وألف من هجرة المصطفى الموصوف بأكمل وصف».اهـ .
قلت: لعله انتهى منه أولاً سنة ١٢٦٦هـ، ثم أعاد فيـه النظـر لتنقيحه وتهذيبه، فكان الانتهاء منه تماماً في المرة الثانية سنة ١٢٦٨هـ، والله تعالى أعلم، وبخاصة أن الذي سعى بطبعه، وذكـر هذا التاريخ لانتهاء التأليف هو ممـن صـحب الميداني في دمشق الشام، كما نص على ذلك في مقدمة الطبعة.
وهذه النسخة المطبوعـة مـنـهـا نسخة مودعة في مكتبة مركز البحث العلمي بجامعة أم القرى، وعنها أخذتُ الصورة، كما توجد منها نسخة أخرى في مكتبة الملك عبد العزيز بالمدينة المنورة في المكتبات الخاصة.

The second chapter: A study of Al-Lubab. From the migration of the Chosen One described with the most complete description, by its compiler, the humble sinner, full of hopes, Abd al-Ghani al-Ghanimi al-Maydani, may Allah forgive him, his parents, his loved ones, and those who have a right upon him, and be good to them and to him, and keep us firm on the true statement at the end and on the Day of standing before Him. Praise be to Allah by whose grace good deeds are completed, and may Allah send blessings upon our master Muhammad and upon his family, his companions, and his pure wives, a perpetual prayer and peace as long as times alternate and blessings continue. Amen. End.
The writing of this book, known by its famous name Al-Lubab Sharh al-Kitab, was completed by the poorest of servants and the most in need of Him, in the year 1269, on the twenty-seventh of Jumada al-Awwal, after the Hijra of the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace. And I am the poor one acknowledging sin and shortcoming, hoping for the Generous: Muhammad, attributed to the master of the first and the last, son of Yasin al-Sufawbari (al-Sunuburi the famous, may Allah forgive him, his parents, his loved ones, his neighbors, and those who have a right upon him, and may Allah bless the master of the worlds and the adornment of the righteous messengers. Amen. Amen. Amen. End.
I have symbolized it with the letter (S).
The third copy:
A copy of an edition printed in Istanbul during the author's lifetime, in the year 1275 AH, during the time of the Ottoman Sultan Abdul Majid bin Mahmud Khan. One of the notables among them, who was honored to accompany the author in Damascus, sought its printing with the permission of the Ottoman Sublime State, copied from a manuscript, then printed it as promised, as mentioned in the introduction of this edition. It is in a large volume, comprising 474 compact pages.
At the end of this copy is mentioned the date of the author's completion of it, as follows: The book was completed at the time of al-dahwa al-kubra (mid-morning) on the blessed Saturday, the seventh of the sacred month of Muharram, in the year 1268, from the Hijra of the Chosen One described with the most complete description. End.
As for the remaining copies of Al-Lubab, it will come that the date of the author's completion of his authorship is mentioned in them, which is the time of al-dahwa al-kubra (mid-morning) on Monday, the thirteenth of the blessed month of Ramadan, in the year 1266, from the Hijra of the Chosen One described with the most complete description. End.
I say: Perhaps he finished it first in the year 1266 AH, then he revised it to refine and improve it, so the completion was entirely the second time in the year 1268 AH. And Allah knows best, especially since the one who sought its printing and mentioned this date for the completion of the authorship was among those who accompanied al-Maydani in Damascus, as he stated in the introduction of the edition.
This printed copy has a copy deposited in the library of the Scientific Research Center at Umm al-Qura University, from which I took the image, and there is another copy in the library of King Abdul Aziz in Medina in private libraries.
The mention of the one who sought its printing came on the second page of it after...
Source pages p. 161

Commentary
This passage is a modern biographical and bibliographical study of the book Al-Lubab Sharh al-Kitab. It begins with the colophon of the author, Abd al-Ghani al-Ghanimi al-Maydani, who praises Allah and sends blessings on the Prophet. He states he completed the book in 1269 AH on 27 Jumada al-Awwal. However, the editor notes that the colophon in some copies gives a different date: the completion was on Saturday, 7 Muharram 1268 AH. The editor reconciles this by suggesting the author completed the first draft in 1266 AH, then revised and finalized it in 1268 AH. The passage also describes the third copy printed in Istanbul in 1275 AH during the reign of Sultan Abdul Majid, facilitated by a companion of the author. The editor indicates that this printed copy is based on a manuscript, and he has deposited copies in libraries in Umm al-Qura and Medina. This front matter provides important chronological context for the work.

Key Terms
الضحوة الكبرى (al-dahwa al-kubra): The mid-morning time, roughly the period between sunrise and midday, considered a blessed time in Islamic tradition.
اللباب (al-lubab): The title of the commentary (sharh) on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar, meaning 'the core' or 'the essence'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the editor's analysis, what is the most likely sequence of completion for Al-Lubab?
A) Finished in 1266, then revised and completed in 1268, with 1269 being a scribal error.
B) Finished in 1268, then expanded in 1269, with 1266 being a misreading.
C) Finished in 1269, then abridged in 1268, with 1266 being a different work.
D) The three dates refer to three different volumes of the same work.

Key Takeaway
Manuscript colophons must be critically cross-checked; conflicting dates often indicate successive revisions rather than errors.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
The Fourth Printed Copy of al-Lubab: A Study in Hanafi Textual Transmission
Bibliographic description of print history and waqf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify key bibliographic details of a Hanafi text and explain the significance of the waqfiyya in preserving classical works.

Core Idea
The preservation of Hanafi knowledge relies on chains of transmission and endowment (waqf) — this copy's history shows both.

This passage from a modern edition of al-Lubab provides bibliographic details about the fourth printed copy. It includes the author's narrative of how he acquired and copied the manuscript, and the waqfiyya (endowment deed) that placed the printed copy in the Meccan Library. Understanding such front matter is crucial for tracing the reliability and transmission of Hanafi texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the book and its context
Al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Quduri is a Hanafi fiqh commentary. Note the author/comments on the chain: the commentator (Sahafilar Shaykhizada) describes how he obtained the manuscript and how it was copied.
This front matter traces the textual lineage.
2
Locate the printing details
The fourth copy was printed in 1286 AH at a Syrian press, patronized by Muhammad Rashid Pasha. The colophon states the author completed al-Lubab in 1266 AH.
Distinguish composition date from printing date.
3
Examine the waqfiyya
The printed copy was endowed to the Meccan Library by a Turkish pilgrim in 1294 AH for the souls of his wife and her brother. The endowment text is quoted.
The waqfiyya ensures the text's availability and preservation.
4
Connect to Hanafi tradition
In Hanafi fiqh, transmission (riwaya) requires a reliable chain. This bibliographic record serves as a modern link in that chain, confirming the text's authenticity.
Even printed copies require chain-of-custody documentation.

Chapter Two: A Study of al-Lubab
Table of contents, wrote the following:
163
What coincided with the completion of the authorship of this gentle commentary during the leisure of this weak, poor servant, the most needy of the masters: (Sahafilar Shaykhizada Sayyid Ahmad Nazif) in Damascus of Syria. I had a copy written, and I took it with me, and after my return to the Sublime Capital, some virtuous people saw it and admired it, and wrote a copy from it. Then it was copied repeatedly, and I witnessed what I witnessed of the eager seekers of benefit [who offered] prayer and praise.
I had undertaken when I was honored with the company of the virtuous commentator in Damascus
and
its publication in print due to its value and the good character of its author, for it is the character of the pious predecessors: good morals and chastity, such that despite his abundance of virtue and perfection, he avoids utmost avoidance of being singled out and fame, and he was not pleased to mix with anyone other than the people of knowledge from among the greats and merchants. Rather, he is devoted to serving the Sharia and teaching the sciences. May Allah make his beautiful effort appreciated and his reward abundant.
Allah
So praise be to Allah who enabled this supplicant servant to fulfill this promise by printing it in the Jarida Press in the Sublime Capital with utmost effort and diligence. That was only by the blessing of the master of the age, the renewer of the times, whose noble assistance favored me and whose care and high concern encompassed me. So the credit is his, and what is for the one who strives
in goodness. May Allah support his state and perpetuate his sultanate. Amen. End.
I have symbolized it with the letter (A).

The Fourth Copy:
A photostat copy printed in a Syrian press during the reign of the Ottoman Sultan Abdulaziz Khan, by the indication of the unique grand vizier, His Excellency, the owner of the state, Muhammad Rashid Pasha, in the year 1286 AH, and it consists of 504 pages.
At the end of this copy – as in the second copy – that the author finished writing al-Lubab in the year 1266 AH.
This printed copy is deposited in the library of the Holy Mosque of Mecca, and it was endowed to the library by one of the Turkish pilgrims in the year 1294 AH, for the soul of his wife and her brother, who died after performing the rituals of Hajj. This endowment deed was written on its first page, arranged in the form of a large circle, in beautiful calligraphy, and its text is as follows:
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. Praise be to Allah who guides whomever He wills from His servants to do good, and blessings and peace be upon our master Muhammad, the master of masters, and upon his family and companions who have attained the highest ranks. Then I say:
When the eternal will was attached to the departure of my protected wife (Khadija Rafi'a Khanum) and her brother (Hasan) Nuri (Bey, sons of Ahmad (Khusraw Agha)) to perform the duty of noble Hajj, in the year 1294 AH, in the company of our master, the Governor of Hijaz (His Excellently Great Halit Pasha).
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage is a bibliographic description of the fourth manuscript copy of al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Quduri. It details the publication history and endowment of this edition. The text begins with the author's personal account of how he arranged for a copy of the commentary to be written, and how it was admired and copied. He praises the original commentator's character, noting his humility and dedication to teaching. Then it describes the fourth printed copy: a Syrian press publication from 1286 AH (1869-1870 CE) under the patronage of Muhammad Rashid Pasha. It consists of 504 pages. The colophon states the author completed al-Lubab in 1266 AH (1849-1850 CE). This copy was endowed to the Mecca Library by a Turkish pilgrim in 1294 AH (1877-1878 CE) for the souls of his wife and her brother, who died after Hajj. The endowment text is quoted, showing the pious intentions behind the waqf. This passage is purely historical and not fiqh content, but it illustrates the chain of transmission and preservation of Hanafi texts.

Key Terms
الوقفية (al-waqfiyyah): The endowment deed written on the first page of the book, stating the terms of the waqf.

Verifying Manuscript Sources in Hanafi Fiqh: The Case of Al-Lubab
Describes the fifth through seventh manuscript copies used for the edition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key manuscript sources of a Hanafi fiqh commentary and explain how their layout (margins, placement) indicates the authority of the base text.

Core Idea
The placement of a fiqh text (margin vs. center) reveals the editor's view of relative authority.

In critical editions of classical works, the description of manuscript copies is not mere bibliography—it determines the reliability of the text. This passage from the introduction to Al-Lubab explains how the editor used several copies to establish the correct text. Understanding these details helps you evaluate the authority of the rulings you will study.

Guided Path
1
Identify the content of each copy
For each copy described (fifth, sixth, seventh), list which texts are included and how they are arranged (margin, center, top, bottom).
Focus on the specific books: Al-Lubab, Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah, and Mukhtasar al-Quduri.
2
Note the publication details
Record the place, year, publisher, and any editorial notes (e.g., corrector, annotations).
These details help assess the provenance and care taken in the edition.
3
Understand the significance of layout
Explain why the editor mentions whether Al-Lubab is in the margin, center, or below another text. Relate this to the hierarchy of authority between the base text (Mukhtasar al-Quduri) and the commentary.
The seventh copy places Mukhtasar al-Quduri at the top, indicating it is the foundational text.

الفصل الثاني : دراسة عن اللباب وبحسب ١٦٥ القدر الإلهي بعد أدائهما الحج والمناسك اخترمتهما المنية بين الحرمين الشريفين أحببت أن أوقف جملة من الكتب المحترمة، فمن جملتها قد وقفتُ هذا الكتاب وقفاً صحيحاً شرعياً كافياً مرعياً خالصاً لوجهه الكريم، وجعلت ثوابه لروح وضريح المرحومين الله، زوجتي وأخيها المذكورين. التي وقفتها بتاريخه في المكتبة المكية الكائنة في الحرم المحترم الشريف المكي، وأن ينتفع بها الخاص والعام في القراءة والمراجعــة من أهل العلم في الحرم الشريف المذكور، راجياً من الله تعالى الرحيم أن يجعل ذلك مقبولاً خالصاً لوجهه العظيم بجاه نبيه الكريم صلى الله عليه وسلم، وعلى آله وصحبه أجمعين. وأنا الفقير إليه تعالى : حسين بن أحمد، الساكن في الدار السلطنة السنية». اهـ وقد رمزت لهذه النسخة بحرف (م). ٥- النسخة الخامسة : صورة عن نسخة مطبوعة في اسطنبول سنة ١٣١٦هـ، زمن السلطان العثماني عبد الحميد خان، وقد جاء نص اللباب في هذه الطبعة في حاشية الصفحة، وطبع في صلبها كتاب: «الجوهرة النيرة» شرح القدوري للحدادي وقد جاءت هذه الطبعة في جزءين ضمن مجلد واحد كبير، الأول منهما في (٤٨٢) صفحة، والثاني في (٤٠٢) صفحة. وقد أُعيد تصوير هذه الطبعة في باكستان، كراتشي، الناشر: مـيـر محمد كتب خانة. وجاء في آخرها ـ كما جاء في آخر النسخة الثانية والرابعة ـ أن المؤلف انتهى من تأليف اللباب يوم (۱۳) رمضان، سنة ١٢٦٦هـ. وقد رمزت لها بحرف: (ن). ٦- النسخة السادسة : صورة عن نسخة مطبوعة في القاهرة سنة ١٣٣١هـ، في مطبعة الفتوح الأدبية بالقاهرة، في جزءين، ضمن مجلد واحد، الأول منهما في (١٧٤) صفحة، والثاني في (١٦٧) صفحة. وفي آخرها أيضاً ـ كما جاء في النسخة الثانية والرابعة والخامسة - أن المؤلف انتهى من تأليف اللباب سنة ١٢٦٦هـ. وقد رمزت لها بحرف : (جـ). - النسخة السابعة : نسخة مطبوعة متداولة الآن كثيراً، وصورت في دور النشـر عـدة مرات، منها تصوير المطبعة العلمية ببيروت سنة ١٤٠٠هـ، وكان قد صححها الأستاذ محمد محيي الدين عبد الحميد، وعليها تعليقات أيضاً للأستاذ محمود النواوي، جاءت في أربعة أجزاء، ضمن مجلدين، كل جزء منها يقع في (۲۳۰) صفحة تقريباً، وقد وضع نص مختصر القدوري في أعلى الصفحة وتحته جاء نص اللباب.
Chapter Two: A Study of Al-Lubab. According to the divine decree after performing Hajj and the rites, death overtook them between the two noble sanctuaries. I wished to endow a number of respected books. Among them I have endowed this book as a valid, complete, and observed legal endowment (waqf), purely for His noble face, and I made its reward for the soul and grave of the deceased, my wife and her brother mentioned above. I endowed it with its date in the Makki library located in the noble Makkan sanctuary, so that both the elite and the commoners may benefit from it in reading and reference by the people of knowledge in the said noble sanctuary, hoping from Allah Almighty, the Merciful, that He makes it accepted purely for His great face, by the honor of His noble Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, and upon his family and all his companions. And I, the needy one before Him: Husayn ibn Ahmad, residing in the supreme royal abode. End of quote. I have symbolized this copy with the letter (M). 5. The fifth copy: A photocopy of a printed copy in Istanbul in the year 1316 AH, during the reign of the Ottoman Sultan Abdul Hamid Khan. In this edition, the text of Al-Lubab came in the margin of the page, and in its center was printed the book 'Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah' by Al-Hadadi. This edition came in two parts within one large volume, the first of which is (482) pages, and the second is (402) pages. This edition was reproduced in Pakistan, Karachi, publisher: Mir Muhammad Kutub Khanah. And at its end — as at the end of the second and fourth copies — it is stated that the author finished composing Al-Lubab on the 13th of Ramadan, 1266 AH. I have symbolized it with the letter (N). 6. The sixth copy: A photocopy of a printed copy in Cairo in 1331 AH, at Al-Futuh al-Adabiyyah Press in Cairo, in two parts within one volume, the first of which is (174) pages, and the second is (167) pages. At its end also — as in the second, fourth, and fifth copies — the author finished composing Al-Lubab in 1266 AH. I have symbolized it with the letter (J). 7. The seventh copy: A printed copy now widely circulated, and reproduced by publishers several times, including the reproduction by the Scientific Press in Beirut in 1400 AH. It was edited by Professor Muhammad Muhyi al-Din Abd al-Hamid, and it also has annotations by Professor Mahmud al-Nawawi. It came in four parts within two volumes, each part covering approximately 230 pages. The text of Mukhtasar al-Quduri was placed at the top of the page and below it came the text of Al-Lubab.
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage is from the front matter of a critical edition of Al-Lubab. It describes the various manuscript and printed copies used by the editor. The fifth copy is a reproduction of an Istanbul print (1316 AH), which contained the text of Al-Lubab in the margin alongside Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah in the center. This copy was reproduced in Pakistan. The sixth copy is from Cairo (1331 AH) and is similar to the fifth. The seventh copy is a widely circulating edition from Beirut (1400 AH), edited by Muhammad Muhyi al-Din Abd al-Hamid, with annotations by Mahmud al-Nawawi, and it places the text of Mukhtasar al-Quduri (the base text) in the top margin with Al-Lubab below. This information is crucial for understanding the textual history of the work and the sources of the edition.

Key Terms
اللباب (al-Lubab): The book being edited; a Hanafi fiqh commentary by al-Maydani on Mukhtasar al-Quduri.
القدوري (al-Quduri): Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri, author of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, a foundational Hanafi fiqh text.
الجوهرة النيرة (al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah): A commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri by al-Hadadi, printed alongside some editions of Al-Lubab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which of the described copies does Al-Lubab appear in the margin and Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah in the center?
A) Fifth copy
B) Sixth copy
C) Seventh copy
D) Fourth copy

Key Takeaway
Manuscript descriptions in fiqh editions are not decoration—they determine the textual authority of the rulings.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Evaluating Printed Editions of Hanafi Fiqh Texts
Editor's evaluation of seven printed editions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the reliability of a printed edition of a Hanafi fiqh text by identifying common editorial flaws such as omissions, reliance on memory, and reproduction of errors.

Core Idea
A popular edition is not always reliable; trust is earned through manuscript-based verification.

When studying a classical Hanafi text like Al-Lubab, the edition you use matters. This lesson examines how a critical editor (Sa'id Bakdash) evaluated seven printed editions, exposing serious flaws in some widely circulated versions. You will learn to look beyond the cover and assess an edition's trustworthiness.

Guided Path
1
List the editions and their codes
Identify the seven editions described, noting the letters assigned to each (N, J, D, etc.). This helps track which edition is referenced.
2
Read the editor's critique of each
Pay attention to what the editor says about each edition's quality. He points out omissions, errors, and lack of manuscript basis. Focus on the seventh edition (D) as a negative example.
3
Identify common textual flaws
From the critique, list the recurring problems: large omissions (up to two lines), many errors, additions unique to one edition, and reliance on memory rather than manuscripts.
4
Understand the chain of reproduction
Note that later editions (Beirut 1415 AH, Damascus 1424 AH) copied the flawed seventh edition, perpetuating its errors. This shows how a single bad edition can propagate mistakes.
5
Apply the criteria to other texts
Use these same principles when you encounter any printed edition of a Hanafi work: check the editor's introduction, look for mention of manuscripts, and be wary of claims like 'revised and corrected' without evidence.

Chapter Two: Study on Al-Lubab
167
In this edition there are many large omissions; the omission in some places reached two lines, and very many terrible errors. It seems that Professor Muhammad al-Din Abd al-Hamid did not rely on a sound copy to compare the text; rather, I was informed that he was correcting from memory.
Muhyi
And Professor Muhammad Muhyi al-Din did not mention in his introduction on which copies he relied in his verification, whether in the Mukhtasar or in Al-Lubab. And at the end of his edition it says: 'Completed with the help of Allah Almighty and His facilitation, the review of the fourth part of the book Al-Lubab, and its verification by referring to its original sources.' End? In this edition there is an addition of scattered words in multiple places that this edition alone has; I do not know where its editor brought them from.
I have designated this edition with the letter (D).
These are the seven copies I relied on in verifying Al-Lubab. After the aforementioned edition of Professor Muhammad Muhyi al-Din Abd al-Hamid, other editions appeared that claimed to be verified, but in reality they are taken from his edition, except that they were newly typeset with their many very disturbing errors and distortions and strange omissions.
It is an edition published by Dar al-Kitab al-Arabi in Beirut, first edition of the book Al-Lubab, dated 1415 AH, and it says: 'Its hadiths were extracted and annotated by: Abd al-Razzaq al-Mahdi.' End?!
Also another edition published in Damascus, year 1424 AH, it says: 'Revised edition, compared with the manuscript, and increased with a chapter on visiting...
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage is the second chapter of the editorial introduction to the book 'Al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri'. The editor, Sa'id Bakdash, provides a detailed description of seven printed editions he used in his critical edition. He explains how he designated each with a letter code (N, J, D, etc.) to track them in his apparatus. The editor critically evaluates the editions, especially the seventh one (widely circulated, corrected by Muhammad Muhyi al-Din Abd al-Hamid). He points out serious flaws: large omissions, numerous errors, and the suspicion that the editor did not rely on a proper manuscript but corrected from memory. He also notes that subsequent editions (Beirut 1415 AH and Damascus 1424 AH) merely reproduced that faulty edition. This discussion is crucial for understanding the textual history of the work. It highlights the importance of critical editions based on multiple reliable manuscripts, and the risks of relying on popular editions that may have textual corruptions. The editor's meticulous approach reflects the Hanafi scholarly tradition's concern for accurate transmission of texts.

Key Terms
اللباب (al-Lubab): The name of a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, written by 'Abd al-Ghani al-Ghunaymi al-Maydani, covering Hanafi fiqh.
المختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): A concise manual of Hanafi fiqh by Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri.
تحقيق (tahqiq): Critical edition of a classical text, involving comparison of manuscripts and correction of errors.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the editor, what was the main problem with the seventh edition (corrected by Muhammad Muhyi al-Din Abd al-Hamid)?
A) It was printed on low-quality paper.
B) It had large omissions and errors, and the editor may have corrected from memory.
C) It was not published in a single volume.
D) It lacked the text of Mukhtasar al-Quduri.

Key Takeaway
Always verify the editorial method behind a printed edition of a classical Hanafi text before relying on it.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate

How to Assess the Reliability of a Hanafi Fiqh Text Edition
Editorial critique of previous print editions of al-Lubab.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the criteria for a reliable critical edition of a Hanafi fiqh text and evaluate a given edition based on manuscript evidence.

Core Idea
A flawed edition of a fiqh text misleads generations; reliable scholarship demands manuscript-based critical editing.

This passage from the editor's introduction to al-Lubab (a commentary on al-Quduri) reveals the serious consequences of relying on a defective edition. The editor details omissions and errors in a previous print and explains why his own seven-manuscript method is necessary. As students of Hanafi fiqh, understanding how to assess the reliability of our sources is essential for sound legal study.

Guided Path
1
Identify the specific criticisms of the previous edition
Note the claims of large omissions (two lines in some places), many errors, and that the editor corrected from memory rather than a sound manuscript.
2
Recognize the editor's method of verification
He used seven manuscripts, designated one as (D), and avoided relying on memory.
3
Trace the chain of dependence among subsequent editions
Later editions from Beirut and Damascus merely reprint the flawed edition, inheriting its errors despite new typesetting.
4
Understand the significance of the unverified manuscript
A manuscript with corrections by Ibn Abidin exists but was inaccessible; its potential value is noted.

الفصل الثاني : دراسة عن اللباب
وفي هذه الطبعة أسقاط كبيرة كثيرة، بلغ السقط في بعض المواضع سطرين، وأخطاء فظيعة كثيرة جداً، وكأن الأستاذ محمد الدين عبد الحميد لم يعتمد على نسخة سليمة يقابل النص بها، بل بلغني أنه كان يصحح من ذاكرته.
محيي
ولم يذكر الأستاذ محمد محيي الدين في مقدمته على أي النُّسَخ اعتمد في تحقيقه، سواء في المختصر أو في اللباب، وقد جاء في آخر طبعته : تم بعون الله تعالى وتيسيره مراجعة الجزء الرابع من كتاب اللباب، وتحقيقه بالرجوع إلى أصوله التي نقل عنها». اهـ ؟! وفي هذه النسخة زيادة لكلمات متفرقة في مواضع متعددة انفردت بها هذه الطبعة، لا أدري من أين أتى بها محققها ؟
وقد رمزت لهذه النسخة بحرف : (د).
هذه النسخ السبعة هي التي اعتمدتها في تحقيق اللباب، وقد صدرت بعد طبعة الأستاذ محمد محيي الدين عبد الحميد السابقة الذكر طبعات أخرى كتب عليها أنها محققة، لكنها في الواقع مأخوذة عن طبعته، إلا أنها صفت صفاً جديداً بأخطائها وتحريفاتها المخلة الكثيرة جداً، وأسقاطها العجيبة.
وهي طبعة صدرت عن دار الكتاب العربي ببيروت، طبعة أولى لكتاب اللباب، بتاريخ سنة ١٤١٥هـ ، وكتب عليها: «خرج أحاديثه وعلّق عليه : عبد الرزاق المهدي». اهـ ؟!
وكذلك طبعة أخرى صدرت في دمشق، عام ١٤٢٤هـ، كتب عليها: «طبعة منقحة ومقابلة على المخطوط ومزيدة بفصل لزيارة سيدنا النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم، وخدمات الفقه ومبادئه ، مع صور للمسائل، وفهرسة شاملة، حققه وخرَّج أحاديثه وعلق عليه: بشار بكري عرابي، وقدم له وراجعه : فضيلة الشيخ عمر المصري». اهـ ؟!!
وعن نسخ أخرى مخطوطة لكتاب اللباب، فقد بلغـنـي أنـه توجد نسخة مخطوطة في دمشق عند الأستاذ الشيخ عبد الجليــل عـطـا حفظه الله، وأن عليها تصحيحات للشيخ أحمد بن عبد الغني بن عمر عابدین (۱۲۳۸ هـ - ۱۳۰۷هـ ) ، وأن المؤلف الميداني شكره على هذه التصحيحات.
وقد اتصلت بالشيخ عبد الجليل عطا ، وأخبرني جزاه الله خيراً بما تقدم من معلومات، وأنه يعمل على مهل في إخراجها، وقد ذكرت له عملي على اللباب والقدوري، وخدمتي الطويلة لهما، لكن كأنه أراد أن يستأثر بها، وهكذا فلم يتيسر لي الوقوف عليهـا لأعـرف حالهـا ووصفها.
Chapter Two: Study of al-Lubab. In this edition there are many large omissions; the omission reached in some places two lines, and very many terrible errors, and it seems that Professor Muhammad al-Din Abd al-Hamid did not rely on a sound manuscript to compare the text; rather it reached me that he used to correct from his memory. Muhammad Muhyi al-Din did not mention in his introduction which manuscripts he relied on in his editing, whether in al-Mukhtasar or in al-Lubab, and at the end of his edition it says: 'Completed with the help of Allah Almighty and His facilitation, a review of the fourth volume of the book al-Lubab, and its editing by referring to the sources from which it was transmitted.' Huh?! And in this edition there is an addition of scattered words in multiple places unique to this edition; I don't know where the editor brought them from. I have designated this edition with the letter (D). These seven manuscripts are the ones I relied on in editing al-Lubab. After the aforementioned edition of Professor Muhammad Muhyi al-Din Abd al-Hamid, other editions appeared that were said to be critical, but in reality they are taken from his edition, except they were newly typeset with their many terrible errors and distortions and amazing omissions. They are: an edition published by Dar al-Kitab al-Arabi in Beirut, first edition of the book al-Lubab, dated 1415 AH, and it says: 'Its hadiths were extracted and annotated by Abd al-Razzaq al-Mahdi.' Huh?! And another edition published in Damascus, 1424 AH, it says: 'Revised and collated with the manuscript, augmented with a chapter on visiting our master the Prophet (peace be upon him), services of fiqh and its principles, with pictures of issues, and comprehensive indexing, edited, hadiths extracted, and annotated by Bashar Bakri Arabi, with introduction and review by His Eminence Shaykh Umar al-Misri.' Huh?!! As for other manuscript copies of al-Lubab, it reached me that there is a manuscript in Damascus with Professor Shaykh Abd al-Jalil Ata, may Allah preserve him, and that it contains corrections by Shaykh Ahmad ibn Abd al-Ghani ibn Umar Abidin (1238 AH - 1307 AH), and that the author al-Maydani thanked him for these corrections. I contacted Shaykh Abd al-Jalil Ata, and he informed me, may Allah reward him, of the aforementioned information, and that he is working slowly on publishing it; I mentioned to him my work on al-Lubab and al-Quduri and my long service to them, but it seemed he wanted to keep it to himself, and thus I was not able to consult it to know its condition and description.
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage is part of the editor's introduction (front matter) to the critical edition of al-Lubab. It provides a detailed critique of previous editions, particularly that of Muhammad Muhyi al-Din Abd al-Hamid, identifying numerous omissions and errors. The editor explains his own method of relying on seven manuscripts, designating one as (D). He also notes that subsequent editions merely reprint Abd al-Hamid's flawed text. Finally, he mentions an unverified manuscript with corrections by Shaykh Ahmad ibn Abd al-Ghani ibn Umar Abidin (a later Hanafi scholar) that he was unable to access. The tone is scholarly and critical, emphasizing the need for a reliable edition of this foundational Hanafi fiqh text.

Key Terms
أسقاط (asqāt): Omissions or lacunae in the printed text where portions of the manuscript were left out.
تحقيق (taḥqīq): Critical editing; the scholarly process of establishing a reliable text by comparing manuscripts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main criticism the editor levels against the edition by Muhammad Muhyi al-Din Abd al-Hamid?
A) It had too many footnotes.
B) It contained many omissions and errors, and the editor relied on memory rather than a sound manuscript.
C) It was printed in too small a font.
D) It was not authorized by any scholar.

Key Takeaway
For a reliable edition of al-Lubab, one must use a critical edition based on multiple manuscripts, not reprints of earlier flawed prints.

Mukhtasar al-Quduri's small size and divine acceptance made it the most copied Hanafi matn.

This passage from the critical edition of Al-Lubab provides a window into the extraordinary manuscript tradition of Mukhtasar al-Quduri. Commentary
This passage is front_matter from the critical edition of al-Lubab, providing a detailed account of the manuscript tradition of Mukhtasar al-Quduri and the editor's efforts. The author notes the astonishing number of manuscripts—566 listed in the Comprehensive Index, with many more in Turkey and other regions. The small size of the text contributed to its widespread copying. The editor also mentions a personal attempt to access a manuscript in Damascus with corrections by a later scholar, but was unable to do so. The passage highlights the global reach of the Hanafi school, as the manuscripts are found even in non-Islamic countries, and the importance of Ottoman printed editions. This provides students with an appreciation of the textual basis for this foundational Hanafi work.

Key Terms
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): The abridged legal manual by Imam Abu al-Husayn al-Quduri, a foundational text in the Hanafi school.
اللباب (Al-Lubab): A commentary (sharh) on Mukhtasar al-Quduri by ‘Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani, explaining its rulings.

The Manuscript Tradition of Mukhtasar al-Quduri: Preserving Hanafi Legal Authority
Discussion of manuscripts and editions used in critical edition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why manuscript evidence is essential for establishing the authoritative text of Mukhtasar al-Quduri and how textual variants can affect Hanafi legal rulings.

Core Idea
The transmission of legal knowledge depends on accurate manuscripts – a single variant can alter a ruling.

This passage introduces the massive manuscript tradition of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, a foundational Hanafi text. The author, Sa'id Bakdash, describes the abundance of manuscripts, their geographic distribution, and the methodological principles he used to select the most reliable ones. Understanding this process is crucial for appreciating how Hanafi jurists have preserved and transmitted legal rulings through centuries.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the scale of transmission
Note the claim of 566+ catalogued manuscripts, showing the work's popularity and the vast textual base available.
This number only from one index; actual count is much higher.
2
Identify selection criteria
What features made a manuscript authoritative? The author prioritizes oldest copies, those read to scholars, and those with precise diacritics and clear wording.
Reading certificates (sama') greatly enhance a manuscript's value.
3
Understand the role of commentaries
Commentaries often contain the full text of the Mukhtasar and may preserve variant readings from early authoritative copies.
Al-Hidayah by al-Marghinani is a prime example.
4
Connect text to law
Why did commentators care about textual variants? Because different readings can lead to different legal rulings (ahkam).
Even a single word change can affect an entire chapter.
5
Appreciate modern methodology
A critical edition today combines multiple manuscripts, printed editions, and commentary texts to produce a reliable, critically established text.
The author also consulted libraries in Turkey, Egypt, and the Two Holy Sanctuaries.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الثاني : دراسة عن اللباب
المبحث السادس
النسخ المعتمدة في تحقيق مختصر القدوري
نُسخ مختصر القدوري المخطوطة كثيرة كثرة بالغة، ولعل السبب في ذلك ما كتب الله له من القبول، وأيضاً بسبب صغر حجمه، ممـا يسهل نسخه وتداوله، وهذه النُّسَخ منتشرة في مكتبات العالم الإسلامي كله بل في مكتبات غير العالم الإسلامي.
(1)
وهكذا، فقد ذكر أصحاب الفهرس الشامل (٥٦٦) نسخة من مختصر القدوري، أما في مكتبات تركيا مما لم يذكره أصحاب الفهرس الشامل فشيء يصعب حصره وعده، وهكذا بقية بلاد الإسلام، وبالأخص البلاد التي انتشر فيها المذهب الحنفي، وكذلك مكتبات الحرمين الشريفين حيث تُجبى إليها ثمرات كل شيء.
وأما عن مطبوعات هذا المختصر، فله طبعات عديدة في بلاد مختلفة، وأهمها ما طُبع أيام الخلافة العثمانية، وصحح من قبل لجنة من العلماء، وكذلك ما طبع في مصر، ثم كان التصوير عنها. وسأذكر فيما يلي ما تيسر لي من مطبوعات هذا المختصر، وما انتقيته من النسخ المخطوطة منه مما ذكر في الفهارس، وما وقفتُ عليه في مكتبات الحرمين الشريفين، ومركز الملك فيصل الخيري في مدينة الرياض، حيث صورتُ أقدمها نَسخاً ، وما له مزية مهمة، كأن تكون النسخة مقروءة على عالم أو إمام، أو لها مزية من نحو دقة الضبط لكلماته، والتحرير لألفاظه، ونحو هذا.
وقد أكرمني الله تعالى بصور عن نسخ مخطوطة نفيسة نادرة لمختصر القدوري، من ناحية أنها أقدم النسخ تاريخاً، وفيهـا دقـة في الضبط، ومن ناحية أنه قرى بعضها على أئمة في الفقه الحنفي، ثم تداول هذه النسخ أئمة أعلام، وذلك بفضل الله، ولـه الحمـد أولاً وآخراً.
كما اعتمدت على النسخ المضمنة في شروح القدوري، سواء الشروح المطبوعة أم المخطوطة مثل الجوهرة النيرة، والسراج الوهاج، وشرح الأقطع والينابيع والزاهدي والإسبيجابي، وغيرها.
بل كنت أرجع إلى بداية الهداية للمرغيناني أصل كتاب الهداية ، حيث إنه ضمن فيه مختصر القدوري مع الجامع الصغير لمحمد بن الحسن الشيباني.
وهكذا أيضاً تابعتُ شُرَّاح القدوري ، وشراح الهداية في مسألة فوارق نسخ هذا المختصر، حيث أعاروا ذلك اهتماماً بالغاً؛ لما يترتب على اختلافها من آثار عديدة، وبخاصة في الأحكام.
Chapter Two: A Study of Al-Lubab
Section Six
Authoritative Manuscripts in the Critical Edition of Mukhtasar al-Quduri
The manuscripts of Mukhtasar al-Quduri are exceedingly numerous, perhaps due to the acceptance Allah granted it, and also because of its small size, which facilitated copying and circulation. These manuscripts are scattered across libraries of the entire Islamic world, and even in libraries outside the Islamic world.
(1)
Thus, the authors of the Comprehensive Index mentioned (566) copies of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, while in the libraries of Turkey, which the authors of the Comprehensive Index did not mention, there is something difficult to enumerate and count. Similarly, the rest of Islamic lands, especially those where the Hanafi madhhab spread, as well as the libraries of the Two Holy Sanctuaries, where the fruits of everything are gathered.
As for the printed editions of this Mukhtasar, it has numerous editions in different countries, the most important being those printed during the Ottoman Caliphate, corrected by a committee of scholars, as well as those printed in Egypt, and then photocopies thereof. I will mention below what I was able to obtain of the printed editions of this Mukhtasar, and what I selected from its manuscripts mentioned in the indexes, and what I came across in the libraries of the Two Holy Sanctuaries and the King Faisal Charitable Center in Riyadh, where I photographed the oldest copies, and those with important advantages, such as the copy having been read to a scholar or imam, or having the advantage of precise recording of its words, refinement of its expressions, and the like.
Allah Almighty has graced me with images of precious rare manuscripts of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, in that they are the oldest copies in date, with precision in recording, and in that some of them were read to imams of Hanafi jurisprudence, and then these copies were passed among prominent imams. This is by the grace of Allah, and to Him is all praise first and last.
I also relied on the copies embedded in commentaries on al-Quduri, both printed and manuscript, such as al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah, al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, Sharh al-Aqta', al-Yanabi', al-Zahidi, al-Isbijahbi, and others.
Rather, I would refer to the beginning of al-Hidayah by al-Marghinani, the original of the book al-Hidayah, because it included Mukhtasar al-Quduri along with al-Jami' al-Saghir by Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani.
Likewise, I followed the commentators of al-Quduri and the commentators of al-Hidayah on the matter of textual variants of this Mukhtasar, as they paid great attention to this, due to the numerous implications of these variants, especially in legal rulings.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage is from the introductory section of a modern critical edition of Al-Lubab (a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri). It is part of a study on the manuscripts and printed editions used in preparing the edition. The author, Dr. Sa'id Bakdash, explains the abundance of manuscripts of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, noting that over 566 copies have been catalogued in the Comprehensive Index alone, with many more in Turkey and other regions where the Hanafi madhhab spread. He highlights that the small size of the Mukhtasar contributed to its wide circulation. For printed editions, he notes the importance of Ottoman-era editions corrected by scholarly committees and Egyptian prints. His methodology for selecting manuscripts includes prioritizing the oldest dated copies, those read to or corrected by authoritative Hanafi jurists, and those with precise diacritics and clear wording. He also consulted manuscripts embedded in major commentaries such as al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah and al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, and relied on the text of Mukhtasar al-Quduri as found within al-Hidayah by al-Marghinani. By referencing variant readings from commentators, he aims to resolve textual differences that affect legal rulings. The passage is not a fiqh ruling but a textual introduction, crucial for understanding the critical apparatus of the edition.

Key Terms
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): A concise manual of Hanafi fiqh by Imam Ahmad ibn al-Husayn al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), widely used as a foundational text for students.
نسخ مخطوطة (nusakh makhtutah): Manuscript copies of the work, handwritten on paper or parchment.
شروح القدوري (shuruh al-Quduri): Commentaries and supercommentaries written to explain and expand upon Mukhtasar al-Quduri.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how many copies of Mukhtasar al-Quduri were listed in the Comprehensive Index?
A) 500 copies
B) 566 copies
C) 600 copies
D) 700 copies

Key Takeaway
The reliability of a fiqh text depends on the careful study of its manuscript tradition.

Introduction and Front Matter

Understanding Textual Criticism in Hanafi Fiqh
Editorial methodology for textual criticism of Mukhtasar al-Quduri

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why textual variants in Mukhtasar al-Quduri matter for deriving accurate Hanafi rulings.

Core Idea
A single word change can alter a ruling; textual criticism safeguards the transmission of the madhhab.

This passage from the critical edition of Al-Lubab gives us a rare behind-the-scenes look at how scholars ensure the fiqh we learn is reliable. The editor describes consulting multiple manuscripts and printed editions, noting even marginal differences. Understanding this process is essential for anyone who wants to know why we trust certain texts over others—and why not all printed editions are equal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the textual focus
The editor is preparing a critical edition of Mukhtasar al-Quduri. He lists the sources he used: manuscripts from libraries in Mecca, Medina, Riyadh, and earlier commentaries. Identify which types of sources he mentions.
Mukhtasar al-Quduri is a foundational Hanafi text.
2
Distinguish manuscript from printed editions
The editor separates manuscripts (hand-copied) from printed editions. He gives special attention to the oldest dated manuscripts and those read to Hanafi authorities. Printed editions come from Istanbul and Cairo. Note the details: page counts, lines, and supervision.
Manuscripts have unique errors and variants.
3
Recognize the importance of variant readings
The editor states that variant readings (furuq) between copies have 'numerous effects, especially in rulings.' This means a single difference in wording can change a legal conclusion. The guided discovery here: how would you verify a disputed ruling in Mukhtasar al-Quduri?
Variant readings are not trivial; they affect fiqh.
4
Analyze the editorial symbols and methodology
The editor uses symbols for each edition (e.g., al-Babi for the Halabi print). He also relies on commentaries and even Marghinani's Bidayat al-Hidayah. Consider why a commentator's work is a source for the original text.
Commentators sometimes quote the original faithfully.
5
Apply the method to a hypothetical scenario
Imagine you find two manuscripts of Mukhtasar al-Quduri with different wording on the conditions of wudu. How would the editor's method help you decide which is more reliable? Consider age, authority of readers, and cross-checking with commentaries.
The editor's approach is a model for all Hanafi text work.

الفصل الثاني : دراسة عن اللباب
من العلماء، وكذلك ما طبع في مصر، ثم كان التصوير عنها. وسأذكر فيما يلي ما تيسر لي من مطبوعات هذا المختصر، وما انتقيته من النسخ المخطوطة منه مما ذكر في الفهارس، وما وقفتُ عليه في مكتبات الحرمين الشريفين، ومركز الملك فيصل الخيري في مدينة الرياض، حيث صورتُ أقدمها نَسخاً ، وما له مزية مهمة، كأن تكون النسخة مقروءة على عالم أو إمام، أو لها مزية من نحو دقة الضبط لكلماته، والتحرير لألفاظه، ونحو هذا.
وقد أكرمني الله تعالى بصور عن نسخ مخطوطة نفيسة نادرة لمختصر القدوري، من ناحية أنها أقدم النسخ تاريخاً، وفيهـا دقـة في الضبط، ومن ناحية أنه قرى بعضها على أئمة في الفقه الحنفي، ثم تداول هذه النسخ أئمة أعلام، وذلك بفضل الله، ولـه الحمـد أولاً وآخراً.
كما اعتمدت على النسخ المضمنة في شروح القدوري، سواء الشروح المطبوعة أم المخطوطة مثل الجوهرة النيرة، والسراج الوهاج، وشرح الأقطع والينابيع والزاهدي والإسبيجابي، وغيرها.
بل كنت أرجع إلى بداية الهداية للمرغيناني أصل كتاب الهداية ، حيث إنه ضمن فيه مختصر القدوري مع الجامع الصغير لمحمد بن الحسن الشيباني.
وهكذا أيضاً تابعتُ شُرَّاح القدوري ، وشراح الهداية في مسألة فوارق نسخ هذا المختصر، حيث أعاروا ذلك اهتماماً بالغاً؛ لما يترتب على اختلافها من آثار عديدة، وبخاصة في الأحكام.
وقد خدمتني في السعي لإثبات نص صحيح سليم لهذا المختصر، مع بيان وإثبات الفوارق المهمة ذات الأثر منها. النسخ الكثيرة المتنوعة المتعددة خدمة جليلة
وقد رمزتُ لنسخ القدوري المخطوطة بتاريخ نسخها، وكذلك المطبوعة إلا طبعة البابي الحلبي، فرمزت لها بـ (البابي)
أ - النسخ المطبوعة :
١ـ نسخة سنة ١٣٠٩هـ، مطبوعة في المطبعة العثمانية باسطنبول، دار السعادة زمن السلطان عبد الحميد.
وقد كُتبت في حاشية الصفحات تعليقات مفيدة، وحواش لطيفة توضح مسائله، وذُكر في نهاية كل حاشية المصدر الذي نُقلت عنه. وقد جاءت هذه النسخة في (١٤٥) صفحة مرصوصة، وفي كل صفحة (۲۷) سطراً، وفي كل سطر (١٢) كلمة.
وهي معتمدة ومرخصة من نظارة المعارف العثمانية، وأشرف على تصحيحها خمسة من علماء الدولة العثمانية.
وميزة هذه النسخة أن فيها زيادات انفردت بها عن النسخ الأخرى المطبوعة ، ولا تخلو من بعض الأخطاء المطبعية.
٢ نسخة سنة ١٣٢٤ هـ، مطبوعة في المطبعة الميمنية في القاهرة، مطبعة مصطفى البابي الحلبي وأخويه بكري وعيسى. وقد جاءت هذه النسخة في (۱۲۰) صفحة مرصوصة، وفي كل صفحة (٢٦) سطراً، وفي كل سطر (١٥) كلمة.
Chapter Two: Study of Al-Lubab
Among scholars, and also what was printed in Egypt, then photography was taken from them. I will mention below what is available to me of printed editions of this Mukhtasar, and what I selected from its manuscript copies mentioned in catalogs, and what I came across in the libraries of the Two Holy Sanctuaries and the King Faisal Charitable Center in Riyadh, where I photographed the oldest copies and those with important merit, such as the copy being read to a scholar or imam, or having the merit of precise wording and refined phrasing.
And Allah Almighty has favored me with photographs of precious rare manuscript copies of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, from the aspect that they are the oldest copies in date, and they have precision in transcription, and that some were read to imams of Hanafi fiqh, and then these copies were circulated by eminent imams - all by the grace of Allah, and to Him is praise first and last.
I also relied on the copies embedded in the commentaries of al-Quduri, both printed and manuscript, such as al-Jawharat al-Nayyirah, al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, Sharh al-Aqta', al-Yanabi', al-Zahidi, al-Isbijabi, and others.
Indeed, I referred to Bidayat al-Hidayah by al-Marghinani, the original of al-Hidayah, as he included in it Mukhtasar al-Quduri along with al-Jami' al-Saghir by Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani.
Likewise, I followed the commentators of al-Quduri and the commentators of al-Hidayah on the matter of variant readings of this Mukhtasar, as they gave it great attention due to the numerous effects resulting from differences, especially in rulings.
The many diverse copies served me greatly in striving to establish a correct sound text for this Mukhtasar, along with explaining and establishing the important variant readings that have impact.
I have coded the manuscript copies of al-Quduri by their date of copying, and similarly the printed ones except for the Bābī al-Ḥalabī edition, for which I used the symbol (al-Bābī).
A - Printed editions:
1. The edition of year 1309 AH, printed at the Ottoman Press in Istanbul, Dar al-Sa'ada during the time of Sultan Abdul Hamid. Useful comments and fine glosses were written in the margins explaining its issues, and at the end of each comment the source from which it was taken was mentioned. This edition is in (145) tightly packed pages, each page (27) lines, each line (12) words. It is approved and licensed by the Ottoman Ministry of Education, and five scholars of the Ottoman state supervised its correction. The distinction of this edition is that it contains additions unique to it compared to other printed editions, and it is not free of some typographical errors.
2. The edition of year 1324 AH, printed at al-Maymuna Press in Cairo, Mustafa al-Babi al-Halabi and his brothers Bakri and Isa. This edition is in (120) tightly packed pages, each page (26) lines, each line (15) words.
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This passage is part of the front matter of the critical edition of Al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri by al-Maydani. The editor describes his methodology for establishing a reliable text of Mukhtasar al-Quduri. He lists the manuscript copies he consulted, including those from libraries in Mecca, Medina, and Riyadh. He also relied on manuscript copies embedded within commentaries of al-Quduri, such as al-Jawharat al-Nayyirah and al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, and even referred to Marghinani's Bidayat al-Hidayah. The passage then enumerates two printed editions: the 1309 AH Ottoman edition from Istanbul, which has annotated margins and is approved by the Ottoman ministry, and the 1324 AH Cairo edition from Mustafa al-Babi al-Halabi. The editor notes the page and line counts of each. This is purely editorial description and does not contain any fiqh rulings.

Key Terms
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): The famous concise manual of Hanafi fiqh by Imam Ahmad al-Quduri (d. 428 AH).
الفروق (al-Furuq): Variant readings or differences between copies of a text.
التحقيق (al-Tahqiq): Critical editing of a text to produce the most authentic version.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) One
B) Two
C) Three
D) Four

Key Takeaway
Textual criticism is an integral part of fiqh preservation: variant readings in Mukhtasar al-Quduri can affect actual rulings, so scholars must consult multiple sources to establish the most reliable text.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Evaluating Printed Editions and Manuscripts: The Case of al-Quduri's Mukhtasar
Describing the editions and manuscripts used for textual criticism

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the reliability of different printed editions and manuscripts of a Hanafi fiqh text based on criteria such as date, corrections, and marginal notes.

Core Idea
Not all printed editions of a classical fiqh text are equal; critical evaluation of manuscripts and editions is essential for accurate legal study.

This passage from al-Maydani's introduction to al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Quduri illustrates the meticulous work of a Hanafi scholar in establishing a reliable text. He compares four printed editions from Istanbul, Cairo, and the Indian subcontinent, and highlights a key manuscript from 611 AH. Understanding this methodology helps us appreciate the chain of transmission and the importance of textual accuracy in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the editions
List the printed editions mentioned, noting their dates, publishers, and locations. This gives the first impression of their provenance.
Al-Maydani covers editions from 1309, 1324, and 1377 AH, plus older prints from India.
2
Assess the corrections
Who supervised the correction? Was it a committee or a single scholar? The Ottoman edition had five scholars, while the 1324 edition had one scholar. Committee oversight often indicates higher reliability.
3
Examine unique features
Does the edition contain marginal notes, additions, or unique readings? The 1309 edition has unique additions, but also typographical errors. Unique features can help identify the text's transmission history.
4
Compare manuscripts
What manuscripts are used? Their date and provenance are crucial. The 611 AH manuscript is the oldest confirmed, giving it high authority.
Al-Maydani also notes a possible 5th-century manuscript that remains unverified.
5
Determine the preferred edition
Based on the above criteria, which edition is most authoritative? The 1309 Ottoman edition, with its committee oversight and marginal notes, might be preferred despite errors.
Al-Maydani's own edition likely relies on a combination of these sources.

Chapter Two: Study of al-Lubab. These [171] served me in the effort to establish a correct and sound text for this abridgment, along with explaining and establishing the important differences that have effect. The many varied and numerous copies are a great service. I have coded the manuscript copies of al-Quduri with their date of copying, and likewise the printed ones, except for the Bābī al-Ḥalabī edition, for which I used the symbol (al-Bābī). A - Printed editions: 1- The edition of 1309 AH, printed in the Ottoman Press in Istanbul, Dar al-Sa‘ada, during the reign of Sultan Abdul Hamid. Useful comments and elegant notes were written in the margins of its pages, clarifying its issues, and at the end of each note the source from which it was taken was mentioned. This edition comprises 145 tightly packed pages, each page having 27 lines, and each line 12 words. It is approved and licensed by the Ottoman Ministry of Education, and five scholars of the Ottoman state supervised its correction. A feature of this edition is that it contains additions unique among other printed editions, but it is not free of some typographical errors. 2- The edition of 1324 AH, printed in the Maymūnīyya Press in Cairo, Mustafa al-Bābī al-Ḥalabī and his two brothers Bakrī and ‘Īsā Press. This edition comprises 120 tightly packed pages, each page having 26 lines, and each line 15 words. Its correction was supervised by Shaykh Muḥammad al-Zuhrī al-Ghamrāwī, and it is a fairly good edition. 3- The edition of 1377 AH, printed in the press of Mustafa al-Bābī al-Ḥalabī and Sons Company in Cairo, corrected by a committee of scholars. This edition comprises 125 pages, each page having 27 lines, and each line 14 words. This edition seems to be taken from the previous edition, and God knows best. 4- There are also old editions of the abridgment in India, Sindh, and Pakistan; I have some of them and they have no special merit, so I did not mention them here, while reminding that I have indicated in the study of this abridgment its first and oldest editions and their locations. B - Manuscript editions: I begin with the oldest in date of copying, then those that follow, and so on: 1- The copy (611 AH), which is the oldest I have come across. (1) The authors of the Comprehensive Index mentioned a copy of al-Quduri from the 5th century, and that it is in the Algeria Museum under number 980, comprising 176 folios. So I sent to verify that to my dear friend, the virtuous brother, Professor Shaykh Nabil Ḥafāf – originally from Algeria, who is now preparing a doctorate in uṣūl al-fiqh. But his reply – may God reward him and do good to him – after researching and searching, was that nothing exists under that number as the authors of the Comprehensive Index mentioned. So God knows best about its condition and location.
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage is from the introduction (Chapter Two) of the commentary 'al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Quduri' by ‘Abd al-Ghani al-Maydānī. Here the author discusses the sources he used to establish a reliable text of al-Quduri’s Mukhtasar. He describes four printed editions and mentions the manuscript he relied upon. The first is the Ottoman edition of 1309 AH (1891-92 CE), which has marginal notes and was approved by the Ottoman authorities. The second is the 1324 AH (1906-07 CE) Cairo edition by al-Bābī al-Ḥalabī, supervised by al-Ghamrāwī. The third is a later 1377 AH (1957-58 CE) edition also from al-Bābī. He notes older editions from the Indian subcontinent but considers them unimportant. For manuscripts, he begins with a copy dated 611 AH (1214 CE) which he claims to have found, though he adds a note about a possible misidentification in the Comprehensive Index regarding a 5th-century (11th century CE) copy. This section is typical of critical editions of classical texts, where the editor enumerates the textual witnesses and evaluates their quality. The author's careful approach demonstrates the importance of textual authenticity in Hanafi fiqh scholarship.

Key Terms
النُسَخ المَطْبُوعَة (al-nusakh al-maṭbū‘a): Printed editions of the text, listed and evaluated by the author for their quality and features.
النُسَخ المَخْطُوطَة (al-nusakh al-makhṭūṭa): Manuscript copies of the text, often dated, used for comparison and establishing the correct reading.
المُخْتَصَر (al-mukhtaṣar): Refers to al-Qudūrī's abridgment (Mukhtasar al-Qudūrī) which is the base text being commented upon.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Critical evaluation of printed editions and manuscripts is essential for establishing an accurate text of a Hanafi fiqh work.
