Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Manuscript Study and Missing Sections (Saqt) in Hanafi Texts
Manuscript study describing saqt in Al-Lubab.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and interpret missing sections (saqt) in a Hanafi fiqh manuscript and explain their impact on the reliability and completeness of the transmitted text.

Core Idea
Missing folios (saqt) compromise textual integrity; comparison with other manuscripts restores missing rulings.

This lesson examines a critical apparatus from a manuscript of Al-Lubab, a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. The passage documents missing folios in the books of Hajj, hunting, sacrifice, oaths, testimony, and judge's etiquette, as well as near the end. Understanding how scholars identify and estimate such gaps is essential for anyone working with classical Hanafi texts, as saqt can lead to incomplete rulings being transmitted.

Guided Path
1
Identify the manuscript and its significance
Note that this is a copy of Al-Lubab, a sharh on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, completed in 794 AH. Recognize that manuscript studies help verify the exact transmission of Hanafi fiqh.
The scribe is As-Sulami al-Hanafi as-Sarkhadi.
2
Locate the reported missing sections (saqt)
Find the specific folio ranges given: loss of five folios in the book of Hajj starting at folio 28; another five folios from folio 94 covering topics including hunting, sacrifice, oaths, testimony, and judge's etiquette; and two folios lost from the end of Mukhtasar al-Quduri.
The author estimated these by comparing with the printed edition of Al-Quduri (Al-Babi Al-Halabi).
3
Understand the cause and impact of saqt
Consider the author's hypothesis that losses occurred during photography in Cairo. Reflect that missing folios mean the corresponding fiqh rulings are absent from this manuscript, potentially leading to gaps in understanding if not cross-referenced.
Saqt can be partial (loss of some pages) or complete (loss of entire sections).
4
Recognize the value of collation
The author mentions a second copy (649 AH, Berlin) with 149 folios. Collation (muqabala) between manuscripts is a standard method to restore missing text and verify authenticity.
The Berlin copy was sought for photography but not used here.
5
Apply critical thinking to manuscript reliability
Assess that even with saqt, a manuscript can still be valuable if the missing parts are identified and supplemented from other sources. Understand that awareness of saqt prevents over-reliance on a single copy.
This passage itself is a critical refinement – it corrects the impression that the manuscript is complete.

And upon it is another ownership that came: 'And it transferred to the ownership of the poor, humble Yusuf, son of our master the virtuous, perfect scholar, proof of Islam... son of Yusuf, son of the pole, the gnostic, the shaykh. May Allah have mercy on him.' End quote. And on the right of the title page is the following: '6- 'Umar. In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. The erudite, noble scholar Shams ad-Din Abu Abdullah Muhammad, son of the late illustrious scholar Taj ad-Din as-Sarkhadi—may Allah envelop him in His mercy and support his son—presented to me this entire book, which is Mukhtasar al-Quduri—may Allah have mercy on its author—from its beginning to its end in one sitting, in places that indicate his memorization of it all with the best presentation and most splendid expression, along with preserving its grammatical parsing in those places, and a fluent, eloquent tongue. And it is no wonder for a young man to follow in the footsteps of his father. And its scribe heard from his teachers, may Allah have mercy on them, that whoever memorizes Mukhtasar al-Quduri deserves to be placed in a rank—as in the manuscript—of sixteen dirhams as a stipend in the schools. How much more since his expenditure was in the school under the supervision of the noble, eminent, excellent lord, the chief judge of the Hanafis—may Allah prolong his shade—in agreement with what the servant heard from the teachers, and that the teachers and professors there had decided his salary, as a regard for his excellence and in honor of his father, for he was from the divinely learned scholars...' End quote. And the full page did not appear in the manuscript image to know the writer of this statement and its date. And in this copy there is a loss I estimated at five folios in the book of Hajj, beginning from folio (28). Also there is another large loss beginning from folio (94)—although the numbering is consecutive—which I estimated at five folios by comparison with the printed edition of Al-Quduri, copy of Al-Babi Al-Halabi, on the topics of hunting, sacrifice, oaths, invitation, testimony, withdrawal of testimony, and the etiquette of the judge. Also there is a loss of about two folios from the end of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, and before the beginning of the copy of Al-Aqida at-Tahawiyya. Perhaps these losses are due to the photography from Cairo, as often happens, and Allah knows best. I was unable to remedy them. 2- Copy (649 AH), an original kept in Berlin, Germany, as mentioned by the authors of the Comprehensive Index, and it consists of 149 folios. When I requested its photography through the dear, virtuous brother, Dr. (1). (9/306)
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This passage is a scholarly study of the manuscript of Al-Lubab, a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. It begins by recording a note from the scribe, As-Sulami al-Hanafi as-Sarkhadi, who finished writing in 794 AH, and includes ownership transfers and a presentation statement praising the scholar Shams ad-Din who presented the book. The text then details known missing sections in this manuscript: a loss of five folios in the book of Hajj (starting at folio 28) and another five-folio loss beginning at folio 94 covering hunting, sacrifice, oaths, testimony, and judge's etiquette. Additionally, two folios are missing from the end of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, before Al-Aqida at-Tahawiyya. The author hypothesizes that these losses occurred during photography in Cairo. The passage also mentions a second copy (dated 649 AH) preserved in Berlin with 149 folios, which was sought for collation. The text serves as a critical apparatus for understanding the manuscript's condition and missing content.

Key Terms
اللباب (Al-Lubab): A commentary (sharh) on Mukhtasar al-Quduri by as-Sulami al-Hanafi as-Sarkhadi.
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): A foundational Hanafi fiqh text authored by Imam al-Quduri.
سقط (saqt): Missing sections (folios) in the manuscript identified by comparison with another copy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) Seven folios
D) Ten folios

Key Takeaway
Manuscript studies are essential for preserving and verifying Hanafi fiqh texts; identifying saqt ensures that missing rulings are not overlooked.

The Role of Manuscripts in Hanafi Fiqh Scholarship
Three manuscript descriptions for a critical edition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate a manuscript's value for a critical edition of a Hanafi fiqh text by analyzing its date, completeness, vowelization, and marginal notations.

Core Idea
A manuscript's date, completeness, vowelization, and marginal glosses determine its utility for reconstructing an authoritative text.

The passage describes three manuscripts of Mukhtasar al-Quduri used by the editor of al-Lubab. Understanding why these manuscripts were chosen helps us appreciate the rigorous textual scholarship behind reliable fiqh texts. This lesson will equip you to identify key features that make a manuscript valuable.

Guided Path
1
Identify the manuscript's date and scribe
Note the year and any named copyist to establish relative age and authenticity.
Earlier is generally better, but not absolute.
2
Examine completeness
Does the manuscript cover the entire text? The 649 AH copy starts from the middle, limiting its use.
Missing sections require reliance on other witnesses.
3
Check vowelization (shakl)
Full vowelization indicates careful copying and helps reduce ambiguity in reading.
The 727 AH copy is fully vowelized; the 745 AH only partially.
4
Look at marginal notes
Marginal glosses often contain scholarly commentary or corrections, adding value.
The 649 and 727 copies have many fiqh comments.
5
Compare multiple manuscripts
Using several witnesses allows cross-checking and establishing a more reliable text.
The editor used three dated manuscripts plus others.

الفصل الثاني : دراسة عن اللباب
عبد الرحمن سليمان المزيني مدير مكتبة الملك عبد العزيز بالمدينة المنورة، وهو بدوره عن طريق مركز الملك فيصل الخيري جزاهم الله خيراً جميعاً، وحين وصلتني هذه النسخة وجدتها تبدأ من منتصف الكتاب من باب البيع الفاسد وقبله خمسة سطور فقط، الصفحة الأولى بترقيمهم، ولم أعلم بحال أول هذه النسخة، وهي ومكان وجودها. وهي نسخة قديمة نفيسة، ضُبطت فيها غالب الكلمات بالشكل، وخطها واضح. وتقع في (١٤٩) ورقة، وفي كل صفحة (۱۳) سطراً، وفي كل سطر (٩) كلمات، وكتب في حاشيتها في صفحات عديدة بعض الحواشي والتعليقات المفيدة على مختصر القدوري. وقد جاء في آخر هذه النسخة ما يلي: تم المختصر بحمد الله وحُسن توفيقه على يدي العبد المذنب الفقير إلى رحمة الله تعالى: علي بن عمر بن أبي بكر بن أحمد الأصفهاني، وقت المغرب من ليلة السبت، سادس من ذي قعدة، من سنة تسع وأربعين وستمائة، والحمد لله رب العالمين، وصلواته على سيدنا محمد وآله وأصحابه أجمعين». اهـ وكتب في آخر النسخة في حاشية الصفحة بالخط نفسه: اتفق - هكذا - المقابلة بتمامها يوم الجمعة ثالث عشر، في شهر ذي قعدة، من سنة تسع وأربعين وستمائة». اهـ
٣ـ نسخة (٧٢٧هـ)، وأصل هذه النسخة محفوظ في المكتبة السليمانية في اسطنبول (١) قسم (ملا جلبي)، برقم (٥٣). وتقع هذه النسخة في (١٦٠) ورقة، وفي كل صفحة (١١) سطراً، وفي كل سطر (٩) كلمات. وهي نسخة نفيسة مضبوطة بالشكل في كلماتها كلها، وقد نُثرت على حواشي النسخة تعليقات فقهية ليست بالقليلة، بخط دقيق جداً، فيها فوائد تتعلق بشرح نص المختصر. وقد جاء في آخر النسخة: تم المختصر بحمد الله وعونه وصلى الله على محمد وآله، يوم الاثنين، من ربيع الآخر، سنة سبعة وعشرين وسبعمائة، على يد أضعف خلق الله المعترف بذنبه: (طُقْصُوا)، غفر الله له ولمن قرأه». اهـ
٤ـ نسخة (٧٤٥هـ)، وأصل هذه النسخة محفوظ في المكتبة البريطانية، قسم المجموعات الشرقية والمكتبة الهندية، وتقع في (١٤٧) ورقة، وفي كل صفحة (١٥) سطراً، وفي كل سطر (٩) كلمات، وهي نسخة مضبوطة بالشكل في ربعها الأول فقط، وختمت بأن نسخها كان في السادس عشر جمادى الآخر، سنة (۱) وقد تفضل مشكوراً بتصويرها صديقي العزيز الأخ الفاضل الأستاذ الدكتور خليل قوتلاي حفظه الله، وكذلك تصوير النسخة التي هي بتاريخ ٨٤٠ هـ. (۲) تم تصوير هذه النسخة، والتي تليها من مركز الملك فيصل الخيري بالرياض، جزى الله القائمين عليه خيراً.
Chapter Two: Study of al-Lubab. Abd al-Rahman Sulayman al-Muzayni, Director of King Abdul Aziz Library in Medina, via King Faisal Charitable Center, may Allah reward them all. When this copy reached me, I found it started from the middle of the book from the chapter of invalid sale, with only five lines before it, the first page by their numbering, and I did not know the state of the beginning of this copy, nor its location. It is a precious old copy, in which most words are vowelized, and its script is clear. It consists of 149 folios, each page has 13 lines, each line 9 words. In its margins on many pages are written some beneficial glosses and comments on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. At the end of this copy appears the following: 'The Mukhtasar was completed with the praise of Allah and His good success by the hand of the sinful servant in need of Allah's mercy: Ali ibn Umar ibn Abi Bakr ibn Ahmad al-Isfahani, at Maghrib time on Saturday night, the sixth of Dhu al-Qa'dah, in the year 649 AH. And praise be to Allah, Lord of the worlds, and His blessings upon our master Muhammad and his family and all his companions.' End quote. Also written at the end in the margin in the same hand: 'The collation was completed fully on Friday, the thirteenth of Dhu al-Qa'dah, in the year 649 AH.' End quote. 3. Copy (727 AH). The original of this copy is preserved in the Suleymaniye Library in Istanbul, Molla Çelebi section, number 53. This copy consists of 160 folios, each page has 11 lines, each line 9 words. It is a precious copy fully vowelized, and on its margins are scattered not a few fiqh comments in very fine handwriting, containing benefits related to the commentary on the text of the Mukhtasar. At the end of the copy: 'The Mukhtasar was completed with the praise of Allah and His help, and blessings upon Muhammad and his family, on Monday, Rabi' al-Akhir, year 727 AH, by the hand of the weakest of Allah's creatures confessing his sin: (Tuqsuwa?), may Allah forgive him and whoever reads it.' End quote. 4. Copy (745 AH). The original of this copy is preserved in the British Library, Oriental and India Office Collections, and consists of 147 folios, each page has 15 lines, each line 9 words. It is a copy vowelized only in its first quarter, and it concludes that its copying was on the sixteenth of Jumada al-Akhir, year [؟]. My dear friend Dr. Khalil Kutlay, may Allah preserve him, was kind enough to photograph it, as well as the copy dated 840 AH. These copies were photographed from the King Faisal Charitable Center in Riyadh, may Allah reward those in charge.
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This passage is from the editor's introduction to al-Lubab, describing three manuscripts used for the critical edition. The first manuscript (dated 649 AH) was incomplete at the start, beginning from the chapter on invalid sale, but is valuable for its vowelization and marginal notes. The second manuscript (727 AH) from Istanbul is fully vowelized with extensive fiqh glosses. The third (745 AH) from the British Library is only partially vowelized. These manuscripts form the textual basis for the edition. The editor acknowledges assistance from King Faisal Center and Dr. Khalil Kutlay.

Key Terms
نسخة (nuskhah): A handwritten manuscript copy of a book, used as textual witness.
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): The famous Hanafi fiqh manual by Imam al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), which al-Lubab is a commentary on.
شكل (shakl): Vowelization marks (diacritics) on Arabic letters to indicate short vowels.
حواشي (hawashi): Marginal notes or glosses, often containing commentary or corrections.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Studying Hanafi Manuscripts: The Codicological Evidence of al-Lubab
Manuscript description and codicological details

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key codicological features described in the manuscripts of al-Lubab and explain their significance for the transmission of Hanafi fiqh texts.

Core Idea
Manuscript copies reveal the living chain of transmission — each folio count and note tells part of the story.

This passage is not a fiqh ruling but a window into how Hanafi texts were transmitted. The editor of al-Lubab lists three manuscripts, giving details about their size, vowelization, marginal notes, and reading certificates. These details help us reconstruct the scholarly network that preserved al-Quduri's Mukhtasar and its commentary. Understanding this background strengthens your confidence in the text you study.

Guided Path
1
Identify Physical Features
Note the folio count, lines per page, and words per line for each manuscript. These numbers help determine completeness and scribal habits.
Folio counts vary: 160, 147, 101. Fewer folios often mean smaller script or fewer marginalia.
2
Assess Vowelization (ضبط بالشكل)
Check whether the manuscript is fully or partially vowelized. Full vowelization indicates careful copying and likely a scholar's hand. Partial vowelization may suggest a quicker, less formal copy.
The 727 AH copy and 768 AH copy are fully vowelized; the 745 AH copy only in its first quarter.
3
Examine Marginal Notes and Certificates
Marginal notes contain extra fiqh comments. Reading certificates (as in the 768 AH copy) record who heard the text and from whom, directly linking the manuscript to known scholars.
The 768 AH copy was read to the Hanafi judge Ibn al-Sa'igh by Qutlubugha al-Hanafi, then re-read.
4
Synthesize for Editorial Reliability
Combine all evidence to judge which manuscript is most authoritative. Full vowelization, clear handwriting, and a strong reading chain increase reliability.
The 768 AH copy appears most reliable due to its clear script and verified reading.

الفصل الثاني : دراسة عن اللباب السليمانية في اسطنبول (۱) قسم (ملا جلبي)، برقم (٥٣). وتقع هذه النسخة في (١٦٠) ورقة، وفي كل صفحة (١١) سطراً، وفي كل سطر (۹) كلمات. وهي نسخة نفيسة مضبوطة بالشكل في كلماتها كلها، وقد نُثرت على حواشي النسخة تعليقات فقهية ليست بالقليلة، بخط دقيق جداً، فيها فوائد تتعلق بشرح نص المختصر . وقد جاء في آخر النسخة: تم المختصر بحمد الله ،وعونه وصلى الله على محمد وآله، يوم الاثنين، من ربيع الآخر، سنة سبعة وعشرين وسبعمائة ، على يد أضعف خلق الله المعترف بذنبه : (طُقْصُوا)، غفر الله له ولمن قرأه». اهـ ٤ـ نسخة (٧٤٥هـ) ، وأصل هذه النسخة محفوظ في المكتبة البريطانية، قسم المجموعات الشرقية والمكتبة الهندية، وتقع في (١٤٧) ورقة، وفي كل صفحة (١٥) سطراً، وفي كل سطر (٩) كلمات، وهي نسخة مضبوطة بالشكل في ربعها الأول فقط، وختمت بأن نسخها كان في السادس عشر جمادى الآخر، سنة خمس وأربعين وسبعمائة. ه - نسخة (٧٦٨هـ) ، وأصل هذه النسخة محفوظ في المكتبة البريطانية قسم المجموعات الشرقية، والمكتبة الهندية. وتقع في (۱۰۱) ورقة، وفي كل صفحة (١٧) سطراً، وأحياناً (١٥) سطراً، وفي كل سطر (١٣) كلمة. وهي نسخة نفيسة مضبوطة بالشكل، وخطها واضح جداً، قرئت على إمام فقيه حنفي كبير، وهو الإمام شمس الدين محمد بن عبد الرحمن بن الصائغ الحنفي (١) ، المصري، قاضي العسكر، الأديب النحوي الكبير، صاحب المصنفات الفقهية والنحوية العديدة الكبيرة، المتوفى سنة (٧٧٧هـ). وقد قرئت عليه سنة (٧٦٨ هـ) ، والقارئ هو الإمام القدوة قطلوبغا بن كراي الحنفي، كما جاء وصفه بذلك في المخطوط. ثم قرئت هذه النسخة نفسها مرة أخرى على قارئها الأول قطلوبغا ابن كراي الحنفي. وقد جاء في خاتمة النسخة ما يلي: تم المختصر بحمد الله ، وعونه صحت المقابلة وثبتت. وافق الفراغ من قراءة جميعه على الشيخ الإمام العالم، فريد (۱) له ترجمة في الفوائد البهية ص ١٧٥ ، الدرر الكامنة ٤٩٩/٣ ، الأعلام .١٩٢/٦
Chapter Two: Study of al-Lubab. The Süleymaniye in Istanbul (1) Section (Molla Çelebi), number (53). This copy is in (160) folios, every page (11) lines, every line (9) words. It is a precious copy fully vowelized, with numerous fiqh comments on its margins in very fine handwriting, containing benefits related to the commentary on the text of al-Mukhtasar. At the end of the copy: 'al-Mukhtasar was completed by the praise of God and His help, and blessings on Muhammad and his family, on Monday, Rabi' al-Akhir, year 727, by the weakest of God's creatures acknowledging his sin: (Taqsu?), may God forgive him and whoever reads it.' 4. Copy (745 AH): The original of this copy is preserved in the British Library, Oriental Collections and India Office Library. It is in (147) folios, every page (15) lines, every line (9) words. It is vowelized only in its first quarter, and ends with the note that copying was completed on 16 Jumada al-Akhir, year 745. 5. Copy (768 AH): The original of this copy is preserved in the British Library, Oriental Collections and India Office Library. It is in (101) folios, every page (17) lines, sometimes (15) lines, every line (13) words. It is a precious copy, fully vowelized, with very clear handwriting. It was read to a great Hanafi jurist Imam, namely Imam Shams al-Din Muhammad ibn Abd al-Rahman ibn al-Sa'igh al-Hanafi (1), Egyptian, army judge, great literary figure and grammarian, author of many large works on fiqh and grammar, died 777 AH. It was read to him in 768 AH, and the reader was the eminent Imam Qutlubugha ibn Karai al-Hanafi, as described in the manuscript. Then this same copy was read again to its first reader Qutlubugha ibn Karai al-Hanafi. At the end of the copy: 'al-Mukhtasar was completed by the praise of God and His help. The collation was correct and confirmed. The completion of its reading to the Shaykh Imam al-Allamah, the unique...' (1) His biography is in al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya p. 175, al-Durar al-Kamina 3/499, al-A'lam 6/192.
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage is a manuscript description section (front matter) of the published edition of al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri. It lists and describes four manuscripts used for the edition: 1) A copy from the Süleymaniye Library, dated 727 AH, in 160 folios, with full vowelization and marginal notes. 2) A copy dated 745 AH from the British Library, with partial vowelization. 3) A copy dated 768 AH from the British Library, read to Imam Shams al-Din ibn al-Sa'igh, a prominent Hanafi jurist, and read by Qutlubugha al-Hanafi. The description includes physical details (folios, lines per page, words per line), condition (vowelization, handwriting clarity), and provenance (where preserved, who read it, notes at the end). This information is crucial for textual criticism and understanding the transmission of the Hanafi legal text.

Key Terms
اللباب (al-Lubab): A commentary (sharh) on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar in Hanafi fiqh by Abdul Ghani al-Maydani.
المختصر (al-Mukhtasar): The base text (matn) being commented upon, i.e., al-Quduri's Mukhtasar.
ضبط بالشكل (dabt bi al-shakl): Fully vowelized with diacritical marks indicating short vowels.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

D) It shows the manuscript was used as a master copy for printing.

Key Takeaway
Manuscript descriptions are not mere trivia — they are evidence of the chain of transmission (isnad) for the text itself.

Manuscript Verification of Al-Lubab: A Window into Hanafi Textual Transmission
Manuscript description of Al-Lubab with colophons

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two key manuscripts of Al-Lubab and evaluate their reliability for textual criticism.

Core Idea
Manuscript provenance and scribal notes are essential for establishing the authentic transmission of Hanafi fiqh texts.

This lesson introduces the manuscript tradition of Al-Lubab, a commentary on Al-Quduri. Understanding how manuscripts were copied, collated, and preserved helps us assess the reliability of the fiqh text we study. The two manuscripts described here, from Istanbul and Riyadh, offer insights into the care taken by Hanafi scholars.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Manuscripts
Locate the basic details: year, location, number of folios, lines per page, and words per line for each manuscript.
Use the colophons and descriptions in the passage.
2
Examine the Colophons
Read the colophons carefully for information about the scribe, date, and any prayers or notes. These provide provenance clues.
The colophons include the scribe's name and a plea for forgiveness.
3
Assess Physical Features
Note the vocalization, handwriting clarity, and marginal comments. These affect readability and accuracy.
The 840 AH manuscript is described as 'excellent, fully vocalized, very clear handwriting'.
4
Evaluate Reliability
Combine the clues: earlier date does not automatically mean more reliable; scribal care and exemplar quality matter. Compare both manuscripts.
The 847 AH manuscript has marginal notes clarifying the text.
5
Understand Importance
Recognize how manuscript study supports textual criticism, which is vital for authentic fiqh transmission.
A corrupted manuscript can lead to incorrect rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الثاني: دراسة عن اللباب

عصره، ووحيد دهره الشيخ شمس الدين محمد بن الصايغ
الحنفي، عفا الله عنهما، يوم الجمعة الثامن عشر من جمادى الآخرة،
عام ثمانية وستين وسبعمائة بجامع الحاكم، والقاري قطلوبغا بن كراي الحنفي، عامله الله بلطفه الخفي، وصلى الله على سيدنا محمد وعلى آله وصحبه وسلم.

وكتب أيضاً في زاوية خاتمة النسخة: «ووافق الفراغ من قراءة جميعه على الشيخ الإمام القدوة قطلوبغا بن كراي، والقاري هو المعلافي - هكذا ـ الحنفي، عامله الله بلطفه الخفي، لخمس بقين...».

ثم جاء في الصفحة التي تلي آخر النسخة ما يلي:
تم الكتاب بحمد الله وعونه وحسن توفيقه، وقوبل، وضبط، والحمد لله، وصلى الله على سيدنا محمد، وآله وصحبه الطيبين الطاهرين، وسلم تسليماً كثيراً، والحمد لله رب العالمين حمداً كثيراً.

- نسخة (٨٤٠هـ)، وأصل هذه النسخة محفوظ في المكتبة السليمانية في اسطنبول، في قسم (لا) له لي)، برقم (١١٣٥)، وتقع في (۱۸۰) ورقة، وفي كل صفحة (١٥) سطراً، وفي كل سطر (۱۰) كلمات. وهي نسخة ممتازة مضبوطة بالشكل في كلماتها كلها، وخطها واضح جداً. وقد جاء في آخرها: «نجز الكتاب بحمد الله وعونه بالقاهرة المحروسة، وكتب في أيام متفرقة من سنة أربعين وثمان مائة. وكتبته بحسب الطاقة والجهد في الإيضاح، مع أني عاجز، وعن بري القلم أيضاً لعاجز، فاعف اللهم عن كاتبه ومالكه وقاريه وسامعه والمسلمين أجمعين، وارحم من توفي منهم، واغفر لهم بفضلك، وارحم من بقي منهم بالتوفيق، وحسن الخاتمة برحمتك يا أرحم الراحمين، والحمد لله وحده وصلى الله وسلم على سيدنا محمد خاتم النبيين وعلى آله وصحبه أجمعين، وسلام على المرسلين والحمد لله رب العالمين آمين.»

- نسخة (٨٤٧هـ)، وأصل هذه النسخة محفوظ في مركز الملك فيصل الخيري بالرياض، وتقع في (۱۰۸) ورقة، وفي كل صفحة (١٥) سطراً، وفي كل سطر (١٤) كلمة. وهي نسخة جيدة، خطها واضح جداً، وغالب كلماتها مضبوطة بالشكل، وعلى حواشيها بعض التعليقات المتعلقة بإيضاح نص القدوري. وقد جاء في آخرها: «وقع الفراغ من نسخة الكتاب القدوري في يوم السبت، آخر يوم من شهر السفر - هكذا ـ من شهور سنة سبع وأربعين وثمان مائة كتبه العبد الفقير الراجي عفو ربه اللطيف حسن ابن خليل بن علي بك غفر الله له ولوالديه، وأحسن إليهما وإليه ولجميع المسلمين والمسلمات والمؤمنين والمؤمنات الأحياء منهم والأموات ولمن قال آمين وصلى الله على سيدنا محمد وعلى آله وصحبه أجمعين، والحمد لله رب العالمين.»
Chapter Two: Study of Al-Lubab. ... His contemporary, the unique of his age, Sheikh Shams al-Din Muhammad ibn al-Sa'igh al-Hanafi, may Allah forgive them, on Friday the 18th of Jumada al-Akhirah, in the year 768 at the Jami' al-Hakim, and the reader Qatlubugha ibn Karay al-Hanafi, may Allah treat him with His hidden grace, and may Allah bless our master Muhammad and his family and companions and grant them peace. And he also wrote in the margin of the copy's colophon: 'The completion of reading all of it upon the Sheikh Imam al-Qudwa Qatlubugha ibn Karay was agreed, and the reader is al-Ma'lawi - thus - al-Hanafi, may Allah treat him with His hidden grace, on the fifth remaining...' Then came on the page following the end of the copy the following: 'The book was completed with the praise of Allah and His help and good success, and it was collated and pointed. Praise be to Allah, and may Allah bless our master Muhammad and his family and his good and pure companions, and grant them abundant peace. Praise be to Allah, Lord of the worlds, abundant praise.' - Copy (840 AH): The original of this copy is preserved in the Suleymaniya Library in Istanbul, in section (??), number (1135), consisting of 180 folios, each page has 15 lines, each line has 10 words. It is an excellent copy, fully vocalized, with very clear handwriting. At its end: 'The book was completed with the praise of Allah and His help in Cairo the protected, and it was written on separate days of the year 840. I wrote it to the best of my ability and effort in clarification, though I am incapable, and also incapable of trimming the pen. So forgive, O Allah, its writer, owner, reader, listener, and all Muslims. Have mercy on those who have died among them, forgive them by Your grace, and have mercy on those who remain by granting success and a good end. By Your mercy, O Most Merciful of the merciful. Praise be to Allah alone, and may Allah bless and grant peace to our master Muhammad, the seal of the prophets, and to all his family and companions. Peace be upon the messengers. Praise be to Allah, Lord of the worlds. Amen.' - Copy (847 AH): The original of this copy is preserved in the King Faisal Charitable Center in Riyadh. It consists of 108 folios, each page has 15 lines, each line has 14 words. It is a good copy, with very clear handwriting, most of its words are vocalized, and on its margins are some comments related to clarifying the text of al-Quduri. At its end: 'The copying of the book al-Quduri was completed on Saturday, the last day of the month of Safar - thus - of the year 847. Written by the poor servant hoping for the pardon of his gentle Lord, Hasan ibn Khalil ibn Ali Beg, may Allah forgive him and his parents, and be good to them and to him and to all Muslim men and women, believers and believers, the living and the dead, and to those who say Amen. May Allah bless our master Muhammad and all his family and companions. Praise be to Allah, Lord of the worlds.'
Source pages p. 179

Commentary
This passage is a manuscript description and study of the book Al-Lubab (a commentary on Al-Quduri). It provides details about two important manuscripts. The first manuscript (840 AH) is kept in Istanbul's Suleymaniya Library and is described as excellent, fully vocalized, and clearly written. Its colophon includes a prayer by the scribe. The second manuscript (847 AH) is in Riyadh at the King Faisal Center; it is also clear and has marginal notes explaining the text of Al-Quduri. Both manuscripts were copied by different scribes, and the passage records their colophons. This information is valuable for textual criticism and establishing the reliability of the transmitted text.

Key Terms
اللباب (al-Lubab): The title of the commentary on Al-Quduri by Al-Maidani, meaning 'The Core' or 'The Essence'.
القدوري (al-Quduri): The author of the matn (Mukhtasar al-Quduri), a foundational Hanafi fiqh text.
نسخة (nuskhah): A manuscript copy of the book.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Manuscript description provides vital clues for textual criticism, which is necessary for accurate transmission of Hanafi fiqh.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner

The Manuscript Tradition of al-Lubab and Mukhtasar al-Quduri
Describes a manuscript colophon and the availability of copies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the significance of manuscript colophons and explain how the abundance of copies attests to the wide acceptance of a Hanafi matn.

Core Idea
Manuscript copies preserve the transmission chain and attest to the enduring authority of a text.

This passage from the introduction to an edition of al-Lubab describes the manuscript basis for the text. It includes a colophon from a copy completed in 980 AH and notes that dozens of ordinary copies of Mukhtasar al-Quduri exist, indicating its widespread use. Understanding the manuscript tradition helps us appreciate the reliability and diffusion of Hanafi fiqh texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the colophon details
Locate the date (12 Safar 980 AH) and the scribe (Ahmad ibn Shaykh Muhammad al-Imam). Note the place ('Ajlun) and the prayer for forgiveness. This gives a concrete example of a manuscript's provenance.
The colophon shows that even a relatively late manuscript (16th century CE) still records transmission details.
2
Note the libraries mentioned
The author lists sources: Haram Library (Mecca), Mahmudiyya Library, and 'Arif Hikmat Library (Medina), now in King Abdulaziz Library. This shows the geographic spread of manuscripts.
3
Interpret the phrase 'ordinary copies'
The author distinguishes between described copies (nine) and ordinary ones. 'Ordinary' means lacking special features like illuminations or rare annotations, but still textually important.
Even ordinary copies are valuable for establishing the text.
4
Understand the purpose of the illustrated examples
The images are samples from both al-Lubab and Mukhtasar al-Quduri, not just one book. They serve as evidence of the manuscript tradition.

الفصل الثاني : دراسة عن اللباب
وقد جاء في آخر هذه النسخة : وافق الفراغ من كتابته في ثاني عشر شهر صفر المظفر من شهور سنة ثمانين وتسع مائة من الهجرة النبوية على صاحبها أفضل الصلاة والسلام، على يد العبد الفقير إلى ربه الملك الكريم: الغلام أحمد بن شيخ محمد الإمام ثم الخطيب بجامع مدينة عجلون، سبط نور الدين الشهيد غفر الله تعالى له ولوالديه ولجميع المسلمين والمسلمات بمنه وكرمه.
آمين». اهـ
وهكذا بين يدي عشرات من نسخ خطية من مختصر القدوري، عادية ليس لها مزايا، مما يسره الله لي من مخطوطات مكتبة الحــرم المكي بمكة المكرمة، ومن مخطوطات المكتبة المحمودية، وعارف حكمت بالمدينة المنورة، المودعة في مكتبة الملك عبد العزيز، وقد اكتفيت بوصف النسخ التسع السابقة الذكر، وإلا فالأمر يطول جـداً، والحمد لله رب العالمين

مصورة من نُسَخ اللباب
Chapter Two: Study of al-Lubab. It has come at the end of this copy: The completion of its writing was on the twelfth of the month of Safar al-Muzaffar of the year nine hundred and eighty of the Prophetic Hijra, may the best prayers and peace be upon its owner, at the hand of the poor slave of his Lord, the Generous King: the boy Ahmad ibn Shaykh Muhammad al-Imam, then the khatib at the mosque of the city of 'Ajlun, grandson of Nur al-Din al-Shahid, may Allah forgive him and his parents and all Muslim men and women by His grace and generosity. Amen. So it ends. Likewise, there are dozens of ordinary manuscript copies of Mukhtasar al-Quduri that have no special features, which Allah facilitated for me from the manuscripts of the Haram Library in Mecca, and from the manuscripts of the Mahmudiyya Library and 'Arif Hikmat in Medina, deposited in the King Abdulaziz Library. I have sufficed with describing the nine copies mentioned before, otherwise the matter would become very lengthy. Praise be to Allah, Lord of the worlds. Below are illustrated examples of what has been mentioned and described of the copies of al-Lubab and Mukhtasar al-Quduri. The generous reader may find them many, but that is due to the abundance of copies. Also, they are examples of two books, not one. Illustrated examples from copies of al-Lubab.
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage is a front-matter section describing the manuscript tradition of al-Lubab and Mukhtasar al-Quduri. The author first presents a colophon from a particular manuscript, stating that it was completed on 12 Safar 980 AH (approximately June 1572 CE) by a scribe named Ahmad ibn Shaykh Muhammad al-Imam, who was the khatib of the mosque in 'Ajlun and grandson of Nur al-Din al-Shahid. The author then notes that he has access to dozens of ordinary manuscript copies of Mukhtasar al-Quduri from various libraries, including the Haram Library in Mecca, and the Mahmudiyya and 'Arif Hikmat libraries in Medina (now housed in the King Abdulaziz Library). He learned from describing only nine of them for brevity. Finally, he indicates that the following images are examples from copies of both al-Lubab and Mukhtasar al-Quduri.

Key Terms
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): A foundational Hanafi fiqh text by Abu al-Hasan Ahmad al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), widely used as a matn for beginners.
اللباب (al-Lubab): A commentary (sharh) on Mukhtasar al-Quduri by 'Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani (d. 1298 AH), explaining its rulings.
النسخة الخطية (al-nuskha al-khattiyya): A handwritten manuscript copy of a text.
التفرغ من كتابته (al-faragh min kitabatihi): The completion of copying the manuscript.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The abundance of manuscript copies of Mukhtasar al-Quduri across major libraries attests to its wide acceptance and reliable transmission, confirming its authority as a foundational Hanafi text.

Introduction and Front Matter

Understanding the Author's Introduction: Purpose and Definitions
Opening of commentary with praise and chapter heading

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the purpose of the author's introduction and explain the etymological definitions of 'kitab' and 'taharah' as given in the text.

Core Idea
The author's introduction sets the stage by defining key terms and showing humility, reminding us that fiqh texts are a legacy of scholarship.

This passage is from the opening of al-Lubab, a commentary on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar. The author, Abd al-Latif al-Maidani, explains his method: he compiled a concise commentary for easy study. He also defines the terms 'kitab' (book) and 'taharah' (purification) etymologically. This introductory material is not part of the fiqh rulings themselves but prepares the reader for the systematic study that follows.

Guided Path
1
Identify the purpose of the introduction
Recognize that the author begins with praise and blessings, then explains his compilation method. This shows the intention behind the commentary.
The author mentions 'جمعته بالفاظ مختصرة' (I compiled it with concise expressions).
2
Understand the definition of 'kitab'
The author defines 'kitab' linguistically as 'the thing' and derives it from 'kitabah' (writing), meaning a collection of letters.
This is a standard linguistic definition, not a legal one.
3
Understand the definition of 'taharah'
The author states that 'taharah' linguistically means cleanliness (al-niqayah). This is the starting point for the chapter on purification.
The fiqh rulings on taharah follow this introduction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والصلاة والسلام على رسول الله انبياء الله و ملائكة الله مور من الصحابة أو ليا مالي شرح المختصر القدوري جمعته بالفاظ مختصرة. المذاكرة ، لوضعته لذوى الاتهام القاصرة اسكنت في ذلك عنه الحمد في الأول . قال الشيخ الامام أبو الحسن رحمه الله تعالى كتاب الطهارة كم بيت الشيء أي جمعته ومنه الكتابة وهي جمع الحروف العبد الفقير الحمان ، عبد التي التنمي الميداني . غفرا المبارك للإماع القدورى . قد شاعت بركته حتى صارت نرجوا على تعلمه وتعليمه وكنت ممن مكف عليه الأيام الكثيرة قد خفيت في معادنها . ويش لطاقه قد استرات في سيارات تكون كالشرح اليه . التفصيل بحمله وحيد يكون معينا لمانيه . الا انه كان يمنعني أنى لست من هذا المقام، رجاء الانتساب بالخدمة لذات الامام الطهارة لنة التقانة اب دارستان جهه الكريم . وموجبا للفوز بجنات ) كتابة والبسملة اعتداء واليك الاقتداء بالكتاب المكرم والي المعلم . سم الله الرحمن الرحيم
And prayers and peace be upon the Messenger of Allah, the prophets of Allah and the angels of Allah... from the companions or friends of the one who commented on al-Mukhtasar of al-Quduri. I compiled it with brief expressions. The study, I placed it for those with limited understanding. I settled on that instead of praise at the beginning. The Shaykh, al-Imam Abu al-Hasan, may Allah have mercy on him, said: Kitab al-Taharah. 'Kitab' means the thing, i.e., I compiled it, and from it is 'kitabah' which is the collecting of letters. The poor slave of Allah, Abd al-Latif al-Tanmi al-Maidani... the blessing of the Imam al-Quduri has spread so that we hope for learning and teaching it. I was among those who spent many days on it; its subtleties were hidden in their depths... but he prevented me because I am not of this status, hoping for affiliation through service to the Imam. Taharah: linguistically, cleanliness... and the cause for winning gardens. Writing and Basmalah... following the honorable book and the teacher. In the name of Allah, the Most Merciful, the Most Gracious.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage is the opening of the author's introduction to al-Lubab, a commentary on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar. The author, Abd al-Latif al-Maidani, begins by praising Allah and sending blessings upon the prophets and angels, then mentions his compilation of a concise commentary. He explains that he wrote it for easy study, addressing those with limited capacity. He quotes the original matn author, al-Quduri, who said 'Kitab al-Taharah'. The author then defines 'kitab' etymologically as a collection of things, linking it to 'kitabah' (writing). He expresses humility about his status and hopes for acceptance. The passage concludes with the beginning of the chapter on purification, stating that 'taharah' linguistically means cleanliness. This is typical front matter in a sharh work, setting the stage for the fiqh rulings that follow.

Key Terms
كتاب (kitab): The author explains that 'kitab' means 'the thing' and is derived from 'kitabah' (writing), which is the collection of letters.
الطهارة (al-taharah): Linguistically, cleanliness (النقاء). This is the opening of the fiqh chapter.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Introduction and Front Matter

Introduction to Al-Lubab: Purpose and Beginning of Taharah
Author's preface and start of matn on taharah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the author's purpose in writing al-Lubab and identify the beginning of the chapter on purification.

Core Idea
Al-Lubab is a concise Hanafi commentary on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar for learners with limited understanding.

This passage introduces the commentary 'al-Lubab' by al-Maydani on the foundational Hanafi text 'al-Mukhtasar al-Quduri'. The author explains he compiled it in concise words for study, intending it for those of limited understanding. The text then opens 'Kitab al-Taharah' (The Book of Purification), setting the stage for the fiqh rulings on purification. Understanding this introduction helps students appreciate the pedagogical purpose of the work.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Author and His Work
The author is al-Maydani, who wrote 'al-Lubab' as a commentary on 'al-Mukhtasar al-Quduri' by Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Quduri. Recognize that this is a Hanafi fiqh commentary.
Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar is a standard matn in the Hanafi school.
2
Understand the Author's Purpose
Al-Maydani states he compiled the commentary in concise words for study, placing it for those of limited understanding. This indicates the work is meant as an accessible learning tool.
The phrase 'لذوي الأفهام القاصرة' means 'for those of limited understanding', emphasizing its pedagogical aim.
3
Recognize the Beginning of the Matn
The passage includes 'Kitab al-Taharah' (The Book of Purification), which is the first chapter of the Mukhtasar. This signals the start of the substantive fiqh content.
Taharah is the first topic because it is a prerequisite for prayer.
4
Note the Linguistic Definition of Taharah
Although the text is corrupted, it attempts to give the linguistic meaning of 'taharah'. In Hanafi fiqh, taharah means purification from ritual impurity (hadath) and physical impurity (najasah).
The full definition will be clarified in subsequent lessons.

Source Text

والصلاة والسلام على رسول الله
أنبياء الله وملائكة الله، ومن [؟] الصحابة أولي [؟].
شرح المختصر القدوري جمعته بألفاظ مختصرة للمذاكرة، وضعته لذوي الأفهام القاصرة.
أسكنت في ذلك عنه الحمد في الأول.

كتاب الطهارة
الطهارة لغة التقانة [؟]
العبد الفقير الحمان، عبد التي التنمي الميداني. غفرا المبارك للإماع القدورى. قد شاعت بركته حتى صارت نرجوا على تعلمه وتعليمه وكنت ممن مكف عليه الأيام الكثيرة قد خفيت في معادنها . ويش لطاقه قد استرات في سيارات تكون كالشرح اليه . التفصيل بحمله وحيد يكون معينا لمانيه . الا انه كان يمنعني أنى لست من هذا المقام، رجاء الانتساب بالخدمة لذات الامام

Commentary
This passage is the author's introduction to the commentary 'al-Lubab' by al-Maydani on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar. It begins with the basmalah and praise, then the author states his purpose: to compile a concise commentary for learners with limited capacity. The text then cites the matn: 'Kitab al-Taharah' (The Book of Purification) attributed to the Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Quduri. There is a fragment about the linguistic meaning of 'taharah' which is unclear due to OCR corruption. The author identifies himself as the poor servant, al-Maydani, and expresses hope for the blessing of this work. The passage sets the stage for the fiqh rulings on purification that follow.

Key Terms
الطهارة (al-taharah): The legal purification from ritual impurity, both from hadath and najasah.
المختصر القدوري (al-Mukhtasar al-Quduri): A foundational Hanafi fiqh text by Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Quduri.
اللباب (al-Lubab): Title of this commentary meaning 'the core' or 'the essence'.

The Author's Preface: Humility and Method in Hanafi Scholarship
Author explains his motivation and method for writing this commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the purpose and key elements of a classical Hanafi fiqh preface, and explain how the author's stated methodology reflects scholarly tradition.

Core Idea
A scholar's preface reveals his methodology, his reliance on Allah, and his chain of authority.

The opening pages of a classical fiqh textbook are never casual. They establish the author's authority, his humility before Allah, and his methodological approach. In this garbled but important passage from al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri, we glimpse how a Hanafi commentator introduces his work, seeking blessing and acknowledging his debts—a model of scholarly adab that shapes how the work should be received.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the classical preface formula
Identify the phrase 'أما بعد' (ammā ba‘d) which marks the transition from the basmalah and hamdalah to the main content. This is a standard feature of Islamic scholarly writing.
2
Analyze the author's self-deprecation and dua
Note how the author (May Allah forgive him, his parents, his teachers) humbly acknowledges his limitations. This is a common trope but carries legal weight: it signals that the author is not claiming infallibility, only transmitting with care.
Hanafi fuqaha often begin with prayers for themselves and their teachers to emphasize the chain of transmission (sanad).
3
Identify the methodological statement
The author mentions consulting Qasim's book 'al-Tashih' and choosing the more apparent (azhar) and clearer (awḍah) expressions from the choices of the leading imams. This indicates a tarjih methodology based on preferring the stronger or more widely accepted position.
4
Interpret the purpose: revealing hidden gems
The author states that 'some of its gems are hidden in their mines,' meaning the original text (al-Quduri) contains subtle legal points that need clarification. His commentary aims to make these accessible.
This reflects the Hanafi tradition of sharh (commentary) as an act of explaining, not creating new law.
5
Appreciate the basmalah and seeking blessing
The author begins with the basmalah following the Prophet's example and seeks blessing for continued benefit. This is not mere ritual: it frames the work as an act of worship (ibadah) and a trust (amanah).
Hanafi scholars often open works with basmalah to invoke divine aid (tawfiq) and to signal that the knowledge is for Allah's sake.

To proceed: He said - may Allah forgive him, his parents, his teachers, and those who have a right over him... and its blessing so that it became like necessary knowledge. So I devoted myself to learning and teaching it. I was among those who devoted many days to it and persisted... Then I saw some of its gems hidden in their mines, and some of the obedience... And often he would like me to compile some expressions as a commentary for it, with clarification, so that it helps in understanding its meanings. This is the matter, and I have a short reach in this field. Then my audacity to enter this... seeking its blessing and as a good omen in serving it, so I sought guidance from Allah: with addition of what is likely needed. And he investigated Qasim in his book al-Tashih from the choices of the leading imams, and investigated what is more apparent and clearer in expression... because it is named when the companions mention. I ask Allah Almighty... and to make me among the righteous for His noble face, and a means to win the gardens. And the author, may Allah have mercy on him, began his book with the basmalah following the Prophet صلى الله عليه وسلم and hoping for blessing in his book through continued benefit from it.
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage is the author's preface (front matter) to his commentary 'al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri'. He begins by humbly acknowledging his own shortcomings and the difficulty of the task. He states that despite the blessing and fame of the original text (al-Quduri), some of its pearls are hidden and need elucidation. He admits his limited ability but expresses courage through reliance on Allah and seeks to compile explanatory notes. He mentions consulting Qasim's book 'al-Tashih' for authoritative choices. The author then mentions beginning the work with the basmalah following the Prophet's example. The text is heavily corrupted in OCR, but the general tone of humility and scholarly dedication is evident.

Key Terms
أما بعد (ammā ba‘d): A transitional phrase meaning 'to proceed' or 'now then', used to move from the opening praise to the main text.
الظاهر والأوضح (al-azhar wa al-awḍah): The most apparent and clearest positions, used by the author to indicate his preference in cases of disagreement.
التصحيح (al-tashih): A book by Qasim (probably Qasim ibn Qutlugh) that verified and selected authoritative rulings.

Key Takeaway
A Hanafi author's preface reveals his chain of authority, his methodology (tarjih), and his humble reliance on Allah—essential for understanding the legal weight of the commentary.

Introduction to Mukhtasar al-Quduri and Its Author
Colophon and biography of the author

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the author of Mukhtasar al-Quduri and explain the significance of the colophon in Hanafi textual transmission.

Core Idea
The Mukhtasar al-Quduri is a foundational Hanafi matn; its colophon ties the commentary to the original work across centuries.

This lesson explores a colophon and biography from al-Maidani's commentary al-Lubab. You will learn about Imam al-Quduri, the author of the Mukhtasar, and the scholarly context in which the commentary was completed. Understanding these details helps appreciate the chain of transmission in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scholars
Read the colophon and biography. Note that the text mentions 'its author' (the commentator al-Maidani) and then 'the author of the book' (al-Quduri). Distinguish between these two figures.
Al-Maidani wrote al-Lubab; al-Quduri wrote the original Mukhtasar.
2
Extract the completion date
Find the date mentioned in the colophon: 13 Ramadan 1266 AH. Convert if needed and note its significance for the commentary's provenance.
This date is equivalent to around 1850 CE, showing the commentary is relatively recent.
3
Review al-Quduri's biography
From the biography, note al-Quduri's full name, birth year (362 AH/973 CE), death year (428 AH/1037 CE), and his city (Baghdad). Understand his stature in the Hanafi school.
Al-Quduri was a leading Hanafi jurist; his Mukhtasar is a key beginner text.
4
Understand the purpose of a colophon
A colophon typically records the completion of a manuscript, including date, author, and prayers. It provides authenticity and historical context.
Colophons are crucial for textual criticism and understanding transmission.
5
Connect to the Hanafi tradition
Reflect on how this colophon links al-Maidani's commentary to al-Quduri's matn, illustrating the continuity of Hanafi scholarship from Baghdad to Damascus (al-Maidani was from Damascus).

Seven Categories of Mujtahids According to Ibn Kamal Pasha
Classification of mujtahids into seven categories

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the first two levels of mujtahids in Ibn Kamal's classification and distinguish between a mujtahid mutlaq and a mujtahid fi al-madhhab.

Core Idea
Ijtihad has levels: absolute mujtahids found schools; later mujtahids work within a school.

This lesson introduces a classical Hanafi classification of jurists into seven categories by the Ottoman scholar Ibn Kamal Pasha. The classification helps understand the hierarchy of authority in fiqh and the different capacities of ijtihad. The source text preserves the first two categories clearly, defining the absolute mujtahids (like the four imams) and the mujtahids within the madhhab (like Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani).

Guided Path
1
Recognize the Author and Work
Ibn Kamal Pasha (also known as Kemalpaşazade) was a prominent Ottoman Hanafi scholar. His treatise 'Taj al-Tarajim' classifies jurists into seven categories. Understanding the author's stature helps contextualize the classification.
Ibn Kamal is a muta'akhkhir (later) authority; his taxonomy is widely cited in Hanafi usul.
2
Identify the First Category
The first category is 'mujtahidun fi al-shar'' – absolute mujtahids who establish usul and derive rulings directly from the Qur'an, Sunnah, and Ijma without taqlid. These include the four imams (Abu Hanifa, Malik, Shafi'i, Ahmad) and those who follow their path.
They are independent in both usul and furu'.
3
Identify the Second Category
The second category includes mujtahids like Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani – they are capable of deriving rulings from evidences but operate within the usul established by their imam (Abu Hanifa). They are 'mujtahid fi al-madhhab'.
Their ijtihad is confined to the madhhab's principles.
4
Note the Remaining Categories
Ibn Kamal mentions five more categories (third to seventh), but the text is corrupted and incomplete. These typically include levels such as as'hab al-takhrij, as'hab al-tarjih, and muqallids. Recognize that a full classification exists in reliable sources.
For a complete list, refer to Ibn Kamal's original treatise or later summaries like Ibn Abidin's Radd al-Muhtar.
5
Memorize the Key Distinction
The essential distinction is between an absolute mujtahid (who creates a school) and a mujtahid within a school (who follows its usul). This hierarchy ensures that later jurists operate within the bounds of the established madhhab.
This distinction is crucial for understanding taqlid and ijtihad in Hanafi jurisprudence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نقل من تاج التراجم } بيان طبقات المجتهدين والفقهاء قدس الله تعالى أرواحهم رحمة رب الملك الا على نقله الفقير حين الطبع ) بالاختصار لا نتفاع طالب العلم والاعتبار } يقول العلامة المحقق في جميع الحال المولى أحمد المفتى المشهور باين الكمال أسكنه الله جنته في رسالته ان الفقهاء على سبع طبقات (الاولى) طبقة المجتهدين في الشرع كالائمة الاربعة ومن سلك مسلكهم تأسيس قواعد الاصول واستنباط أحكام الفروع من الادلة الاربعة الكتاب والسنة والاجماع ب تلك القواعد من غير تقليد لا حد لا في الفروع ولا فى الاصول (الثانية) طبقة المجتهدين كاني يوسف ومحمد وسائر أصحاب أبي حنيفة القادرين على استخراج الاحكام عن الادلة . المستفيدين بية الفاضل / . ستطاب . السلطان بن السلط خان بسبب والاختصار ولم يرض تلف الحالي معلمة مشكورا والجرة مؤقورا- اما لانجاز الوعد بطبقة فى من الاهتمام واعقد التام وناداك الايمن
Transferred from Taj al-Tarajim: Clarification of the categories of mujtahids and jurists, may Allah sanctify their souls, the mercy of the Lord of the Kingdom. The poor one transferred it at the time of printing with abbreviation for the benefit of the student of knowledge and consideration. The all-knowing investigator in every state, the master Ahmad, the mufti known as Ibn Kamal, may Allah give him a place in His Paradise, says in his treatise: The jurists are of seven categories. (First) The category of the mujtahids in the Shariah, like the four imams and those who followed their path, establishing the principles of usul and deriving rulings of the branches from the four evidences: the Book, the Sunnah, and Ijma, with those principles, without taqlid of anyone, neither in branches nor in principles. (Second) The category of the mujtahids like Abu Yusuf and Muhammad and the rest of the companions of Abu Hanifa, capable of deriving rulings from the evidences... [corrupted text continues]
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This passage is a classification of jurists (fuqaha) according to Ibn Kamal Pasha (also known as Ibn Kamal, a prominent Ottoman Hanafi scholar). It is taken from his work 'Taj al-Tarajim'. He divides jurists into seven categories. Only the first two are detailed here. The first category is the absolute mujtahids in Shariah, like the four imams (Abu Hanifa, Malik, Shafi'i, Ahmad). They established the principles of usul (legal theory) and derived rulings from the primary sources without following anyone. The second category are mujtahids within the madhhab, like Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. They could derive rulings but followed the usul of their imam (Abu Hanifa). The remaining categories (third to seventh) are not given due to corruption or abridgement. This classification helps students understand the hierarchy of authority in fiqh. The first two categories correspond to 'mujtahid mutlaq' and 'mujtahid fi al-madhhab' in later terminology.

Key Terms
مجتهد في الشرع (mujtahid fi al-shar'): An absolute mujtahid who derives rulings from primary sources without following any imam.
مجتهد (mujtahid): A jurist capable of performing ijtihad (independent reasoning). Ibn Kamal defines several levels.
طبقة (tabaqa): A level or category in the classification of scholars.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Kamal's classification, which category includes Imam Abu Hanifa?
A) First category (mujtahidun fi al-shar')
B) Second category (mujtahidun like Abu Yusuf)
C) Third category (mujtahidun fi al-madhhab)
D) Fourth category (as'hab al-takhrij)

Key Takeaway
Ibn Kamal's classification reminds us that ijtihad has degrees, and even within a madhhab, later scholars are qualified to perform ijtihad within established principles.

Introduction to Al-Lubab: Purpose and Structure
Preface discussing the purpose and structure of the study

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the purpose and structure of the study of Al-Lubab and identify its place in the Hanafi tradition.

Core Idea
Al-Lubab is a concise commentary on Al-Quduri, essential for Hanafi fiqh study.

This lesson introduces the second chapter of a study on Al-Lubab, a foundational Hanafi work. The author explains his motivation to provide a concise yet thorough explanation of Al-Quduri for students. Understanding the purpose of this text helps you appreciate its structure and utility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the text being introduced
Recognize that Al-Lubab is a commentary (sharh) on the matn Al-Quduri, a foundational Hanafi fiqh manual.
Al-Lubab means 'the core' – it aims to extract the essence of Al-Quduri.
2
Understand the author's motivation
The author wanted to be concise (ikhtisar) yet provide sufficient explanation (tafsil) so that students with limited background could benefit.
This balance between brevity and clarity is a hallmark of good Hanafi educational texts.
3
Recognize the target audience
The text is directed at learners who are 'short of reach' (qasir al-ba') – new students of fiqh.
Such students needed a commentary that was not overwhelming.
4
Note the manuscript sources
The editor used two manuscript copies (A) to establish the text, indicating scholarly care.
This is common in critical editions of classical works.

The Purpose and Humility of a Sharh: Al-Maydani's Introduction
Author explains his motivation for writing this commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why al-Maydani wrote his commentary and identify the key literary features of a Hanafi sharh introduction.

Core Idea
A sharh is written out of service to knowledge, not personal pride.

Al-Maydani opens his commentary with a classic Islamic preamble: praise to Allah, blessings on the Prophet, and a humble self-introduction. He then explains his reason for writing: the widespread benefit of al-Quduri's matn and his desire to clarify its hidden gems. This introduction sets the tone for the entire sharh, emphasizing service to the Hanafi tradition over personal acclaim.

Guided Path
1
Analyze the preamble
Read the opening lines from 'Bismillah' to 'amma ba'd'. Note the elements: praise, blessings, and the author's self-description. What does this reveal about the author's character and purpose?
Classical sharh introductions typically begin with hamdalah and salawat.
2
Identify the author's motivation
Al-Maydani states he saw that some of al-Quduri's 'gems were hidden'. What does he mean by this? Why did he feel compelled to write a commentary?
He felt the matn needed further elaboration for students.
3
Examine the author's humility
Al-Maydani admits he is 'not among the people of this field' and has a 'short reach'. How does this humility serve the purpose of the sharh?
Such humility is a standard trope, but it underscores the seriousness of the task.
4
Connect to the sharh genre
What does al-Maydani aim to do in his commentary? He mentions detailing summaries, restricting absolutes, and clarifying meanings. How does this define the role of a sharh?
A sharh explicates, restricts, and clarifies the matn.

And prayers and peace be upon our master Muhammad, the trustworthy, sent as a mercy to the worlds, and upon all the prophets and messengers, and upon his family, the Companions, the relatives, the followers, the righteous scholars, the mujtahid imams, and those who follow them in righteousness until the Day of Judgment. I was among those who devoted many days to it and persisted in returning to it until I became familiar with it. Then I saw that some of its gems were hidden in their mines and some of its finer points had settled in their places. I often felt impelled to compile some expressions that would serve as a commentary to detail its summarized parts, restrict its absolute statements, and clarify its meanings in a moderate way with explanation, so that it would help understanding its meanings. But I was prevented by the fact that I am not among the people of this field and have a short reach in this arena. Then [something] drove me to venture into this endeavor by virtue of affiliation through service to that imamate.

Commentary
This passage is the author's introduction to his commentary on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar. Al-Maydani praises Allah and sends blessings, then introduces himself humbly. He notes the widespread acceptance of al-Quduri's matn among students and scholars. He explains that he undertook writing this sharh because he noticed some subtle points in the matn that needed clarification. He aimed to detail what is summarized, restrict the absolute, and clarify meanings in a balanced way. He also admits his initial hesitation due to feeling unqualified, but he was motivated by a desire to serve the Hanafi school (the imamate).

Key Terms
القدوري (al-Quduri): The author of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, a foundational Hanafi fiqh matn.
شرح (sharh): A commentary that explains and expands upon a base text (matn).
متن (matn): The base text being commented upon.
الخدمة (al-khidmah): Service; al-Maydani calls his work a service to the Hanafi madhhab.

Al-Lubab is a commentary unlocking hidden gems in Mukhtasar al-Quduri.

In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. Praise be to Allah who guides whomever He wills to understanding religion, and by His grace leads whomever He wishes to the path of the guided. Therefore, students have devoted themselves to understanding and teaching it, and I was among those who studied it for many days and kept returning to it until I internalized it. I saw that some of its gems were hidden in their mines, and some subtleties had settled in their places. It often occurred to me to write a commentary on it, gathering statements that would serve as an explanation, detailing its summaries, qualifying its absolutes, and clarifying its meanings in a moderate yet clear manner, so that it would be helpful for understanding. However, I refrained because I considered myself unworthy of this task and short of ability in this field. Nothing prompted me to enter this arena except hope of being associated with the service of that Imam.

This preface sets the tone for the entire commentary, emphasizing its purpose of making al-Quduri's text accessible.

مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): A seminal Hanafi fiqh manual by Imam Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), widely used as a foundational text for Hanafi jurisprudence.

Introduction to Al-Lubab: The Author's Methodology and the Hanafi Mu'tamad
Author's preface explaining his methodology

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the author's criterion for selecting rulings (mu'tamad) and distinguish it from other Hanafi positions.

Core Idea
This commentary prioritizes the mu'tamad (relied-upon) position of the Hanafi school, which is the basis for fatwa.

When studying a classical fiqh text, it is essential to know which positions are authoritative for practice. In this introduction, the author Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani explains his methodology: he sets out to compile a commentary on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar, focusing on the mu'tamad (relied-upon) rulings of the Hanafi school. Understanding this will help you navigate later rulings and recognise the hierarchy of authority in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's purpose
Read the preface and note why al-Maydani wrote this commentary. He wanted to make al-Quduri's text clearer for students, while also selecting only the most authoritative rulings.
He mentions that he captured hidden 'jewels' from the text.
2
Locate the key methodological statement
Find the phrase where he describes his selection criterion. He writes: 'تحري ما هو المعتمد والفتوى عليه' (I strove for what is the mu'tamad and the position for fatwa). This is the core of his method.
Mu'tamad means the relied-upon ruling; mufta bihi means the ruling used for issuing fatwas.
3
Understand the hierarchy of positions
Al-Maydani explains that he also added preponderant opinions from the imams (الأئمة). This means he sometimes goes beyond the basic mu'tamad to include stronger views from later scholars.
This shows the dynamic nature of Hanafi tarjih.
4
Recognise the authority level of this commentary
Because al-Maydani focuses on mu'tamad and mufta bihi, his work belongs to the 'fatwa literature' category. It is a reliable guide for practice, not just a theoretical discussion.
Students and muftis alike use such works for everyday fiqh.

Commentary
This passage is the author's introduction (muqaddimah) to his commentary, Al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri. Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani begins with praise and salutations, then explains his motivation: the Mukhtasar of al-Quduri is widely studied and considered essential, so students dedicate themselves to it. He himself spent much time on it until he grasped its subtle points. He wanted to produce a commentary that would clarify its meanings in a balanced way, despite his own humility about his qualifications. His method is to compile the words of earlier scholars that indicate their intended meanings, and to focus on the mu'tamad (relied-upon) and mufta bihi positions of the Hanafi school. He also incorporates selected preponderant opinions from the imams. He states that he will follow the original text and begins with the Basmalah, emulating the Quran and the Prophet's practice to seek blessing. This introduction establishes the authority weight of his commentary: he relies on the established Hanafi position, not rare transmissions.

Key Terms
المعتمد (al-mu'tamad): The relied-upon ruling within the Hanafi school, which is the basis for fatwa.
الفتوى (al-fatwa): The legal ruling issued to a questioner; here it refers to the position that is used for giving fatwas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Introduction and Front Matter

The Author's Introduction: Methodology and Purpose of Al-Lubab
Author's preface explaining motivation, method, and naming of Al-Lubab.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the author's motivation, methodology, and naming rationale for Al-Lubab Sharh Al-Quduri.

Core Idea
Al-Lubab is the relied-upon commentary, capturing the Hanafi school's mu'tamad with the preferred choices of the imams.

This lesson examines the preface of Al-Lubab Sharh Al-Quduri by Abd al-Ghani al-Ghanimi al-Maidani. The author explains his humble beginnings, his reverence for Imam al-Quduri's matn, and his decision to write a commentary despite feeling unqualified. He outlines his method: relying on the mu'tamad positions and fatwa, incorporating preferred views from the imams, and naming the work 'Al-Lubab' (The Core) to indicate it contains the essential meanings. This introduction sets the stage for understanding the authority and approach of this key Hanafi text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's self-characterization
The author describes himself as 'al-'abd al-faqir al-jani' and seeks forgiveness. This shows his scholarly humility and awareness of human fallibility.
Such humility is common in Islamic scholarly prefaces and reflects the author's intent to serve the school.
2
Recognize the status of Al-Quduri's matn
The author says it 'shaa wa ishtahara' (became widespread) and is like 'al-'ilm al-daruri' (necessary knowledge). This indicates its central place in Hanafi studies.
Al-Mukhtasar of al-Quduri is a foundational text in the Hanafi school.
3
Trace the author's hesitation and motivation
He felt he was 'laysa min ahl hadha al-shan' (not among the people of this matter) but proceeded clinging to the blessing of association with al-Quduri.
His motivation is service to the school, not personal fame.
4
Extract the author's methodology
He aimed to compile expressions that clarify the matn, rely on 'al-mu'tamad' and 'al-fatwa', and include 'ikhtiyarat al-a'imma' (choices of the imams) for what is 'al-rajih wa al-sahih' (the preponderant and sound).
This shows his commentary is a selective, authoritative guide, not a mere summary.
5
Understand the naming rationale
He named it 'Al-Lubab' because it is 'al-ma'na 'inda itlaq al-ashab' (the meaning when the companions [Hanafi scholars] use the term). This signifies it captures the core intended meanings.
'Al-Lubab' thus indicates a concise yet comprehensive commentary.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فيقول العبد الفقير الجاني، عبد الغنى الغنيمي الميداني، غفر الله تعالى له ومحا عنه ومن له حق عليه : إن الكتاب المبارك للإمام القدوري، قد شاع واشتهر وصار كالعلم الضروري، ولذا عكفت الطلبة على تفهمه وتفهيمه، وازدحموا على حفظه وتعليمه، وكنت ممن عكف عليه الأيام الكثيرة، ودأب على التردد إليه حتى أسر بعض جواهره قد خفيت في معادنها، وبعض اللطائف قد استترت في غوامضها، وكان كثيرا ما يخطر لي أن أتطفل عليه، فأجمع بعض عبارات تكون كالشرح إليه، مع إيضاح معانيه، على وجه التوسط مع الإيضاح بحيث يكون مطلقا، إلا أنه كان يمنعني أني لست من أهل هذا الشان، وقصير الباع في هذا الميدان، ثم إني تشبثت بأذيال بركته، فشرعت في هذا المقام، رجاء الانتساب بالخدمة لذلك الإمام، وجمعت من كلامهم ما يدل على مقصودهم ومرامهم مما هو محتاج إليه، وتحري ما هو المعتمد والفتوى عليه، وضممت نجيم من اختيارات الأئمة لما هو الراجح والصحيح. ولم أرتض ما هو الأظهر والأوضح في التعبير. وسميته "اللباب" لأنه المعنى عند إطلاق الأصحاب، والذي تبعا لأصله، وأسأل الله تعالى أن يجعله خالصا لوجهه الكريم، إنه ما شاء قدير، وبالإجابة جدير.
The poor sinning servant, Abdul Ghani al-Ghanimi al-Maidani, may Allah forgive him and pardon him and those who have a right against him, says: Indeed, the blessed book of Imam al-Quduri has spread, become famous, and become like necessary knowledge. Therefore, students have devoted themselves to understanding it and making it understood, and have crowded upon memorizing it and teaching it. I was among those who devoted themselves to it for many days and persisted in attending to it until I captured some of its jewels that were hidden in their mines, and some of its subtleties that were concealed in their intricacies. It often occurred to me to occupy myself with it, to compile some phrases that would serve as an explanation for it, clarifying its meanings, in a moderate way with exposition so that it would be comprehensive, except that I was prevented by the fact that I am not among the people of this matter, and I have a short reach in this field. Then I clung to the skirts of his blessing, so I began this station, hoping for affiliation through service to that Imam. I collected from their statements what indicates their intent and aim of what is needed, and I sought out what is relied upon and given fatwa, and I added some stars from the choices of the imams for what is more preponderant and sound. And I did not choose what is more apparent and clearer in expression. I named it 'Al-Lubab' because it is the intended meaning when the companions use the term, and it follows its original. I ask Allah Almighty to make it sincere for His noble face; He is powerful over whatever He wills, and worthy of answering.
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage is the author's preface to his commentary. Abd al-Ghani al-Ghanimi al-Maidani begins by humbly introducing himself as a poor sinful servant, seeking forgiveness. He praises Imam al-Quduri's matn (Al-Mukhtasar) as widely known and essential, such that students have dedicated themselves to its study and teaching. Al-Maidani confesses his initial hesitation to write a commentary due to his perceived inadequacy, but eventually undertook the task, hoping for the blessing of association with the great imam. His methodology: to compile expressions that clarify the matn's meanings in a moderate style, relying on the relied-upon (mu'tamad) position and fatwa, and incorporating preferred choices from the imams. He named the work 'Al-Lubab' (The Core) because it captures the intended meaning used by the Hanafi scholars. He ends with a supplication for sincerity and acceptance.

Key Terms
اللباب (al-lubab): The name of this commentary, meaning 'the core' or 'the essence', indicating it contains the essential meanings of the matn.
المعتمد (al-mu'tamad): The relied-upon position in the school, which is the basis for fatwa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Because it covers all fiqh topics.

Key Takeaway
Al-Maidani's preface establishes Al-Lubab as a commentary that prioritizes the mu'tamad and rājih positions, making it a reliable guide for Hanafi fatwa.

Author's colophon recording completion

The colophon marks the book's completion and includes the author's humble supplication.

This passage is the closing note of 'al-Lubab', the commentary by Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani on al-Quduri's matn. Colophons are important for establishing the date and authenticity of a manuscript. Here, the author records the exact time of completion and offers prayers for himself and his readers.

1

قال مؤلفه حفظه الله : قد تم بحمد الله تعالى وقت الضحوة الكبرى من يوم الاثنين ثالث عشر رمضان المبارك سنة ست وستين ومائتين وألف ، من هجرة المصطفى الموصوف بأكمل وصف ، على يد جامعه الحقير الجاني ، كثير الأماني : عبد الغني النتيسي الميداني ، غفر الله ولوالديه ، وأحبابه ومن له حق عليه ، وأحسن إليهم وإليه ! وثبتنا بالقول الثابت عند الخاتمة ويوم الوقوف بين يديه ! والحمد لله الذي بنعمته تتم الصالحات ، وصلى الله على سيدنا محمد وعلى آله وأصحابه وأزواجه الطاهرات ، صلاة وسلاماً دائمين ما تعاقبت الأوقات ، وتواصلت البركات ، آمين .
Its author, may Allah protect him, said: It has been completed, by the praise of Allah Almighty, at the time of the great forenoon on Monday, the thirteenth of blessed Ramadan, in the year 1266 of the Hijrah of the Chosen One, described with the most complete description, by the hand of its compiler, the humble sinner, with many hopes: Abd al-Ghani al-Nutaysi al-Maydani. Commentary
This is the colophon of the book 'اللباب' by Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani, marking the completion of his commentary on al-Quduri. The author states he finished writing at forenoon on Monday, 13th Ramadan 1266 AH (corresponding to approximately July 1850 CE). He describes himself humbly as 'the compiler, the humble sinner, with many hopes'. He prays for forgiveness for himself, his parents, and his loved ones, and asks Allah to make them firm with the firm word (a reference to the testimony of faith) at the time of death and on the Day of Judgment. The colophon includes the standard formula: praise to Allah, and blessings upon the Prophet. This type of passage is typical at the end of classical Islamic manuscripts, recording the date of completion and the author's supplication.

Key Terms
الضحوة الكبرى (al-ḍaḥwa al-kubrā): The great forenoon, a time after sunrise when the sun has risen well above the horizon (approximately mid-morning).
القول الثابت (al-qawl al-thābit): The firm word, often a reference to the testimony of faith (shahada) that one hopes to utter at death.

Author's Introduction to Al-Lubab
Author opens his commentary with praise and introduction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the author Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani, his work Al-Lubab, and its relationship to al-Quduri's Mukhtasar.

Core Idea
Al-Lubab is a commentary on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar, arranged in order, seeking Allah's benefit and sincerity.

This lesson examines the opening passage of Al-Lubab Sharh Al-Quduri, a celebrated Hanafi fiqh commentary. The author introduces himself, his work, and its purpose, following the classical scholarly tradition. Understanding this introduction helps situate the commentary within the Hanafi curriculum.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author
The author introduces himself as 'Abd al-Ghani al-Ghunaymi al-Maydani'. He calls himself 'the poor servant' (al-ʿabd al-faqīr). Note that humility in introductions is a scholarly tradition.
Al-Maydani (d. 1298 AH) was a prominent Hanafi scholar from Damascus.
2
Identify the base text
He states he is commenting on 'Kitab al-Quduri', which is Mukhtasar al-Quduri by Abu al-Husayn al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), a foundational Hanafi matn.
The Mukhtasar is one of the Zahir al-Riwayah texts.
3
Note the title and arrangement
The commentary is named 'Al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Kitab' and is arranged according to the original book's order (ʿalā tartībihi).
'Al-Lubab' means 'the core' or 'the essence'.
4
Identify the purpose
He writes seeking Allah's reward, hoping to benefit Muslims, and for the work to be purely for Allah's sake.
This reflects the sincere intention (ikhlas) expected in Islamic scholarship.

بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم
الحمد لله الذي وفق من أراد به خيرا في الدين وأرشده إلى سبيل المهتدين، والصلاة والسلام على خير خلقه محمد المبعوث رحمة للعالمين، وعلى آله وصحبه والتابعين والعلماء العاملين والأئمة المجتهدين. أما بعد، فيقول العبد الفقير عبد الغني الغنيمي الميداني: هذا كتاب مبارك شرحته على كتاب القدوري، ورتبته على ترتيبه، وسميته "اللباب في شرح الكتاب"، راجيا من الله تعالى أن ينفع به المسلمين، وأن يجعله خالصا لوجهه الكريم. وصلى الله على سيدنا محمد وعلى آله وصحبه وسلم تسليما كثيرا.
Chapter Two: Study of Al-Lubab. In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. Praise be to Allah who guides whom He wills to goodness in religion and directs them to the path of the rightly guided, and blessings and peace be upon the best of His creation, Muhammad, sent as a mercy to the worlds, and upon his family, companions, followers, the righteous scholars, and the diligent imams. It follows the standard format of classical Islamic scholarly works: opening with the basmalah, praising Allah, sending blessings on the Prophet Muhammad, and then stating the purpose of the work. The author identifies himself as Abd al-Ghani al-Ghunaymi al-Maydani and explains that his book is a commentary (sharh) on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar, which is a foundational text in Hanafi fiqh.
