Author's Introduction: The Purpose of al-Lubab
Author's biographical introduction explaining his motivation for writing the commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the author's name, the title of his commentary, and his motivation for writing it.

Core Idea
Al-Lubab distills the essence of al-Quduri's Mukhtasar, aiming to clarify its absolute statements and present the most preponderant Hanafi views.

This passage introduces the author of al-Lubab, Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani, and his purpose in writing this commentary on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar. Although al-Maydani humbly disclaims his own qualifications, his work became a standard Hanafi reference. By understanding his motivation, you gain insight into the tradition of scholarly commentary in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author and his background
Locate the author's name and self-description. Note his humility as a rhetorical trope.
He calls himself 'al-`abd al-faqir al-jani' (the poor, sinning servant).
2
Recognize the motivation for writing
Al-Maydani found that al-Quduri's text needed clarification of its absolute expressions (taqyid al-mutlaq).
He saw 'some gems had been exhausted' and felt compelled to explain.
3
Understand the title's meaning
He named it 'al-Lubab' meaning 'the core' – it distills the essence of the original.
This is a common commentary genre: concise yet comprehensive.
4
Note the method of correction
He added corrections based on the 'tests of the imams' to present the most sound (rajih) views.
This shows commitment to the mufta bihi (operative) positions.
5
Observe the opening with basmalah
He begins with the basmalah following the Quran and the original text, seeking blessings.
This is standard practice in Islamic scholarly works.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم
[من يرد الله به خيرا يفقهه في الدين] وجدي في المهتدين، والصلاة والسلام على النبي المبعوث رحمة للعالمين وعلى آله والقرابة والتابعين، والعلماء العاملين ومن مقلدهم بإحسان إلى يوم الدين. 
أما بعد: يقول العبد الفقير الجاني، عبد الغني الفيح الميداني، غفر الله تعالى له ولوالديه ولمن تند ومن له حق عليه: هذا الكتاب المبارك للإمام القدوري قد شاعت بركته حتى صار كالماء الضروري، ولذا عكفت الطلبة على تفهمه وتفهيمه، ورغبوا على تعلمه وتعليمه، وكنت ممن عكف عليه الأيام الكثير وترددت إليه حتى أسرة لي ضميره، فرأيت بعض جواهره قد ناه وبعض الطوائف قد استقرت في مكامنها، وكان إلي أن اطلع عليه ستجد بعض عبارات تكون كالشرح الحامل له تقييد مطلقة، وإيضاح معانيه على وجه الإيضاح بحيث يكون معينا لمعاني، إلا أنه كان يمنعني أني لست من أهل هذا الشأن، وقصير الباع في هذا الميدان. ثم جرأتي على وضع هذا المقامة، جاء الانتساب بالخدمة لذلك الإمام تشتت أهداب بركته وتناهي منته، فاستخرت الله تعالى وجمعت ما ومرامهم، مع زيادة ما يغلب على الظن أنه علاج المقصد والمنتهى عليه، وختم ما جمعه بتصحيح من اختبارات الأئمة ما هو الراجح في التهذيب والتحرير، وتحري ما هو الأظهر والأبين، وسميته اللباب في شرح الكتاب، والله المعني ويقرب القرابة، وأسال الله تعالى أن يتقبله بفضله وينفع تبعا لأصله، وإن يجعله خالصا لوجهه الكريم وموجبا لذخائر نعمته عند ما يشاء تقديره وبالإجابة جديرة. وقد توخى رحمه الله تعالى في كتابه البسملة اقتداء بالكتاب العزيز عليه الصلاة والسلام، ورجاء حصول البركة في كتابه التأليف به فقال:
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. [Whoever Allah desires good for, He grants him understanding of religion] and my effort among the guided. Peace and blessings upon the Prophet sent as a mercy to the worlds, and upon his family, relatives, and followers, and the righteous scholars and those who follow them in excellence until the Day of Judgment. To proceed: The poor humble servant, Abd al-Ghani al-Fayyad al-Maydani, may Allah forgive him and his parents and those who have rights upon him, says: This blessed book of Imam al-Quduri has become so widespread that it is like essential water. Therefore, students have devoted themselves to understanding and teaching it, and I was among those who studied it extensively and revisited it until it became ingrained in my heart. I saw some of its gems had been exhausted and some aspects had settled in their places. When I examined it, I found some expressions that serve as explanatory notes restricting its absolute statements and clarifying its meanings clearly so that it helps understanding. However, I was prevented because I am not qualified in this field and have limited ability. Then I dared to undertake this task due to my affiliation with that Imam, hoping for the blessings of his legacy. So I sought guidance from Allah and compiled what I could, adding what I deemed beneficial for the purpose. I concluded it with corrections from the tests of the imams on the most preponderant views in refinement and verification, and I named it 'al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Kitab'. Allah is the bestower, and He is near. I ask Allah to accept it by His grace and benefit through it as its original, and to make it sincere for His noble face and a means for His treasures of grace. The author (may Allah have mercy on him) began his book with the basmalah following the Noble Book (the Quran) and hoping for blessings, saying:
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage is a biographical introduction by the author, Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani, explaining his motivation for writing the commentary 'al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Kitab' on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar. He begins with the basmalah and a paraphrased hadith about seeking understanding of religion. He humbly introduces himself as a poor servant seeking forgiveness. He praises al-Quduri's book as essential and widely studied. He describes how he studied it deeply and found areas that required clarification. Despite his initial hesitation due to his perceived lack of qualification, he was emboldened by his connection to Imam al-Quduri. He sought Allah's guidance (istikhara) and compiled his work, aiming to present the most preponderant views of the Hanafi imams. He named it 'al-Lubab' (the core/pith) because it distills the essence of the original. He ends by noting that al-Quduri began his text with the basmalah following the Quranic example. This introduction sets the tone of humility and scholarly dedication typical of Hanafi commentaries.

Key Terms
اللباب (al-Lubab): Title of the commentary: 'al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Kitab' meaning 'The Core in Explaining the Book'
القدوري (al-Quduri): Imam Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), author of the famous Hanafi matn 'Mukhtasar al-Quduri'

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Understanding the Commentator's Preface: Methodology and Humility
Author's preface explaining motivation and methodology

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key methodological principles of al-Maydani's commentary from his preface.

Core Idea
A scholar's preface reveals his method: al-Maydani selects preferred views, clarifies ambiguities, and humbly serves al-Quduri's text.

The preface of al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Kitab is not mere formality. It discloses the commentator's approach: he aims to extract the essence (lubab) of al-Quduri's matn, clarify ambiguous expressions, and present the most preferred (rajih) positions. He also expresses humility despite his scholarly effort.

Guided Path
1
Identify the commentator and his self-description
Read the opening lines: he calls himself the poor, sinful servant and seeks forgiveness. This frames his humility and reliance on Allah.
This sets the tone for the entire commentary.
2
Note his assessment of al-Quduri's matn
He describes it as 'essential water' and notes that students flock to it, but some jewels have been neglected.
This reveals his motivation: to restore and clarify neglected aspects.
3
Recognize his stated goal
He aims to restrict absolute expressions, clarify meanings, and select the most apparent and clear (azhar wa abyin) positions from the imams' tests.
His goal is not mere repetition but refined understanding.
4
Understand the significance of the title
He names it 'al-Lubab' (the essence) because it captures the core and is close to the original matn.
The title reflects his method: extracting essential meanings.
5
Observe the transition into commentary
He begins with basmalah following the Quran, then defines 'taharah' lexically and legally.
This shows he follows the structure of the matn while providing immediate clarification.

بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم الحمد لله رب العالمين والصلاة والسلام على سيدنا محمد المبعوث رحمة للعالمين وعلى آله وصحبه والتابعين والعلماء العاملين ومن قلدهم بإحسان إلى يوم الدين. أما بعد: العبد الفقير الجاني عبد الغني الفيح الميداني – غفر الله له ولوالديه ولمن تعلق به من ذوي الحق عليه – يقول: إن كتاب المبارك للإمام القدوري قد شاعت بركته حتى صار كالماء الضروري، ولذا عكفت الطلبة على تفهمه وتفهيمه، وازدحموا على تعلمه وتعليمه. وكنت ممن عكف عليه الأيام الكثير وتردد إليه حتى أسر إلي ضميره. فرأيت بعض جواهره قد نبذ، وبعض الطايفة قد استقرت في مكامنها. وكان إلى أن أطل عليه ستجد بعض عبارات تكون كالشرح الحمله هو تقييد مطلقه، وإيضاح معانيه على وجه الإيضاح بحيث يكون معينا لمعاني. إلا أنه كان يمنعني أني لست من أهل هذا الشأن، وقصير الباع في هذا الميدان. ثم جرهاني عا اتضاع هذا المقامة، جاء الانتساب بالخدمة لذلك الإمام تشينا باديال بركنده و تنهایی منده. فاستخرت الله تعالى وجمعت من ومرامهم، مع زيادة ما يغلب على الظن أنه علاج الـ[؟] والمنتوى عليه د وختم ما جمعه تصحيح من اختبارات الأيمة ما هو الراجح في التهذيب والتحرير وتحري ما هو أظهر و بين. وسميته اللباب في شرح الكتاب لأنه المعني والقريب. وأسال الله تعالى أن يتقبله بفضله النفع تبعا لأصله، وأن يجعله خالصا لوجهه الكريم و موجبا تورجنات النعده اند على ما يشا تقديره وبالإجابة جديرة. وقد توكلت على الله رحمه الله تعالى كتابه بالبسملة اقتداء بالكتاب المكرم صلى الله عليه وسلم، ورجاء حصول البركة في كتابه التاء به فقال: بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم. العبارة الطهارة لغة النظافة وشرعا النظافة عن النجاسة.
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. Praise be to Allah, Lord of the worlds, and prayers and peace be upon our master Muhammad, sent as a mercy to the worlds, and upon his family, companions, followers, and the righteous scholars and those who emulate them in goodness until the Day of Judgment. To proceed: The poor, sinful servant, Abd al-Ghani al-Fayyad al-Maydani – may Allah forgive him, his parents, and those who have a right upon him – says: Indeed, the blessed book of Imam al-Quduri has spread in its blessing until it became like essential water. Hence students devoted themselves to understanding it and making it understood, and crowded to learn it and teach it. I was among those who devoted many days to it and repeatedly returned to it until its inner meaning was revealed to me. I saw that some of its jewels had been neglected and some of the [scholarly] community had settled in their places. And when I approached it, you would find some expressions that are like a commentary, restricting its absolute, and clarifying its meanings in a clear manner so that it becomes an aid to its meanings. But I was prevented because I am not of this status and have limited capacity in this field. Then my circumstances drove me [to undertake] this task, and affiliation with service to that Imam came [to me] resembling its blessing and ... So I sought guidance from Allah and compiled from their [previous scholars'] aims, with additions that are likely to be a treatment for ... and concluded what I compiled by correcting from the tests of the imams what is the preferred view in refinement and editing, and investigating what is most apparent and clear. I named it 'al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Kitab' because it is the essence and the close. I ask Allah to accept it with His favor for the benefit following its original, and to make it purely for His noble face, and a means for ... and worthy of acceptance. And I relied on Allah, may He have mercy on him, [beginning] his book with the basmalah following the honored Book (Quran), upon him peace and blessings, and hoping for blessing in his book. He said: 'In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. The expression: purity (taharah) lexically means cleanliness, and legally means cleanliness from impurity.'
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This is the author's preface (front matter) to his commentary 'al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Kitab'. The commentator, Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani, begins with the basmalah and praise, then humbly introduces himself as a poor servant seeking forgiveness. He explains the immense popularity and importance of al-Quduri's matn (core text) in the Hanafi school, comparing it to essential water. He notes that despite its widespread use, some of its fine points have been neglected. He initially hesitated due to his own perceived inadequacy but felt compelled to serve the text. He compiled the work by selecting the most preferred (rajih) positions from the imams and clarified ambiguous expressions. He names his work 'al-Lubab' (the essence) and seeks Allah's acceptance. He then transitions into the commentary by stating his intention to follow the basmalah, just as the Quran does, and begins the first topic of purification (taharah), defining it lexically and legally.

Key Terms
اللباب (al-Lubab): The title of the commentary, meaning 'the essence' or 'the core'.
الكتاب (al-Kitab): Refers to the matn 'Mukhtasar al-Quduri', the foundational Hanafi fiqh text.
الطهارة (al-taharah): Purity; lexically cleanliness, legally removal of ritual impurity (hadath) and physical impurity (najis).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is the longest commentary on al-Quduri.
B) It extracts the essence and clarifies the meanings of the matn.
C) It only covers the topic of purification.
D) It is a simplified version for beginners.

Key Takeaway
The preface of al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Kitab establishes that the commentary will present the most preferred Hanafi positions with clarity, drawing out the core meanings of al-Quduri's matn.

Colophon of al-Lubab: The Scribal Tradition in Hanafi Fiqh
Author's completion statement with prayer and date

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the elements of a classical Hanafi manuscript colophon and explain its role in the transmission of fiqh texts.

Core Idea
A colophon is not a closing; it is a chain of custody for the fiqh tradition.

This final passage of al-Lubab is not a legal ruling but a scribal record. It tells us when, where, and by whom the manuscript was copied. For a Hanafi student, understanding the transmission chain is crucial: the reliability of a text depends on the integrity of its scribes. This colophon illustrates the piety and humility expected of a transmitter.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of text
Recognize that this passage is a colophon, not a fiqh ruling. It marks the completion of the manuscript and provides metadata.
Colophons are standard at the end of Islamic manuscripts.
2
Locate the date and scribe
Find the phrase 'سنة التسعين ومائتين' and the scribe's name 'محمد البدوي ابن الحاج'. Note that the year is ambiguous (likely 1290 AH) and needs verification.
Dates in colophons can be abbreviated.
3
Note the religious context
The work was completed after the Friday congregational prayer ('بعد صلاة الجمع'), showing the connection between scholarly labor and worship.
Many scribes recorded pious acts.
4
Examine the doxology
The text includes prayers upon the Prophet, his family, companions, and wives. These are standard closing formulae invoking blessings.
Doxologies reflect the scribe's devotion.
5
Reflect on the scribe's humility
The scribe describes himself as 'المقيرا زو التقصير' (the poor and deficient), indicating the traditional humility of transmitters.
This self-deprecation is common in colophons.

The Colophon of Al-Lubab: Textual Transmission and Printing of Hanafi Works
A printing colophon from the Ottoman era.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key elements of a classical colophon and explain the historical context of the printing of Al-Lubab under the Ottoman Sultan Abdul Hamid II as an example of Hanafi textual transmission.

Core Idea
The colophon of Al-Lubab records the Ottoman state's role in preserving and spreading the Hanafi madhhab.

A colophon is more than a publisher's note; it is a snapshot of the intellectual and political environment in which a text was produced. This colophon from the printing of Al-Lubab, a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, reveals the authority of the matn, the praise for the Ottoman sultan, and the exact date of publication. Understanding such paratextual elements is essential for a rigorous study of fiqh because it grounds texts in their historical chain of transmission.

Guided Path
1
Identify the components of the colophon
Look for the praise of Allah, the mention of the text's title and author, the ruler praised, the printing press, and the date.
2
Recognize the authority of Mukhtasar al-Quduri
Note the description of the matn as 'most beneficial' and 'necessary knowledge,' indicating its canonical status.
3
Understand the printing context
The colophon mentions the Ottoman Sultan Abdul Hamid II and the Ottoman Press, showing state sponsorship.
4
Interpret the date
The date is 25 Dhu al-Hijjah 1309 AH, which corresponds to a specific year; this helps in establishing the historical timeline.

Understanding Colophons and Manuscript Notes in Hanafi Textual Tradition
Colophon and manuscript note of the Hanafi work Al-Lubab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key components of a colophon and explain the significance of manuscript notes for the transmission history of a Hanafi text.

Core Idea
Colophons and manuscript notes are vital evidence for tracing the scholarly chain and authenticity of Hanafi works.

A colophon is not merely a closing note—it is a historical document that records who, when, and where a work was copied or printed. In the Hanafi tradition, such notes connect us to the living chain of transmission. This passage from the printed edition of Al-Lubab includes both a colophon and a precious manuscript note from 611 AH, offering a rare glimpse into the book's journey through centuries.

Guided Path
1
Identify the colophon's basic elements
Look for the name of the printer, the date, and the location. This colophon mentions Muhammad al-Zahri al-Ghumari, the Maimaniyya press in Cairo, and the year 1324 AH.
The colophon also includes praise for Allah and the Prophet, which is typical.
2
Interpret the significance of the printing date
The date 1324 AH (approx. 1906 CE) places this edition in the late Ottoman period, a time of active printing of Hanafi classical texts. Cairo's al-Azhar area was a center for such publishing.
Knowing the era helps assess the edition's authority.
3
Analyze the manuscript note despite corruption
The manuscript page from 611 AH (approx. 1214 CE) is heavily corrupted, but its very existence indicates that copies of Al-Lubab existed soon after the death of al-Quduri (d. 428 AH/1037 CE). Such early copies are invaluable for textual criticism.
The note likely contains a biography or praise, but the text is mostly illegible.
4
Reflect on the role of such paratexts in Hanafi scholarship
Colophons and ownership notes help establish the chain of transmission (sanad). For Hanafi fiqh, verifying the chain is crucial for the authority of the text. This lesson bridges textual history and fiqh methodology.
Even corrupted notes provide clues: the date alone is a key data point.

Studying a Front Matter: Identifying Authors and Manuscripts in Hanafi Texts
Biographical introduction and manuscript copy description

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the elements of a front matter section in a Hanafi fiqh commentary, determine the author and manuscript date, and explain the importance of textual criticism.

Core Idea
A manuscript's date and author's name anchor the authority of a Hanafi text.

When studying classical Hanafi works, you often encounter front matter sections that describe the manuscript and author. This lesson teaches you how to parse such sections, even when the text is corrupted, by focusing on key markers like dates and names.

Guided Path
1
Identify the heading
Look for words like 'الفصل', 'باب', etc. to locate the chapter or section title. Here it is 'الفصل الثاني : دراسة عن اللباب'.
Headings often contain the book title and author.
2
Locate the author's name
Search for recognizable names of Hanafi scholars. Despite corruption, 'القدوري' appears, referring to the famous Hanafi faqih.
Knowing major Hanafi authors helps identify corrupted text.
3
Find the manuscript date
Manuscript dates are given as 'نسخة (سنة)هـ'. Here it is 'نسخة (٦١١هـ)'.
The date 611 AH corresponds to approximately 1214 CE.
4
Determine the type of work
Look for words like 'شرح' (commentary) or 'متن' (text). 'اللباب' is a commentary (sharh) on Mukhtasar al-Quduri.
Commentaries expand and explain the base text.
5
Assess the purpose of the front matter
Understand whether it is a biography, a description of the manuscript, or a study. The heading 'دراسة عن اللباب' indicates a study.
Critical editions often include a study section.

Understanding Manuscript Notes on al-Lubab
Bibliographic notes on a manuscript of al-Lubab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the bibliographic details of a Hanafi manuscript and explain the significance of al-Lubab as a core Hanafi commentary.

Core Idea
A manuscript's date and condition tell us about the transmission of Hanafi fiqh.

This passage is not a fiqh ruling but a bibliographic note about a manuscript copy of al-Lubab. Such notes are critical for understanding the history of our texts. Here we learn that the manuscript is from 649 AH and only the second half survives, while another copy is from 611 AH.

Guided Path
1
Identify the work
The passage mentions 'al-Lubab', which is a Hanafi fiqh commentary by al-Maydani on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar.
Al-Lubab means 'the core' – it is a concise summary of Hanafi law.
2
Note the manuscript date
It states 'Copied in 649' – this is the hijri year of the manuscript copy (about 1251 CE).
The date helps establish the age and provenance of the text.
3
Assess completeness
The note says 'Only the second half', indicating the manuscript is incomplete.
Incomplete manuscripts are common; scholars must compare multiple copies.
4
Relate to textual tradition
The two dates (611 and 649) show that al-Lubab was being copied within a few decades of its composition, attesting to its early importance in Hanafi circles.
This helps us understand the work's reception and transmission chain.

This passage appears to be from a manuscript description section at the beginning of al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri. It includes a repeated chapter heading and a date (745 AH). The text is heavily garbled due to poor OCR of marginalia and headings. Manuscript Colophon and Transmission of al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri
Bibliographical notes and colophon of the manuscript

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key bibliographical details from the colophon of a Hanafi manuscript and explain their significance for the transmission of al-Quduri's text.

Core Idea
Colophons preserve the date and provenance of manuscripts, anchoring the transmission of Hanafi fiqh texts.

This passage presents the final pages of a manuscript of al-Lubab, a commentary on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar. Though the text is heavily garbled by OCR, the colophon reveals that this copy was completed in 892 AH. Understanding how to read manuscript notes is essential for evaluating the historical layers of our fiqh sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of text
Recognize that the passage is a colophon and manuscript note, not a legal discussion. Look for dates, scribe names, and technical terms like 'صفح'. The garbled text indicates OCR error, but the structure is typical of a manuscript endnote.
Colophons often contain the date of copying and sometimes the location.
2
Extract the dates
Locate the Hijri year numbers. The text mentions 'تسعون وثمانمائة' (892 AH) on page 235 and 'تسعمائة ثمانون' (980 AH) on page 236. These are two different copies or a note about an older copy.
The later date (980 AH) may be a note added by a later owner or reader.
3
Identify the authors and works
The passage names 'القدوري' (al-Quduri) and 'اللباب' (al-Lubab). Al-Quduri authored the matn 'Mukhtasar al-Quduri', and al-Lubab is a commentary (sharh) by al-Maydani on that matn.
Knowing the chain of matn and sharh is crucial for fiqh study.
4
Assess the reliability
Note the OCR corruption, which requires human verification. The colophon date 892 AH is relatively early; a copy from that period holds authority if properly verified.
Always check multiple manuscripts to establish a reliable text.

The Role of Biographical Chapters in Hanafi Fiqh Works
Heading for biographical chapter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the function of biographical chapters in Hanafi fiqh commentaries and identify the type of scholars included.

Core Idea
Biographical chapters establish scholarly authority, linking rulings to their transmitters.

This lesson introduces the third chapter of al-Lubab, which contains brief biographies of scholars cited in the commentary. While not containing legal rulings itself, this chapter serves an important function: it helps students trace the authority of transmitted opinions and understand the hierarchy within the Hanafi school. Knowing who these scholars are and their rank is essential for evaluating the strength of different narrations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the purpose of this chapter
The chapter provides biographical sketches (tarajim) of the scholars whose names appear in al-Lubab. This helps readers gauge the reliability and authority of each transmitted opinion.
Such chapters are common in Hanafi commentaries to establish the chain of transmission.
2
Recognize the hierarchy of Hanafi scholars
Biographies often indicate the scholar's rank in the madhhab, e.g., mujtahid, ashab al-takhrīj, etc. This guides practitioners in preferring certain opinions over others.
For example, a mujtahid mutlaq's opinion is given more weight than a mujtahid fi al-madhhab.
3
Explain the importance of isnad in fiqh
Just as in hadith, fiqh works trace their knowledge back to the early imams. Knowing the transmitters strengthens confidence in the rulings.
Even though fiqh isnad is less formalized, the principle remains: authority depends on the chain.

الفصل الثالث
ترجمة موجزة للأعلام المذكورين في اللباب
Chapter Three: A brief biography of the notable scholars mentioned in al-Lubab.
Source pages p. 239

Commentary
This is a chapter heading in the commentary al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri by al-Maydani. The author dedicates a chapter to providing concise biographical entries for the jurists and hadith transmitters whose names appear throughout his work. Such biographical notes are a standard feature of Hanafi fiqh works to establish the authority and chain of transmission of the rulings. This chapter likely covers the founding imams of the Hanafi school—Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad al-Shaybani—as well as later authorities like al-Quduri and the commentator himself. The biographies help students situate each scholar in time and place, understand their rank in the madhhab, and recognize the weight of their transmitted opinions.

Key Terms
ترجمة (tarjamah): In this context, a brief biographical sketch of a scholar, including name, lineage, teachers, students, and works.
الأعلام (al-a‘lām): Notable personalities, specifically scholars of fiqh and hadith whose names are cited in the commentary.
اللباب (al-Lubāb): The title of al-Maydani's commentary on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar, meaning 'The Core' or 'The Essence'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The rulings on purification
B) A brief biography of scholars mentioned in al-Lubab
C) A summary of the Mukhtasar al-Quduri
D) The history of the Hanafi school

Key Takeaway
The biographical chapter establishes the chain of authority for rulings, a critical element in Hanafi fiqh methodology.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
8 min
Notable Hanafi Scholars Mentioned in Al-Lubab
Biographical list of Hanafi scholars from al-Lubab's appendix.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify key Hanafi scholars from the classical period, state their honorific titles, and name their major works referenced in al-Lubab.

Core Idea
Al-Lubab's biographical appendix reveals the chain of scholarly transmission through commentaries and fatwas.

This lesson introduces the Hanafi jurists whose works and commentaries are cited in al-Lubab. Understanding who these scholars are and their contributions helps you appreciate the depth of the Hanafi tradition and the authorities behind the rulings.

Guided Path
1
Scan the list
Identify each scholar's name, honorific title, and year of death. These are the key identifiers.
Use the death dates to place the scholar in chronological context.
2
Note the honorifics
Recognize titles like al-Sadr al-Shahid, Burhan al-A'imma, Shams al-A'imma, etc. These indicate the scholar's rank and recognition.
Hanafi honorifics are specific to the madhhab and reflect scholarly esteem.
3
Link to works
Connect each scholar to their major work(s) mentioned, such as commentaries on al-Quduri, al-Hidaya, or al-Jami' al-Kabir.
Many scholars are known for a single important commentary.
4
Contextualize chronologically
Understand the spread of dates: from early companions of Abu Hanifa (d. 204 AH) to later commentators (d. 1207 AH). This shows the ongoing development of the school.
The list spans over 1000 years of Hanafi scholarship.
5
Use for reference
Know that this appendix is a tool for locating authoritative sources when reading al-Lubab. If a scholar is cited, you can find their biography here.
The references (Taj al-Tarajim, etc.) are standard biographical works.

Chapter Three: Brief Biography of the Notable Figures Mentioned in al-Lubab
43 - al-Husam al-Shahid is al-Sadr al-Shahid 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz ibn Mazah Burhan al-A'imma. He has al-Fatawa al-Sughra and al-Kubra. Died 536 AH. Taj al-Tarajim p. 217.
44 - al-Haddadi (or al-Haddad Abu Bakr ibn 'Ali ibn Muhammad, author of al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: commentary on al-Quduri and its abridgment al-Jawhara al-Nayyira, and a commentary on the versified work of al-Nasafi. Died 800 AH. Taj al-Tarajim p. 141.
45 - al-Hasan ibn Ziyad al-Lu'lu'i, companion of Imam Abu Hanifa, he has many books. Died 204 AH. Taj al-Tarajim p. 150.
46 - al-Halabi Ibrahim ibn Muhammad ibn Ibrahim. He has Talkhis Fath al-Qadir by Ibn al-Humam, and Sharh Munyat al-Musalli. Died 956 AH. Hadiyyat al-'Arifin 1/27. He is the one intended when [the name] is used absolutely. And al-Halabi is also applied occasionally to: Ibn Amir Haj al-Halabi Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn Hasan, author of al-Taqrir wa al-Tahbir: commentary on al-Tahrir in usul. Died 879 AH. Hadiyyat al-'Arifin 2/208.
47 - al-Hulwani 'Abd al-'Aziz ibn Ahmad ibn Nasr Shams al-A'imma, the leading Hanafi of his time in Bukhara. He has a commentary on al-Jami' al-Kabir by Muhammad ibn al-Hasan, al-Fatawa, a commentary on al-Siyar al-Kabir, al-Waqi'at fi al-Furu', and a commentary on al-Hiyal al-Shar'iyya by al-Khassaf. Died 456 AH, and some say otherwise. Taj al-Tarajim p. 189, al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya p. 95, Hadiyyat al-'Arifin 1/577.
48 - Hamid al-Din 'Ali ibn Muhammad ibn 'Ali al-Ramshi al-Bukhari al-Darir. Died 666 AH. He has a commentary on al-Jami' al-Kabir by Muhammad ibn al-Hasan, a commentary on al-Hidaya by al-Marghinani, and a commentary on al-Manzuma al-Nasafiyya. Al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya p. 125, al-Jawahir al-Mudiyya 2/598, Hadiyyat al-'Arifin 1/711.
49 - al-Khujandi, perhaps Jalal al-Din al-Khujandi 'Umar ibn Muhammad ibn 'Umar al-Khabbazi. He has a gloss on al-Hidaya, al-Fatawa, and al-Mughni fi Usul al-Fiqh. Died 691 AH. Hadiyyat al-'Arifin 1/787, Taj al-Tarajim p. 220.
50 - al-Khassaf Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn 'Amr ('Umar). He has al-Hiyal, al-Kharaj, and al-Manasik. Died 261 AH. Taj al-Tarajim p. 97.
51 - Khalil al-Kamili, author of a gloss on Risalat al-Asturlab: Khalil ibn 'Abd al-Salam al-Dimashqi. Died 1207 AH. Hilyat al-Bashar 1/591.
52 - Khwahar Zada Muhammad ibn al-Husayn known as Bakr Khwahar Zada al-Bukhari. He has al-Mukhtasar, al-Tajnis, and al-Mabsut. Died 483 AH. Al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya p. 163. And the meaning of 'Khwahar Zada' is the son of a scholar's sister, and the subject is the son of the sister of Qadi Abi Thabit Muhammad ibn Ahmad al-Bukhari.
53 - al-Khayr al-Ramli, Khayr al-Din ibn Ahmad ibn Nur al-Din 'Ali al-Ayyubi al-'Alimi al-Faruqi. He has a gloss on al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir, and a gloss on Kanz al-Daqa'iq and al-Fatawa. Died 1081 AH. Hadiyyat al-'Arifin 1/358.
54 - al-Rustughfani 'Ali ibn Sa'id, from the great mashayikh of Samarqand, from the most eminent companions of Abu Mansur al-Maturidi. He has Irshad al-Muhtadi. Died around 345 AH. Al-A'lam 4/291, al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya p. 65, Taj al-Tarajim p. 205.
55 - Rukn al-A'imma al-Sabbabi 'Abd al-Karim ibn Muhammad Abu al-Makarim. He has a commentary on al-Quduri, and he studied fiqh under Abu al-Yusr al-Bazdawi al-Madini.
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage is the third chapter of the book's appendix, providing brief biographical notes on notable Hanafi scholars mentioned in the main text (al-Lubab). Each entry includes the scholar's full name, honorific titles, major works, and death date, with references to standard biographical sources like Taj al-Tarajim, al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya, and Hadiyyat al-'Arifin. The list covers a range of early to later Hanafi authorities: from early companions of Abu Hanifa like al-Hasan ibn Ziyad al-Lu'lu'i (d. 204 AH) to later commentators like al-Halabi (d. 956 AH) and al-Khayr al-Ramli (d. 1081 AH). Many of these scholars are known for key commentaries on foundational Hanafi texts: al-Quduri, al-Hidaya, al-Jami' al-Kabir, etc. The entry for al-Halabi distinguishes two figures with the same nisba. The entry for Khwahar Zada explains the Persian term meaning 'sister's son', indicating he was a nephew of a famous judge. This biographical appendix serves as a quick reference for students to situate the authorities cited in the commentary.

Key Terms
الصدر الشهيد (al-Sadr al-Shahid): An honorific title for 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz ibn Mazah, meaning 'the martyr leader', indicating his high rank and martyrdom.
برهان الأئمة (Burhan al-A'imma): An honorific title meaning 'Proof of the Imams', used for a leading Hanafi jurist.
شمس الأئمة (Shams al-A'imma): An honorific title meaning 'Sun of the Imams', indicating great scholarly stature.
خواهر زاده (Khwahar Zada): Persian compound word meaning 'sister's son' (nephew). Here it is the nickname of Muhammad ibn al-Husayn al-Bukhari, indicating he was the nephew of a scholar.
ركن الأئمة (Rukn al-A'imma): An honorific title meaning 'Pillar of the Imams', used for 'Abd al-Karim al-Sabbabi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Knowing the scholars behind the texts anchors your understanding of the Hanafi tradition's intellectual lineage.

Understanding Bibliographic Introductions in Hanafi Commentaries
Chapter heading introducing sources.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the purpose of a bibliographical chapter heading in a classical Hanafi commentary and identify its role in establishing scholarly authority.

Core Idea
A chapter heading can reveal the author's methodology and the sources relied upon.

In classical Hanafi works like Al-Lubab, authors often include introductory chapters that list the books and sources they reference. These introductions are not mere formalities; they orient the reader to the tradition behind the commentary and signal the author's scholarly lineage. This short chapter heading sets the stage for the following discussion of key texts.

Guided Path
1
Locate the Chapter Heading
Identify the title 'الفصل الرابع' and note its position within the larger work. Recognize that Al-Lubab is a commentary (sharh) on Al-Quduri's matn.
This is the opening of Chapter Four.
2
Identify the Genre
Recognize that this is a bibliographical introduction, not a fiqh ruling. The phrase 'تعريف موجز بالكتب والمصادر' tells us the author will define and describe the sources used.
Such sections are common in classical commentaries.
3
Understand the Purpose
Reflect on why the author includes this section: to establish the authority and reliability of the work by naming the key texts relied upon, and to help the reader follow the references.
Transparency in sources is a mark of scholarly rigor.
4
Apply to Reading Practice
When studying any classical Hanafi text, first scan for introductory sections that list sources. This prepares you to trace the arguments back to their foundations.
This is a practical skill for advanced study.

Commentary
This passage is a chapter heading from Al-Lubab. It signals that the following section will define and describe the various books and sources used throughout the commentary. Such introductions are common in classical Hanafi works to help the reader understand the foundational texts relied upon by the author. No legal ruling is presented here; it is purely bibliographical.

Key Terms
اللباب (Al-Lubab): The title of the commentary being introduced; literally 'the core' or 'the essence'.
الفصل الرابع (Al-Fasl al-Rabi'): Chapter Four, indicating the section of the work that follows.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Bibliographic introductions orient the reader to the authoritative sources used in a commentary, establishing scholarly transparency and lineage.

Introduction and Front Matter

Key Hanafi Reference Works in al-Lubab
List of Hanafi reference works

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the major Hanafi reference works cited in al-Lubab, state their authors, and classify their authority within the madhhab.

Core Idea
Knowing the sources of the Hanafi school is the key to understanding the authority of rulings.

This lesson introduces you to the Hanafi books that the author of al-Lubab frequently cites. Each work has a specific place in the madhhab's hierarchy—some are primary (Zahir al-Riwayah), some are later teaching texts, and others are rare transmissions (Nawadir). Understanding these sources will help you weigh rulings correctly when studying al-Lubab and other Hanafi commentaries.

Guided Path
1
List the books and their authors
Go through each entry in the source and note the book title, author's full name, and death year. This gives you the historical and biographical context.
Some entries have partially corrupted numbering; ignore those artifacts.
2
Classify each book by type
Determine whether the work is a primary source (like al-Mabsut), a later commentary (like al-Ikhtiyar), a work of usul (like Usul al-Bazdawi), or a collection of rare transmissions (like al-Amali).
al-Mabsut = Zahir al-Riwayah; al-Amali = Nawadir; al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir = qawaid work.
3
Note the publication status
The source marks each book as printed (ط) or manuscript (خ). This tells you about availability and potential textual variations.
al-Asrar and al-Amali are still in manuscript form.
4
Understand the hierarchy
In the Hanafi school, rulings from al-Mabsut and other Zahir al-Riwayah texts are most authoritative. Later commentaries like al-Ikhtiyar summarize and explain, while Nawadir sources like al-Amali contain weaker transmissions.
This hierarchy affects which opinion is relied upon for fatwa.

Chapter Four: Brief definition of the books mentioned in al-Lubab
Brief definition of the books and sources mentioned in al-Lubab
1 - al-Ikhtiyar li-Ta'lil al-Mukhtar by Abu al-Fadl al-Mawsili ‘Abdullah ibn Mahmud, d. 683 AH, (printed).
2 - al-Asrar fi al-Usul wa al-Furu‘ by Abu Zayd al-Dabusi ‘Ubaydullah ibn ‘Umar, d. 430 AH, (manuscript).
3 - al-Ashbah wa al-Naza’ir by Ibn Nujaym Zayn al-Din ibn Ibrahim, d. 970 AH, (printed).
4 - al-Asl (also called al-Mabsut) by Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani, d. 189 AH, (a quarter of the book published, the rest in manuscript).

(al-Fawa’id al-Bahiyyah p. 11), (printed with its commentary al-Idah by Ibn Kamal Pasha as well).
-7

Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This is a front-matter appendix from 'al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri' listing the key Hanafi reference works cited throughout the commentary. The author provides each book's title, full author name, death date, and a note on publication status: (ط) for printed and (خ) for manuscript. These include major Hanafi texts such as al-Ikhtiyar, al-Asrar, al-Ashbah wa al-Naza’ir, and the foundational works of the school like al-Asl (al-Mabsut) by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani. Other entries include commentaries on al-Wiqayah and the usul work of al-Bazdawi. The list serves as a bibliography to help the student identify the sources and their authority within the Hanafi tradition. Note that the numbering in the OCR is slightly corrupt, but the content is clearly a continuous list of references.

Key Terms
المبسوط (al-Mabsut): Also called al-Asl, the magnum opus of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, one of the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah.
الاختيار (al-Ikhtiyar): A Hanafi fiqh work by al-Mawsili that explains the rulings of al-Mukhtar with their legal evidences.
الأمالي (al-Amali): A collection of dictations by Imam Abu Yusuf on various fiqh topics.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which book is by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani and is also known as al-Mabsut?
A) al-Ikhtiyar
B) al-Asl
C) al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir
D) al-Amali

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's authority hierarchy begins with Zahir al-Riwayah texts like al-Mabsut, followed by later commentaries, qawaid works, and finally Nawadir sources.

Identifying the Sources of Al-Lubab: A Bibliography of Hanafi Fiqh Works
A bibliography of Hanafi fiqh sources cited in Al-Lubab.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and classify the key Hanafi fiqh books referenced in Al-Lubab, distinguishing between commentaries, fatwa collections, and works on khilaf.

Core Idea
Knowing the sources of Al-Lubab unlocks the chain of authority in Hanafi fiqh.

This passage is a bibliography — a list of the books cited by the commentator of Al-Lubab. Each entry gives the title, author, death date, and format (printed or manuscript). Understanding these references is crucial for tracing the chain of transmission and authority in Hanafi rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the book title and author
For each entry, note the full title and author's name. This gives you the exact work being referenced.
Titles often indicate the genre, e.g., 'Sharh' means commentary.
2
Note the death date (t)
The death date (in Hijri) tells you the historical layer of the source. Earlier authors are closer to the founding Imams.
This helps assess the authority of the work within the school.
3
Check the format
Printed (ط) or manuscript (خ) indicates availability and level of dissemination.
Printed works are widely accessible; manuscripts may be rare or unverified.
4
Classify the work
Determine whether it is a commentary (sharh), a fatwa collection, a work on khilaf (disputed issues), or another genre.
This tells you the purpose of the work.
5
Connect to other works
Many authors wrote multiple books; the notes sometimes list them. This shows the intellectual network.
For example, al-Marghinani wrote Al-Hidaya and also Al-Tajnis wa al-Mazid.

الفصل الرابع: تعريف موجز بالكتب المذكورة في اللباب
- البحر الرائق في شرح كنز الدقائق، لابن نجيم زين الدين بن إبراهيم، ت ٩٧٠ هـ، (ط).
٩- بدائع الصنائع في ترتيب الشرائع (شرح تحفة الفقهاء للسمرقندي، ت ٥٣٩ هـ)، لعلاء الدين الكاساني أبي بكر بن مسعود، ت ٥٨٧ هـ ، (ط).
۱۰ - البرهان شرح مواهب الرحمن في مذهب النعمان، كلاهما لإبراهيم بن موسى الطرابلسي، ت ٩٢٢هـ، (خ).
۱۱ - البزازية (الفتاوى البزازية المسماة بالوجيز، لحافظ الدين بن محمد، المعروف بابن البزاز الكردري، ت ٨٢٧هـ، (ط).
١٢ - البناية في شرح الهداية لبدر الدين العيني محمود بن أحمد محمد، ت ٨٥٥هـ ، (ط).
١٣ - تبيين الحقائق شرح كنز الدقائق للزيلعي عثمان بن علي، ت ٧٤٣هـ ، (ط).
١٤ - التتارخانية (الفتاوى التتارخانية لعالم بن العلاء الأنصاري الأندربتي الدهلوي، ت ٧٨٦هـ، (ط).
١٥ - التتمة (تتمة الفتاوى لأبي المعالي محمود بن أحمد بن عبد العزيز بن عمر بن مازه صاحب المحيط البرهاني، والذخيرة، وشرح الجامع الصغير، وشرح أدب القضاء للخصاف، والطريقة البرهانية ، ت ٦١٦ هـ ، (خ) . الفوائد البهية ص ٢٠٥.
١٦ - التجريد في مسائل الخلاف بين الحنفية والشافعية، للقدوري أحمد بن محمد، صاحب المختصر المشهور، ت ٤٢٨هـ، (ط).
١٧ - التجنيس والمزيد، وهو لبيان ما استنبطه المتأخرون، ولم ينص عليه المتقدمون للمرغيناني علي بن أبي بكر، صاحب الهداية، ت ٥٩٣هـ ، (ط).
١٨ - التحرير في أصول الفقه للكمال ابن الهمام، ت ٨٦١هـ.
١٩ - تحرير النقول في نفقات الفروع والأصول، لابن عابدين محمد أمين، ت ١٢٥٢هـ ، (ط ضمن رسائله، رسالة رقم ١٢).
٢٠ - التحفة (تحفة الفقهاء)، لأبي منصور علاء الدين السمرقندي أحمد، ت ٥٣٩ هـ ، (ط).
۲۱ - تصحيح القدوري، لقاسم بن قُطلُوبُغَا، ت ٨٧٩هـ ، (ط).
٢٢ - التعريفات للجرجاني علي بن محمد، ت ٨١٦ هـ، (ط).
٢٣ - تفسير الحاكم؟ لم يتبين لي أي حاكم أراد.
٢٤ - التقريب في المسائل الخلافية بين الإمام أبي حنيفة وأصحابه، للقدوري أحمد بن محمد، ت ٤٢٨هـ، (خ).
٢٥- تنبيه الرقود على مسائل النقود من رخص وغلاء وكساد وانقطاع، لابن عابدين محمد أمين، ت١٢٥٢هـ ، (ط ضمن رسائله ٥٨/٢).
٢٦- تنوير الأبصار وجامع البحار، للتمرتاشي محمد بن عبد الله، ت ١٠٠٤هـ ، (ط).
۲۷- تنوير البصائر على الأشباه والنظائر، لشرف الدين عبد القادر بن بركات الغزي فرغ منه سنة ١٠٠٥هـ، (خ).
۲۸ - التهذيب (تهذيب اللغة)، للأزهري محمد أحمد، ت ٣٧٠هـ، (ط).
Chapter Four: A brief definition of the books mentioned in Al-Lubab
- Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq fi Sharh Kanz al-Daqa'iq, by Ibn Nujaym Zayn al-Din ibn Ibrahim, d. 970 AH, (printed).
9- Bada'i' al-Sana'i' fi Tartib al-Shara'i' (Commentary on Tuhfat al-Fuqaha' of al-Samarqandi, d. 539 AH), by 'Ala' al-Din al-Kasani Abu Bakr ibn Mas'ud, d. 587 AH, (printed).
10 - Al-Burhan Sharh Mawahib al-Rahman fi Madhhab al-Nu'man, both by Ibrahim ibn Musa al-Tarabullusi, d. 922 AH, (manuscript).
11 - Al-Bazzaziyya (Al-Fatawa al-Bazzaziyya called al-Wajiz), by Hafiz al-Din ibn Muhammad, known as Ibn al-Bazzaz al-Kardari, d. 827 AH, (printed).
12 - Al-Binaya fi Sharh al-Hidaya by Badr al-Din al-'Ayni Mahmud ibn Ahmad Muhammad, d. 855 AH, (printed).
13 - Tabyin al-Haqa'iq Sharh Kanz al-Daqa'iq by al-Zayla'i 'Uthman ibn 'Ali, d. 743 AH, (printed).
14 - Al-TatarKhaniyya (Al-Fatawa al-TatarKhaniyya by 'Alam ibn al-'Ala' al-Ansari al-Andarbiti al-Dihlawi, d. 786 AH, (printed).
15 - Al-Tatimma (Tatimmat al-Fatawa by Abu al-Ma'ali Mahmud ibn Ahmad ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz ibn 'Umar ibn Maza, author of al-Muhit al-Burhani, al-Dhakhira, Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir, Sharh Adab al-Qada' al-Khassaf, and al-Tariqa al-Burhaniyya, d. 616 AH, (manuscript). Al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya p. 205.
16 - Al-Tajrid fi Masa'il al-Khilaf bayn al-Hanafiyya wa al-Shafi'iyya, by al-Quduri Ahmad ibn Muhammad, author of the famous Mukhtasar, d. 428 AH, (printed).
17 - Al-Tajnis wa al-Mazid, which explains what the later scholars deduced and the earlier scholars did not explicitly state, by al-Marghinani 'Ali ibn Abi Bakr, author of al-Hidaya, d. 593 AH, (printed).
18 - Al-Tahrir fi Usul al-Fiqh by al-Kamal Ibn al-Humam, d. 861 AH.
19 - Tahrir al-Nuqul fi Nafaqat al-Furu' wa al-Usul, by Ibn 'Abidin Muhammad Amin, d. 1252 AH, (printed within his treatises, treatise no. 12).
20 - Al-Tuhfa (Tuhfat al-Fuqaha'), by Abu Mansur 'Ala' al-Din al-Samarqandi Ahmad, d. 539 AH, (printed).
21 - Tashih al-Quduri, by Qasim ibn Qutlubugha, d. 879 AH, (printed).
22 - Al-Ta'rifat by al-Jurjani 'Ali ibn Muhammad, d. 816 AH, (printed).
23 - Tafsir al-Hakim? It is not clear to me which Hakim is intended.
24 - Al-Taqrib fi al-Masa'il al-Khilafiyya bayn al-Imam Abi Hanifa wa Ashabihi, by al-Quduri Ahmad ibn Muhammad, d. 428 AH, (manuscript).
25- Tanbih al-Ruqud 'ala Masa'il al-Nuqud min Rukhsa wa Ghala' wa Kasad wa Inqita', by Ibn 'Abidin Muhammad Amin, d. 1252 AH, (printed within his treatises 2/58).
26- Tanwir al-Absar wa Jami' al-Bihar, by al-Tamartashi Muhammad ibn 'Abdullah, d. 1004 AH, (printed).
27- Tanwir al-Basa'ir 'ala al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir, by Sharaf al-Din 'Abd al-Qadir ibn Barakat al-Ghazzi, completed in 1005 AH, (manuscript).
28 - Al-Tahdhib (Tahdhib al-Lugha), by al-Azhari Muhammad Ahmad, d. 370 AH, (printed).
Source pages p. 262

Commentary
This passage is the front matter of Al-Lubab, specifically a bibliography chapter titled 'A brief definition of the books mentioned in Al-Lubab.' It lists 28 works (numbered with dashes) that are referenced in the main text. The list includes commentaries, fatwa collections, and other Hanafi fiqh sources. Each entry gives the book title, author name, death date (t = year AH), and often the format (printed = ط, manuscript = خ). Some entries include additional notes like the author's other works. This bibliography aids students in identifying the primary and secondary sources of the Hanafi school that the commentator relies upon.

Key Terms
شرح (sharh): A commentary that explains and expands upon a base text (matn).
فتوى (fatwa): A non-binding legal opinion issued by a qualified jurist.
خلاف (khilaf): Disputed issues between schools of thought or within a school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) To provide a biography of the author
B) To define the books referenced in the commentary
C) To explain the principles of fiqh
D) To list the chapters of the book

Key Takeaway
This bibliography is a gateway to the Hanafi textual tradition; each entry represents a link in the chain of knowledge.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Navigating the Bibliography of Al-Lubab
Bibliography of referenced Hanafi fiqh works

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the major Hanafi fiqh works referenced in Al-Lubab, state their authors and approximate periods, and interpret the editor's notations for print and manuscript status.

Core Idea
Knowing the sources behind a Hanafi commentary is essential to understanding its authority and method.

This lesson introduces the bibliography appended to Al-Lubab, a commentary on Al-Quduri. The list includes 23 works ranging from early foundational texts to later commentaries. Understanding these references helps you appreciate the chain of transmission and the scope of sources used by the author, Al-Maydani.

Guided Path
1
Survey the list
Read through the titles and authors, noting the variety of subjects (fiqh, usul, language) and the time periods covered.
Entries are numbered from 17 to 39, continuing from a previous section.
2
Identify key heavyweight works
Look for works that are frequently cited in Hanafi studies, such as Al-Hidayah, Mukhtasar al-Quduri, and Al-Jami' al-Saghir.
These are the core texts of the school.
3
Analyze author chronology
Note the death dates of the authors; they range from the 2nd century (e.g., Muhammad al-Shaybani d. 189) to the 13th century (e.g., Ibn Abidin d. 1252). This shows the continuous development of Hanafi fiqh.
The majority are from the 6th–8th centuries AH.
4
Interpret the notations
The symbols ط (printed) and خ (manuscript) indicate availability. Pay attention to question marks after some titles, which signal uncertainty by the editor.
This critical apparatus is important for evaluating the reliability of citations.
5
Use the bibliography as a reference tool
When studying Al-Lubab, cross‑reference any cited work with this list to locate the original source and understand its authority.
This bibliography is a gateway to deeper research.

Commentary
This passage is a bibliography (front matter) listing key Hanafi fiqh works referenced throughout Al-Lubab. It provides book titles, authors, death dates, and publication status (ط = printed, خ = manuscript). The list includes well-known works like Al-Tahawi's Mukhtasar, Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar, Al-Hidayah, and others. Note some titles are given with notes from the editor about uncertain identifications (e.g., 'Tafsir al-Hakim' and 'Jami' Shams al-A'imma'). This section serves as a reference guide for students to locate the sources cited in the commentary.

Key Terms
ط (Tā’): Abbreviation for 'matbu‘' (printed), indicating the work is available in print.
خ (Khā’): Abbreviation for 'makhṭūṭ' (manuscript), indicating the work exists only in manuscript form.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The bibliography in Al-Lubab demonstrates the author's reliance on a wide range of Hanafi authorities, from early masters to later commentators, and is a vital tool for verifying references.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Navigating the Hanafi Source Texts: Al-Lubab's Bibliography
Bibliographic list of Hanafi source texts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify major Hanafi texts listed in al-Lubab's bibliography, their authors, and their significance as sources of law.

Core Idea
This bibliography maps the foundational sources of the Hanafi madhhab.

This chapter provides a list of books referenced in al-Lubab, with brief descriptions. It serves as a reference tool for students to locate the original sources behind the rulings. Understanding this list helps you appreciate the depth and breadth of the Hanafi textual tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Title and Author
For each entry, note the book title (e.g., al-Jami' al-Saghir) and its author (e.g., Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani).
Some titles are attributed with uncertainty, indicated by editorial marks.
2
Note the Death Date
Each author's death date (in AH) gives you a chronological sense of the work's era and its place in the school's development.
Dates help distinguish early foundational texts from later commentaries.
3
Check Publication Status
Entries often indicate whether the work is in manuscript (خ) or print (ط). This tells you about availability.
Manuscript works may be less accessible; printed ones are more widely used.
4
Recognize Commentary Relationships
Some entries are commentaries on earlier works, e.g., al-Jawhara al-Nayyira is a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. Note the relationship.
Commentaries expand on or explain earlier matn texts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الرابع: تعريف موجز بالكتب المذكورة في اللباب
٢٩ - التوضيح شرح مقدمة أبي الليث السمرقندي، لمصلح الدين مصطفى بن زكريا، ت ٨٠٩هـ، (خ).
٣٠- جامع شمس الأئمة؟ لعل المراد: السرخسي.
٣١- الجامع الخاني؟ لعله شرح الجامع الصغير لقاضي خان.
٣٢- الجامع الكبير، للإسبيجابي قطب الدين أبي الحسن علي بن محمد، ت ٥٣٥هـ، (خ).
٣٣- جامع الكرخي، (الجامع الكبير في فروع الحنفية)، لأبي الحسن عبيد الله بن حسين الكرخي، ت ٣٤٠هـ، (خ).
٣٤- جامع الفصولين، لابن قاضي سماونة محمود بن إسرائيل، ت ٨٢٣هـ، (ط).
٣٥- الجامع الحسامي، للحسام الشهيد عمر بن عبد العزيز بن مازه، برهان الأئمة المعروف بالحسام الشهيد، له الفتاوى الصغرى والكبرى، وله الجامع الصغير المطول، ولعله هو المراد، والله أعلم، ت ٥٣٦ هـ، (خ)، ينظر تاج التراجم ص ٢١٧.
٣٦- الجامع الصغير، لمحمد بن الحسن الشيباني، ت ١٨٩هـ، (ط).
٣٧- الجوامع، لأبي يوسف القاضي يعقوب بن إبراهيم، ألفه ليحيى بن خالد يحتوي على أربعين كتاباً، ذكر فيه اختلاف الناس، والرأي المأخوذ به، ت ١٨٢هـ، (خ).
٣٨- جوامع الفقه = فتاوى العتابي.
٣٩- الجواهر، للحنفية أكثر من كتاب في الفقه يبتدىء عنوانه بـ: الجواهر، منها: جواهر الفتاوى للكرماني، ومنها: جواهر الفقه للمرغيناني نجل صاحب الهداية، وجواهر الفقه في العبادات، لطاهر بن قاسم الخوارزمي، وذكر صاحب الفهرس الشامل ٢٤٠/٣ شرحاً لمختصر القدوري اسمه الجواهر لمجهول، فلعله هو المراد، والله أعلم.
٤٠ - الجوهرة النيرة شرح مختصر القدوري، للحدادي أبي بكر ابن علي، ت ٨٠٠هـ، (ط).
٤١ - حاشية ابن عابدين = رد المحتار.
٤٢ - حاشية أخي زاده عبد الحليم بن محمد، الشهير بأخي زاده، ت ١٠١٣ هـ، له عدة حواش، منها حاشية على الأشباه والنظائر لابن نجيم، وحاشية على جامع الفصولين، وعلى الدرر والغرر لمنلا خسرو، وحاشية على صدر الشريعة. ينظر هدية العارفين ٥٠٤/١، ولعله أراد الأخيرة.
٤٣ - حاشية الحموي؟ لعله أحمد بن محمد مكي الحموي، ت ١٠٩٨ هـ له حاشية على الدرر والغرر لمنلا خسرو، وله غمز عيون البصائر على محاسن الأشباه والنظائر لابن نجيم، ونثر الدر الثمين على شرح ملا مسكين وإتحاف أرباب الدراية بفتح الهداية، ينظر الأعلام للزركلي ٢٣٩/١، وهدية العارفين ١٦٤/٥، ولم يظهر لي أي كتبه أراد.
٤٤ - حاشية الرحمتي، مصطفى بن محمد بن رحمة الله الأنصاري الدمشقي ثم المدني، الشهير بالأيوبي، وبالرحمتي، له حاشية على الدر المختار وهي المرادة والله أعلم، وله حاشية على المنح، ت ١٢٠٥هـ، ينظر هدية العارفين ٤٥٤/٢، (خ).
Chapter 4: Brief definition of the books mentioned in al-Lubab
29- al-Tawdeeh: commentary on Muqaddimah of Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi, by Muslih al-Din Mustafa ibn Zakariyya, d. 809 AH, (MS).
30- Jami' Shams al-A'imma? Possibly meaning: al-Sarakhsi.
31- al-Jami' al-Khani? Perhaps it is the commentary on al-Jami' al-Saghir by Qadikhan.
32- al-Jami' al-Kabir, by al-Isbijaabi Qutb al-Din Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Muhammad, d. 535 AH, (MS).
33- Jami' al-Karkhi, (al-Jami' al-Kabir fi furu' al-Hanafiyya), by Abu al-Hasan Ubaydullah ibn Husayn al-Karkhi, d. 340 AH, (MS).
34- Jami' al-Fusulayn, by Ibn Qadi Samawiya Mahmud ibn Isra'il, d. 823 AH, (printed).
35- al-Jami' al-Husami, by al-Husam al-Shahid Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz ibn Maza, Burhan al-A'imma known as al-Husam al-Shahid, he has al-Fatawa al-Sughra and al-Kubra, and he has al-Jami' al-Saghir al-Mutawwal, perhaps this is intended, and Allah knows best, d. 536 AH, (MS), see Taj al-Tarajim p. 217.
36- al-Jami' al-Saghir, by Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani, d. 189 AH, (printed).
37- al-Jawami', by Abu Yusuf al-Qadi Ya'qub ibn Ibrahim, he authored it for Yahya ibn Khalid; it contains forty books; he mentioned therein the differences of people and the adopted opinion, d. 182 AH, (MS).
38- Jawami' al-Fiqh = Fatawa al-Atabi.
39- al-Jawahir, for the Hanafis more than one book in fiqh whose title begins with: al-Jawahir, among them: Jawahir al-Fatawa by al-Karmani, and among them: Jawahir al-Fiqh by al-Marghinani, the son of the author of al-Hidayah, and Jawahir al-Fiqh fi al-Ibadat by Tahir ibn Qasim al-Khwarizmi, and the author of al-Fihris al-Shamil (3/240) mentioned a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri named al-Jawahir by an unknown author, perhaps it is the intended one, and Allah knows best.
40- al-Jawhara al-Nayyira: commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, by al-Hadadi Abu Bakr ibn Ali, d. 800 AH, (printed).
41- Hashiyat Ibn Abidin = Radd al-Muhtar.
42- Hashiyat Akhi Zada Abd al-Halim ibn Muhammad, famous as Akhi Zada, d. 1013 AH, he has several glosses, among them: a gloss on al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir by Ibn Nujaym, and a gloss on Jami' al-Fusulayn, and on al-Durar wa al-Ghurar by Mulla Khusraw, and a gloss on Sadr al-Shari'a. See Hadiyat al-Arifin 1/504, and perhaps he intended the last.
43- Hashiyat al-Hamawi? Possibly Ahmad ibn Muhammad Makki al-Hamawi, d. 1098 AH, he has a gloss on al-Durar wa al-Ghurar by Mulla Khusraw, and he has Ghammz Uyun al-Basa'ir on Mahasin al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir by Ibn Nujaym, and Nathr al-Durr al-Thamin on Sharh Mulla Miskin, and It'haf Arbab al-Diraya bi-Fath al-Hidaya, see al-A'lam by al-Zirikli 1/239 and Hadiyat al-Arifin 5/164, and it did not become clear to me which of his books he intended.
44- Hashiyat al-Rahmati, Mustafa ibn Muhammad ibn Rahmat Allah al-Ansari al-Dimashqi then al-Madani, famous as al-Ayyubi and as al-Rahmati, he has a gloss on al-Durr al-Mukhtar and it is intended, Allah knows best, and he has a gloss on al-Minah, d. 1205 AH, see Hadiyat al-Arifin 2/454, (MS).
Source pages p. 264

Commentary
This passage is a bibliographic chapter from al-Lubab, listing and briefly describing the books that are referenced in the main text. It serves as a reference guide for students and scholars to identify the sources. The list includes works from prominent Hanafi scholars such as al-Sarakhsi, al-Shaybani, Abu Yusuf, and later commentators. Each entry provides the title, author, death date (or approximate), and sometimes a note on whether the work exists in manuscript (خ) or print (ط). Some entries have editorial clarifications in parentheses, indicating uncertainties in identification. This chapter helps contextualize the authorities behind the rulings in al-Lubab.

Key Terms
الجامع الصغير (al-Jāmi‘ al-Ṣaghīr): A foundational Hanafi legal work by Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani (d. 189 AH), one of the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah.
الجوهرة النيرة (al-Jawhara al-Nayyira): A commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri by al-Hadadi (d. 800 AH), a widely used Hanafi fiqh primer.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
The Hanafi Scholarly Chain: Matn, Sharh, and Hashiyah
Bibliographical list from al-Lubab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key types of Hanafi scholarly works (matn, sharh, hashiyah) and explain how a bibliography like this one reflects the chain of transmission in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Hanafi fiqh lives in a chain of commentaries: every hashiyah is a link connecting the student to the original matn.

This passage is not a legal ruling but a scholarly apparatus. The author of al-Lubab lists the books he references, showing the reader the web of commentaries that support his commentary. Understanding this apparatus is essential for navigating any Hanafi fiqh text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of entry
For each entry, determine if the work is a matn (original), sharh (commentary), hashiyah (gloss), or fatwa collection. Note the author and title.
For example, al-Jawharah al-Nayrah is a sharh on Mukhtasar al-Quduri.
2
Locate the author and his period
Note the death date (if given). This helps place the work in the historical development of the Hanafi school.
Works from earlier centuries (e.g., 5th-7th AH) are often more foundational than later glosses.
3
Recognize cross-references
The author often cites other bibliographic sources (e.g., Hadiyyat al-Arifin) to confirm or question identifications. This reflects the collaborative nature of scholarship.
For entry 42, the author expresses uncertainty, showing scholarly caution.
4
Assess the authority level
Classify the work by its place in the Hanafi textual hierarchy: zahir al-riwayah, nawadir, or later fatwa collections.
Al-Hawashi al-Sa'diyyah is a hashiyah on al-Inayah, which is a sharh on al-Hidayah.
5
Synthesize the picture
See how these works form a chain from the original matn (e.g., Mukhtasar al-Quduri) through multiple layers of commentary.
This chain illustrates the living tradition of Hanafi fiqh.

نجل صاحب الهداية، وجواهر الفقه في العبادات، لطاهر بن قاسم الخوارزمي، وذكر صاحب الفهرس الشامل ٢٤٠/٣ شرحاً لمختصر القدوري اسمه الجواهر لمجهول، فلعله هو المراد، والله أعلم. ٤٠ - الجوهرة النيرة شرح مختصر القدوري، للحدادي أبي بكر ابن علي، ت ٨٠٠هـ، (ط). حاشية ابن عابدين = رد المحتار. ٤١ - حاشية الشيخ صالح؟ لعله الغزي نجل صاحب التنوير. ٤٥ - حاشية على رسالة الإسطرلاب للشيخ خليل الكاملي، لعله غالباً : خليل بن عبد السلام الكاملي الدمشقي، ت ١٢٠٧هـ، وله ثبت، ذكره الكتاني في فهرس الفهارس ٩٣٣/٢، له ترجمة مختصرة في حلية البشر ٥٩١/١، (خ). ٤٦ - Perhaps al-Ghazzi, the son of the author of al-Tanwir. 45 - Hashiyah on Risalah al-Isturlab by al-Shaykh Khalil al-Kamili, probably: Khalil ibn Abd al-Salam al-Kamili al-Dimashqi, d. 1207 AH, and he has a register, al-Kattani mentioned it in Fihris al-Faharis 2/933, he has a brief biography in Hilyat al-Bashar 1/591 (manuscript). 46 - al-Haqa'iq (Haqa'iq al-Manzumah), a commentary on Manzumah al-Nasafi, by Mahmud ibn Muhammad ibn Dawud Abu al-Mahamid al-Afshanji al-Lu'lu'i al-Bukhari, died as a martyr in the Mongol invasion of Bukhara, in 671 AH (manuscript). 47 - Halbat al-Mujalli wa-Bughyat al-Muhtadi fi Sharh Munyat al-Musalli, by Ibn Amir Hajj Muhammad ibn Muhammad, d. 879 AH (manuscript), and Munyat al-Musalli is by al-Kashghari Sadid al-Din Muhammad ibn Muhammad, d. 705 AH. 48 - al-Hawashi al-Sa'diyyah (a gloss on al-Inayah Sharh al-Hidayah by al-Babarti), Sa'd Allah ibn Isa ibn Amir Khan al-Qastamuni, then al-Rumi famous as Sa'di Jilbi d. 945 AH, printed with al-Fath al-Qadir with al-Inayah. al-Khaniyyah = Fatawa Qadi Khan. 49 - Khizanat al-Akmal fi al-Furu', by Abu Ya'qub Yusuf ibn Ali al-Jurjani, it is said his death was after 522 AH, as it is said he began composing it in this year, and it is said before this, as it is mentioned that he was a student of al-Karkhi, and al-Karkhi died in 340 AH, see Taj al-Tarajim p. 318, Kashf.

Commentary
This passage is a bibliographical listing from the introduction or appendix of al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri. The author provides brief definitions and identifications of the books he references throughout his commentary. This section is not a legal ruling but a scholarly apparatus that helps the reader identify the sources used. The list includes well-known Hanafi works such as al-Jawharah al-Nayrah, various glosses (hawashi) on key texts like al-Durr al-Mukhtar, and commentaries on al-Hidayah. The author often clarifies uncertainties (e.g., 'perhaps he intended the last') and provides cross-references to biographical dictionaries like Hadiyyat al-Arifin. For example, entry 42 discusses a gloss by al-Hamawi, noting multiple possible works, indicating the author's careful scholarship. This section demonstrates the depth of the Hanafi tradition and the reliance on a chain of commentaries and super-commentaries.

Key Terms
اللباب (al-Lubab): The title of the book being commented upon, a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri by al-Maydani.
الحواشي (al-hawashi): Glosses or super-commentaries written in the margins of a primary text.
الهداية (al-Hidayah): A foundational Hanafi fiqh text by Burhan al-Din al-Marghinani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A Hanafi text's authority is determined not only by its author but by its place in the chain: matn, sharh, hashiyah, each building on the previous.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Understanding the Bibliography of al-Lubab
Bibliographic list of Hanafi fiqh sources

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the major categories of Hanafi fiqh works cited in al-Lubab and state the author and genre of each listed title.

Core Idea
A scholar's library is a map of his methodology: al-Lubab's bibliography reveals the Hanafi tradition's backbone.

The fourth chapter of al-Lubab's introduction provides a concise inventory of the books referenced in the commentary. This is not a mere list—it is a window into the Hanafi scholarly ecosystem, showing the hierarchy of primary texts, commentaries, glosses, and fatwa collections that shaped later fiqh. Understanding this bibliography will help you navigate the broader Hanafi tradition and recognize the sources behind any ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Structure
Scan the list and note that entries are numbered sequentially. Each entry typically gives the book title (often with alternate names), the full name of the author, his death date (if known), and sometimes a note on whether it is printed (ط) or extant in manuscript (خ).
The compiler uses parenthetical numbers or bullet points; here they are separated by line breaks.
2
Categorize Each Work
Determine the genre of each listed work. Is it a primary matn (like al-Quduri), a commentary (sharh), a gloss (hashiyah), a fatwa collection (fatawa), or a specialized work (e.g., on inheritance)? For example, 'al-Hawashi al-Sa'diyya' is a gloss, while 'al-Khaniyyah' is a fatwa collection.
Use the titles and descriptions to classify.
3
Note the Author's Approach
Observe that the compiler clarifies ambiguities—for instance, he explicitly distinguishes 'al-Khulasah' from 'Khulasat al-Dala'il'. This shows scholarly care in attribution and avoiding confusion between similar titles.
This is a key skill for anyone working with classical texts.
4
Map the Chain of Transmission
For each work, note the author's death date and any mention of teachers or students (e.g., al-Jurjani was a student of al-Karkhi). This helps you situate the work in the historical timeline of the Hanafi school.
The dates are Hijri; convert mentally to Common Era if helpful.

الفصل الرابع : تعريف موجز بالكتب المذكورة في اللباب

حاشية سعدي جلبي على العناية شرح الهداية = الحواشي
٤٤ - حاشية الشيخ صالح؟ لعله الغزي نجل صاحب التنوير. ٤٥ - حاشية على رسالة الإسطرلاب للشيخ خليل الكاملي، لعلـه غالباً : خليل بن عبد السلام الكاملي الدمشقي، ت ١٢٠٧هـ، وله ثبت، ذكره الكتاني في فهرس الفهارس ٩٣٣/٢، له ترجمة مختصرة في حلية البشر ٥٩١/١، (خ).
٤٦ - الحقائق (حقائق المنظومة)، شرح على منظومة النسفي، لمحمود بن محمد بن داود أبي المحامد الأفشنجي اللؤلؤي البخاري، توفي شهيداً في وقعة التتار ببخارى، سنة ٦٧١هـ، (خ). ٤٧ - حَلْبَة حَلْبَةُ المُجَلّي وبغية المهتدي في شرح منية المصلي)، لابن أمير حاج محمد بن محمد، ت ٨٧٩هـ، (خ)، ومنيـة المصلي هي للكاشغري سديد الدين محمد بن محمد، ت ٧٠٥
٤٨ - الحواشي السعدية (حاشية على العناية شرح الهداية للبابرتي)، السعد الله بن عيسى بن أمير خان القسطموني، ثم الرومي الشهير بسعدي جلبي ت ٩٤٥هـ ، مطبوع بحاشية الفتح القدير مع العناية.
الخانية = فتاوى قاضي خان.
٤٩ - خزانة الأكمل في الفروع ، لأبي يعقوب يوسف بن علي الجرجاني، قيل : إن وفاته بعد سنة ٥٢٢هـ، حيث قيل إنه بدأ بتأليفه في هذه السنة، وقيل قبل هذا، حيث ذكر أنه من تلاميذ الكرخي ، والكرخي توفي سنة ٣٤٠هـ ، ينظر تاج التراجم ص ۳۱۸، كشف
الظنون ۷۰۲/۱، (خ).
٥٠ - خزانة المفتين في الفروع حسين بن محمد السميقاتي (السمنقاني) الحنفي، صاحب الشافي شرح الوافي (للنسفي)، فرغ منه سنة ٧٤٠هـ، كشف الظنون ٧٠٣/١.

١٠٦٩هـ، (ط).
الذخيرة (الذخيرة البرهانية لبرهان الإسلام السرخسي محمد بن محمد، رضي الدين صاحب المحيط البرهاني، ت ٥٤٤هـ، ينظر الفوائد البهية ص۱۸۸ ، فقد اختلف في اسم صاحب الذخيرة وسنة وفاته وكذلك تاج التراجم ص ٢٤٨.

Hashiyah of Sa'di Chalabi on Al-Inayah Sharh al-Hidayah = al-Hawashi
44 - Hashiyah of Shaykh Salih? Probably al-Ghazzi, son of the author of al-Tanwir. 45 - Hashiyah on the treatise on the astrolabe by Shaykh Khalil al-Kamili, probably: Khalil ibn Abd al-Salam al-Kamili al-Dimashqi, died 1207 AH, he has a thabat, mentioned by al-Kattani in Fihris al-Faharis 2/933, a brief biography in Hilyat al-Bashar 1/591, (Ms).
46 - al-Haqa'iq (Haqa'iq al-Manzumah), commentary on the Manzumah of al-Nasafi, by Mahmud ibn Muhammad ibn Dawud Abu al-Mahamid al-Afshinji al-Lu'lu'i al-Bukhari, martyred in the Mongol attack on Bukhara, 671 AH, (Ms). 47 - Halbat al-Mujalli wa-Bughyat al-Muhtadi fi Sharh Munyat al-Musalli, by Ibn Amir Hajj Muhammad ibn Muhammad, died 879 AH, (Ms), and Munyat al-Musalli is by al-Kashghari Sadid al-Din Muhammad ibn Muhammad, died 705 AH.
48 - al-Hawashi al-Sa'diyyah (Hashiyah on al-Inayah Sharh al-Hidayah by al-Babarti), by Sa'd Allah ibn Isa ibn Amir Khan al-Qastamuni, then al-Rumi, known as Sa'di Chalabi, died 945 AH, printed as a marginalia on al-Fath al-Qadir with al-Inayah.
al-Khaniyyah = Fatawa Qadi Khan.
49 - Khizanat al-Akmal fi al-Furu', by Abu Ya'qub Yusuf ibn Ali al-Jurjani, it is said his death was after 522 AH, as he began writing this work in that year, and some say earlier, as he is mentioned as a student of al-Karkhi, and al-Karkhi died 340 AH, see Taj al-Tarajim p. 318, Kashf al-Zunun 1/702, (Ms).
50 - Khizanat al-Muftin fi al-Furu', by Husayn ibn Muhammad al-Samiqati (al-Samnaqani) al-Hanafi, author of al-Shafi Sharh al-Wafi (by al-Nasafi), completed 740 AH, Kashf al-Zunun 1/703.
51 - al-Khulasah (Khulasat al-Fatawa, by Iftikhar al-Din al-Bukhari Tahir ibn Ahmad, died 542 AH (printed). It is not meant to be Khulasat al-Dala'il Sharh al-Quduri, by al-Razi Ali ibn Ahmad al-Makki died 598 AH, as I compared the texts transmitted from al-Khulasah and did not find them in Khulasat al-Dala'il. 52 - (Dir) al-Durr al-Mukhtar (Sharh Tanwir al-Absar by al-Timirtashi), by al-Ala'i al-Haskafi Muhammad ibn Ali, died 1088 AH, printed separately, and with the Hashiyah of Radd al-Muhtar by Ibn Abidin. 53 - Durar al-Bihar, by al-Qunawi Muhammad ibn Yusuf al-Rumi, resident of Damascus, died 788 AH, (Ms).
54 - Durar (Durar al-Hukkam fi Sharh Ghurar al-Ahkam), both by Mulla Khusraw Muhammad ibn Faramuz, died 885 AH, printed with the Hashiyah: Ghunyat Dhawi al-Ahkam fi Bughyat Durar al-Hukkam by al-Sharnablali Hasan ibn Ammar, died 1069 AH, (printed).
al-Dhakhirah (al-Dhakhirah al-Burhaniyyah li-Burhan al-Islam al-Sarakhsi Muhammad ibn Muhammad, Radi al-Din, author of al-Muhit al-Burhani, died 544 AH, see al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyyah p. 188, there is disagreement about the name of the author of al-Dhakhirah and his death year, and Taj al-Tarajim p. 248.
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage is the fourth chapter of the introduction to al-Lubab, providing a brief description of the books cited in the work. It is essentially a bibliography of Hanafi fiqh sources. Each entry typically includes the book title, author, death date (where known), and sometimes a note on whether it is printed (ط) or only extant in manuscript (خ). The compiler clarifies common confusions, such as distinguishing al-Khulasah from Khulasat al-Dala'il. The list spans various genres: commentaries (shuruh), glosses (hawashi), fatwa collections (fatawa), and specialized works on inheritance, etc. This chapter serves as a reference key for students and scholars to identify the primary sources used in the main commentary of al-Lubab.

Key Terms
حاشية (ḥāshiyah): A super-commentary or gloss, typically marginal notes explaining or commenting on a primary work.
فتاوى (fatāwā): Collection of legal responsa (fatwas) by a Hanafi jurist.
شرح (sharḥ): A commentary that explains and expands upon a base text (matn).
خ (kh): Abbreviation for 'makhṭūṭ' meaning manuscript (handwritten copy).
ط (ṭ): Abbreviation for 'maṭbū' meaning printed (published).

The bibliography in al-Lubab is a practical guide to the key Hanafi sources, teaching you to identify genres, authors, and textual chains.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Major Hanafi Fiqh References in al-Lubab
Listing and briefly describing major Hanafi fiqh works cited in al-Lubab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify major Hanafi fiqh works as matn, sharh, fatwa collection, or super-commentary (hashiyah), and identify their authors and eras.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school relies on a hierarchy of texts: matn, sharh, and super-commentary (hashiyah).

This lesson introduces key Hanafi fiqh references cited in al-Lubab. Understanding these sources is essential for navigating Hanafi jurisprudence. Each work has a specific function: some are foundational matns (e.g., Mukhtasar al-Quduri), others are commentaries (e.g., al-Lubab itself), and some are fatwa collections or super-commentaries (e.g., Radd al-Muhtar). These texts form the backbone of Hanafi legal study and fatwa practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of each referenced work
Scan the list and note whether each entry is a matn (original text), a sharh (commentary), a super-commentary (hashiyah), a fatwa collection, or a work on a specific topic like inheritance (fara'id). For example, 'Mukhtasar al-Quduri' is a matn, 'al-Lubab' is a sharh on it, and 'Radd al-Muhtar' is a super-commentary on 'al-Durr al-Mukhtar'.
The list also includes hadith collections (Sunan al-Tirmidhi, Sunan al-Nasa'i) used as sources of proof.
2
Note the author and death date
For each work, record the author's name and death date (where given). This helps gauge the historical layer of the school: early (e.g., Imam Muhammad, d. 189 H), middle (e.g., al-Sarakhsi, d. 544 H), and later (e.g., Ibn 'Abidin, d. 1252 H).
Death dates are often approximate; the author indicates when there is disagreement.
3
Recognize the role of each work in the school
Assess whether the work is a primary source (zahir al-riwaya), a relied-upon fatwa reference (like Radd al-Muhtar), or a specialized text (like al-Sirajiyyah for inheritance). This hierarchy determines which text is given precedence in deriving rulings.
Later super-commentaries often synthesize earlier works and become the standard for fatwa.
4
Identify any disputes noted
The author sometimes points out disagreements, e.g., the correct name of the author of al-Dhakhirah or the death date of al-Sajawandi. These notes show that even the identification of sources can involve scholarly debate.
Such disputes are minor and do not affect the legal rulings themselves.

Commentary
This passage is a bibliography (front matter) from the book 'al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri', where the author lists and briefly identifies the major Hanafi fiqh references that he cites in his commentary. Each entry provides the full title of the work, its author, death date, and often indicates whether it is in print (ط) or exists only in manuscript (خ). The author also mentions occasional confusions, such as distinguishing between 'Khulasat al-Fatawa' and 'Khulasat al-Dala'il'. This list is valuable for students to recognize the authoritative sources of the Hanafi school, including primary texts (e.g., al-Siyar al-Kabir), commentaries (e.g., al-Durr al-Mukhtar), fatwa collections (e.g., Khizanat al-Muftin), and specialized works on inheritance (al-Sirajiyyah). The inclusion of hadith collections like Sunan al-Tirmidhi and Sunan al-Nasa'i shows that Hanafi fiqh relies on sound prophetic traditions. This list is typical of classical Hanafi works, which often cite their sources meticulously.

Key Terms
الذخيرة البرهانية (al-Dhakhirah al-Burhaniyyah): A Hanafi fiqh work by Burhan al-Islam al-Sarakhsi, considered a major reference in the school.
رد المحتار (Radd al-Muhtar): A super-commentary (hashiyah) by Ibn Abidin on al-Durr al-Mukhtar, widely used as a standard reference for fatwa in the later Hanafi school.
السراجية في الفرائض (al-Sirajiyyah fi al-Fara'id): A classic Hanafi work on inheritance law (fara'id) by Siraj al-Din al-Sajawandi, widely used as a textbook.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's literature is layered: matn, sharh, and hashia; knowing the type of a work helps assess its authority.
